# Doe status archive: 2026-04-16 to 2026-04-18

Slice of the former monolithic `2026-04.md` archive covering 2026-04-16
through 2026-04-18 entries. Original ordering preserved.

## Push: 2D layout probe + stream-execution-plan emitter (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Landed:**

- **2D layout probe** (`bench/tools/probe_cslc_2d_grid.py`): tests cslc across `WxH` grids. Added `bench/out/cslc-grid-probe/elementwise-double-2d/` â€” a 2D variant of the minimal elementwise kernel. Ran 4x2 (8 PE, 6.7s PASS) â†’ 149x117 (17,433 PE, 414.6s PASS, E2B grid). 246x236 (31B grid, 58,056 PE) probe is still running at this commit â€” follow-up will record its result.
- **Stream-execution-plan emitter** (`bench/tools/validate_stream_graph.py`): reads a `doe_stream_graph` artifact, runs the schema-declared validations (layerRange non-empty, prefetch lookahead in [1,4], kv policy present, optional real-hash check), and emits a concrete per-layer firing sequence as a `doe_stream_execution_plan` artifact. Schema at `config/doe-stream-execution-plan.schema.json`.
- Both E2B and 31B lanes now emit a stream-execution-plan as the final step. E2B: 35 layers, 2,191 bytes/PE/layer steady-state. 31B: 61 layers, 7,249 bytes/PE/layer steady-state.
- This plan artifact is the shovel-ready hand-off to the future SdkLayout streaming executor (priority #6). `executorStatus: plan_only` until the actual runtime implementation lands.

**Why a 2D probe at all:** last turn's 1D probe surfaced that 31B (58,056 PE flattened) overflows the SDK memcpy module's internal i16 `.width` parameter. 2D layouts keep each axis under i16 max (246x236 â†’ each dim <= 32,767). 4x2 and 149x117 both pass with the new 2D layout + `u16` grid params, validating the preferred unblock path from the earlier aggregate. 246x236 pending.

**Gates green (6/6):** `schema_gate` (with stream-execution-plan schema), `csl_runtime_fixture_gate --require-ready-receipts` (12 fixtures), `wgsl_backend_matrix_gate --min-csl-runtime-ready 12 --sdk-optional`, `model_runtime_receipt_gate --require-structural-full-coverage` for E2B and 31B, `verify_cmaddr_propagation`.

## Push: cslc grid-limit probe â€” E2B full-grid compile proven (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Landed:** user-review item #3 â€” "prove full-grid compile" â€” exercised. `bench/tools/probe_cslc_grid_limits.py` runs cslc on the elementwise-double kernel across 1D grid widths from 4 to 58,056 PEs (31B scale). Produces `bench/out/cslc-grid-probe/grid-probe-aggregate.json`.

**Results:**

| width (peCount) | status | elapsed |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 4 | succeeded | 6.1 s |
| 16 | succeeded | 6.3 s |
| 64 | succeeded | 7.6 s |
| 256 | succeeded | 12.2 s |
| 1,024 | succeeded | 31.7 s |
| 4,096 | succeeded | 107.3 s |
| **17,433 (gemma-4-e2b)** | **succeeded** | **439.7 s** |
| 58,056 (gemma-4-31b) | blocked | 5.6 s |

**E2B compile is real.** The 149Ã—117 grid compiles cleanly in 7.3 minutes wall time for the simplest kernel. cslc linear-log scaling holds well across four orders of magnitude.

**31B blocker, isolated:** the Cerebras SDK's `<memcpy/get_params>` module declares `.width` as i16 internally. 58,056 overflows i16 (max 32,767). The error originates in the SDK module, not in Doe's emitter â€” fixing Doe's own `param width: i16` to `u16` (in-tree change applied to elementwise-double) is necessary but not sufficient. Three unblock paths documented in the aggregate; **preferred path: emit 2D layouts** (`@set_rectangle(width, height)` where each axis stays under i16 max). 31B's 246Ã—236 fits per-axis without needing SDK changes or PE partitioning.

**Model receipt now carries the probe evidence:** `fullGridCompileProbeEvidence.maxProvenPeCount1D = 17433` and `thirtyOneBRequires2DEmitter = true` are surfaced in every regenerated E2B and 31B receipt.

**Gates green (6/6):** `schema_gate`, `csl_runtime_fixture_gate --require-ready-receipts` (12), `wgsl_backend_matrix_gate --min-csl-runtime-ready 12 --sdk-optional` (SDK detected), `model_runtime_receipt_gate --require-structural-full-coverage` for E2B and 31B, `verify_cmaddr_propagation`.

## Push: Receipt taxonomy + reduceStrategy cleanup (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Landed:** taxonomy cleanup so the model-level receipt stops reading as "model executed" when it's only structural coverage, and the partial/fabric reduce tradeoff is now explicit per kernel.

**Receipt taxonomy (user-requested):**

- `laneStatus` renamed to `structural_full_coverage` / `structural_partial_coverage_kernel_gap` / `structural_memory_plan_does_not_fit` (legacy values kept so older receipts parse).
- New `executionStatus` enum: `not_attempted` / `simulator_success` / `simulator_failure` / `hardware_success` / `hardware_failure` / `compile_failure`.
- New `executionBlocker` enum with priority: `partial_kernel_coverage` â†’ `memory_plan_does_not_fit` â†’ `sdk_layout_streaming_executor_missing` â†’ `full_grid_compile_unattempted` â†’ `hardware_endpoint_unavailable` â†’ `none`.
- Receipt builder sets `executionStatus=not_attempted` + the first unmet blocker.
- Gate gains `--require-structural-full-coverage` + `--require-execution` flags.
- Both E2B and 31B receipts now honestly read: `laneStatus=structural_full_coverage`, `executionStatus=not_attempted`, `executionBlocker=sdk_layout_streaming_executor_missing`.

**reduceStrategy field:**

- New `reduceStrategy` enum on every fixture in `config/csl-runtime-fixtures.schema.json`: `none`, legacy `on_device_fabric`, `on_device_fabric_validated`, `on_device_fabric_quarantined`, legacy `host_partial`, and canonical `host_reduce_partial`.
- Populated for all 12 fixtures:
  - `on_device_fabric`: `tiled-matmul` (c2d_params broadcast chain on WSE).
  - `host_reduce_partial`: `fused-gemv-dequant`, `sample` (fabric allreduce deferred or intentionally host-combined; partials exported to host with `reduceStrategyNote` carried into model receipts).
  - `none`: remaining 9 kernels (per-PE-only or workgroup-internal reductions).
- Field threaded through `build_model_runtime_receipt.py` so every host-plan kernel in the E2B / 31B receipts carries `reduceStrategy` and optional `reduceStrategyNote`. Downstream tooling (and the future streaming executor) can now tell apart a kernel that needs a host-side reduction step from one whose per-PE output is already the final value.

**Gates green** (6/6): `schema_gate`, `csl_runtime_fixture_gate --require-ready-receipts` (12 fixtures), `wgsl_backend_matrix_gate --min-csl-runtime-ready 12 --sdk-optional` (SDK detected), `model_runtime_receipt_gate --require-structural-full-coverage` for E2B and 31B, `verify_cmaddr_propagation`.

**Remaining work** (unchanged in shape): SdkLayout streaming executor (the actual runtime implementation), full-grid cslc compile receipts for 149Ã—117 / 246Ã—236 layouts, and model-level parity â€” logit-checkpoint comparison through the graph, not just per-kernel parity against numpy.

## Push: Stream-graph emitter + cmaddr propagation smoke (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Landed:** the stream-graph and hardware-endpoint plumbing pieces that sit between the memory plan and the not-yet-built SdkLayout streaming runtime.

- `bench/tools/build_stream_graph.py` â€” derives a `doe_stream_graph` artifact from the memory plan + model config. Replaces the hardcoded 31B sample with a real emitter that reads `streamStages` and maps stage kind â†’ (source, muxPattern) via a small table: `embedding_rows â†’ host_embeddings / broadcast`, `layer_weights â†’ host_weights / row_broadcast`, `ple_rows / ple_projection â†’ host_ple_table / column_broadcast`, `kv_stream â†’ kv_overflow / unicast`. Ring-buffer depth defaults to 2 (double-buffered prefetch).
- Lane drivers (`bench/runners/run_e2b_full_graph_lane.py`, `bench/runners/run_31b_full_graph_lane.py`) now emit the stream-graph as the final pipeline step alongside the model-level receipt.
- Generated: `bench/out/e2b-full-graph/gemma-4-e2b-stream-graph.json` (4 streams, 35-layer code region) and `bench/out/31b-full-graph/gemma-4-31b-stream-graph.json` (4 streams, 61-layer code region). Both validate under `schema_gate`.
- `bench/tools/verify_cmaddr_propagation.py` â€” priority #7 hardware-endpoint plumbing verifier. Unit-tests the driver's pure functions (`materialize_command` + `redact_command_for_receipt` + execution-target classification) with simfabric (empty cmaddr) and system (fake cmaddr) cases. Runs in milliseconds without invoking `cslc` or `cs_python` or needing a real endpoint. Asserts: empty cmaddr drops the `{cmaddr_arg}` slot cleanly; non-empty cmaddr embeds `--cmaddr=IP:PORT`; the recorded receipt replaces the raw endpoint with `$DOE_CSL_CMADDR`; `executionTarget` flips `simfabric` â†” `system` on cmaddr presence. Proves the hardware-endpoint path is wired end-to-end without requiring a live CS system, so the E2B-on-hardware step can land the moment an endpoint becomes available.

**Gates green:** `schema_gate`, `csl_runtime_fixture_gate --require-ready-receipts` (12 fixtures), `wgsl_backend_matrix_gate --min-csl-runtime-ready 12 --sdk-optional` (SDK detected), `model_runtime_receipt_gate --require-fits --require-full-coverage --min-kernel-coverage-pct 100` for both E2B and 31B.

**Next:** the actual SdkLayout streaming-runtime implementation remains the big follow-up â€” async DSDs for prefetch, ring-buffer management, compile-artifact cache lookup, KV spill-to-host. The stream-graph schema lets this implementation work land in stages without blocking downstream consumers.

## Push: Gemma 4 31B lane + streaming-migration receipt + stream-graph schema (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Landed:** priorities #5 (31B memory-plan migration) and #6 (SdkLayout streaming-runtime schema skeleton). Evidence that Doe's existing plan-chain scales from E2B to 31B structurally and that the runtime-path boundary between memcpy RPC and streaming runtime is explicit.

**31B lane:**

- `runtime/zig/examples/execution-v1/gemma-4-31b-smoke.json` â€” scaled from E2B (hidden=5120, heads=32, layers=61, same step graph, same vocab/PLE shape)
- `bench/runners/run_31b_full_graph_lane.py` â€” end-to-end driver
- `bench/out/31b-full-graph/` â€” host-plan, memory-plan, runtime-config, simulator-plan, runtime receipt
- Result: 246Ã—236 = **58,056 PEs, 34.2 GB total model, fits=true, 17/17 kernel coverage, full_coverage lane status**
- Compile-artifact reuse factor: 61 â€” all transformer layers share one compile shape

**Streaming migration derivation** (both E2B and 31B receipts now carry):

- `perPeSramBudget`, `headroomBytesPerPe` (E2B: 8 bytes, 31B: 4 bytes â€” razor-thin by current planner)
- `maxPerLayerStage` vs `maxSetupStage` â€” distinguishes per-layer streaming workload (repeatCount > 1, double-buffered) from one-shot init stages
- `doubleBufferedWorkingSetPerPe` + `doubleBufferedFits` (both models: fits=true for per-layer double-buffering)
- `compileArtifactReuseFactor` (E2B: 35Ã—, 31B: 61Ã—) â€” direct measure of the per-layer compile cache savings
- `runtimePath` âˆˆ {`memcpy_rpc`, `sdk_layout_streaming`} with `streamingRuntimeRequired` boolean â€” both E2B and 31B flag streaming runtime required because `streamed_working_set_per_pe > per_pe_sram / 2` (embeddings dominate SRAM)

**Stream-graph schema** (`config/doe-stream-graph.schema.json`):

Captures the SdkLayout streaming-runtime config knobs before the runtime itself is implemented:

- `codeRegions` â€” per-layer ELF placement (compile-artifact sha256 + PE range + layer range). Different layers sharing compile shape reuse one region.
- `streams` â€” async prefetch streams with source (host_weights / host_embeddings / host_ple_table / kv_overflow / activation_input), destinationPort, ringBufferDepth, payloadBytes, muxPattern (broadcast / row_broadcast / column_broadcast / unicast / demux_round_robin).
- `prefetchSchedule` â€” lookaheadLayers (1-4), kickoffTrigger (layer_start / activation_ready / unblock_signal), stallPolicy (fail_closed / backpressure / drop_oldest).
- `kvPolicy` â€” residency (resident / spill_to_host / partitioned_across_pes), spillBehavior (eager / on_demand / lru), maxResidentTokens.
- `compileArtifactCache` â€” key/value SHA-256 hash lookup; per_session vs shared_across_sessions.
- `validation` â€” fail-closed routing reachability + port binding + acyclicity booleans.

Sample 31B stream-graph at `bench/out/31b-full-graph/gemma-4-31b-stream-graph.json` validates under `schema_gate`. The implementation of the actual runtime (code regions + async DSDs + ring buffer + compile-artifact cache lookup) is the next follow-up.

**Gates green:** `schema_gate` (with new stream-graph + receipt schemas), `model_runtime_receipt_gate --require-fits --require-full-coverage --min-kernel-coverage-pct 100` passes for **both E2B and 31B**.

## Push: E2B full coverage â€” sample + kv_write runtime-ready, 12/12 matrix (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Landed:** the two remaining E2B kernel-pattern gaps closed â€” gemma-4-e2b-it-text-q4k-ehf16-af32 now flips from `partial_coverage_kernel_gap` (14/17 = 82%) to **`full_coverage` (17/17 = 100%)**.

- **sample** runtime-ready: variant pe_program exports per-PE `(local_max_val, local_max_idx)`; host computes global argmax. For 4096-vocab Ã— 4 PE, selects token **1913 bit-for-bit** identical to numpy argmax. Same host-side-reduce pattern as fused_gemv_dequant â€” bypasses the async-send fabric-reduce teardown stall.
- **kv_write** runtime-ready: standalone variant with fixed-size local `k_cache`/`v_cache` buffers per PE. Writes the K/V projections at `position=7` and the runner verifies `write_err=0.0`, `stray_abs=0.0` (no spillage into neighboring slots). Surfaced + fixed a latent emitter bug: `@as(u32, @intCast(head_dim))` in `emit_csl_kv_cache.zig` â€” `@intCast` is not a CSL builtin, replaced with `@as(u32, head_dim)`.
- Schema fix: `config/csl-runtime-fixtures.schema.json` kernelPattern enum extended with `kv_write`.

**Matrix after push:** 12 rows, Vulkan SPIR-V 12/12, Metal MSL 12/12, D3D12 HLSL+DXIL 12/12, **CSL runtime 12/12**. All Gemma HostPlan kernel-pattern outcomes relevant to 270M/E2B are runtime-parity-verified on the Cerebras WSE-3 simulator.

**E2B receipt:** `bench/gates/model_runtime_receipt_gate.py --require-fits --require-full-coverage --min-kernel-coverage-pct 100` passes. 149Ã—117 grid (17,433 PEs), residencyMode=layer_streaming, fits=true.

**Next under the plan roadmap:** priority #5 31B memory-plan migration (layer_streaming residency + streamed weight shards + per-layer compile-artifact reuse cache) and #6 SdkLayout streaming runtime (code regions, ports, streams, async send/receive, demux/mux). These are schema-expansion + new-runtime-path work beyond the current resident E2B shape.

## Push: Gemma 4 E2B full-graph lane + model-level runtime receipt (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Landed:** priorities #3 and #4 from the CSL plan roadmap â€” an end-to-end E2B lane driver that converts the model config manifest into HostPlan + memory-plan + runtime-config + simulator-plan, plus a model-level runtime receipt that binds every artifact by SHA-256 and resolves each host-plan kernel to its CSL runtime-ready fixture.

**E2B evidence (gemma-4-e2b-it-text-q4k-ehf16-af32):**

- Grid: 149 Ã— 117 = **17,433 PEs**
- Residency mode: **layer_streaming** (E2B already uses streaming, not resident)
- Memory: 6.88 GB total (51.4 MB persistent + 6.84 GB streamed), 99% SRAM utilization, **fits = true**
- 17 kernels classified; 14 runtime-ready (82% coverage); 3 missing: `kv_write` (Ã—2) + `sample`
- 20 prefill launches + 23 decode launches

**New artifacts:**

- `bench/runners/run_e2b_full_graph_lane.py` â€” single-command driver for the whole pipeline
- `bench/tools/build_model_runtime_receipt.py` â€” binds manifest + host-plan + memory-plan + runtime-config + simulator-plan + fixture registry into a model-level receipt; id-first fixture lookup with pattern fallback (so gelu resolves to the gelu fixture rather than the first element_wise fixture)
- `config/doe-model-runtime-receipt.schema.json` â€” schema registered in `config/schema-targets.json`

- `bench/out/e2b-full-graph/gemma-4-e2b-runtime-receipt.{json,md}` â€” first published receipt

**Gates green:** `model_runtime_receipt_gate --require-fits --min-kernel-coverage-pct 80` passes for E2B (coverage=14/17 = 82%, fits=True). `schema_gate` passes with the new receipt in the schema-targets registry.

**Why this matters:** this is the first artifact that answers "can Doe run this model end-to-end" at the model level rather than the kernel level. It's also the structural template 31B will extend with a streaming-runtime path â€” the `residencyMode=layer_streaming` field and `streamStages` in the memory plan are already where 31B's extra metadata will live (stream buffer sizing, per-layer compile-artifact reuse cache, KV-cache residency policy).

**Next:** close the 3-kernel gap (kv_write + sample) to flip E2B's laneStatus from `partial_coverage_kernel_gap` â†’ `full_coverage`. Then 31B memory-plan migration (priority #5) and SdkLayout streaming runtime (priority #6).

## Push: CSL runtime coverage to 10 â€” fused_gemv_dequant via host-reduce variant (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Landed:** fused_gemv_dequant promoted to the 10th CSL runtime-ready fixture, completing the Gemma kernel-pattern coverage relevant to 270M/E2B.

- **Kernel:** Q4K dequant (f16 scale + 128 packed nibble-bytes per 144-byte block) fused with per-PE GEMV. Each PE dequants its weight slice and computes `partial[out_dim]` via scalar dot products; the host memcpy_d2h's per-PE partials and sums across PEs. Verified bit-close against a numpy Q4K dequant+GEMV reference on 4 PE Ã— out_dim=64 Ã— in_dim_per_pe=512: `per_pe_err=4.2e-05`, `reduce_err=4.2e-05`.
- **Fabric allreduce deferred**: the primary emitted `pe_program.csl` (`bench/out/dual-compile-evidence/fused-gemv-dequant/csl/pe_program.csl`) uses a hand-rolled async-send chain that has a known teardown-ordering stall (documented in iter-35/36 of the original runtime-run/result.json). Adopting the canonical `<collectives_2d>` or `<benchmark-libs/allreduce>` module is a multi-day rewrite. This fixture uses a `runtime/zig/examples/simulator/fused-gemv-dequant-runtime/compile/fused-gemv-dequant/pe_program.csl` variant that exports `partial` and does host-side reduction. Proves dequant + per-PE GEMV correctness today; fabric-reduce adoption is tracked separately in the governed-lane-report's `variantNotes.fabricReduce`.

**Matrix after push:** 10 rows, Vulkan SPIR-V 10/10, Metal MSL 10/10, D3D12 HLSL+DXIL 10/10, **CSL runtime 10/10**. All Gemma HostPlan kernel-pattern outcomes relevant to 270M/E2B are now runtime-parity-verified on the Cerebras WSE-3 simulator.

**Gates green:** `csl_runtime_fixture_gate --require-ready-receipts` (10 fixtures), `schema_gate`, `wgsl_backend_matrix_gate --min-csl-runtime-ready 10 --sdk-optional --require-vulkan/metal/d3d12-ready` (SDK detected, threshold enforced).

**Next under user's priority list (post-kernel coverage):** priority #3 E2B full-graph lane (WGSL kernels â†’ classifier â†’ HostPlan â†’ memory plan â†’ CSL bundles â†’ operationGraph â†’ runtime-config â†’ simulator trace), then #4 model-level runtime receipt binding model/tokenizer config hash + HostPlan hash + memory-plan hash + backend artifact hashes + numerical parity.

## Push: CSL runtime coverage to 9 â€” attention_tiled + attention_decode + matrix gate (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Landed:** two Gemma attention kernels promoted to CSL runtime-ready, and the cross-backend matrix gate wired into the blocking bundle with SDK-optional CSL.

- **attention_tiled** (prefill Flash Attention): max_abs_err=2.24e-07 on 4 PE Ã— head_dim=32 Ã— kv_len=64 Ã— q_len=32. The tiled_matmul DSD .offset fix did NOT apply here â€” attention_tiled uses scalar-indexed array loops (no @get_dsd calls), not @fmacs DSD flow. Fixture at `runtime/zig/examples/simulator/attention-tiled-runtime/`, runner at `bench/runners/csl-runners/attention_tiled_sim_runner.py` (shares `common.py`).
- **attention_decode** (single-query decode): max_abs_err=1.79e-07 on 4 PE Ã— head_dim=32 Ã— kv_len=64 Ã— q_len=1. Shares emitter body with attention_tiled; only q_len differs. Fixture at `runtime/zig/examples/simulator/attention-decode-runtime/`.
- **Matrix lock:** `bench/gates/wgsl_backend_matrix_gate.py` now supports `--sdk-optional` with a `csl_sdk_detected()` helper that checks DOE_CSL_SDK_ROOT, DOE_CSLC_EXECUTABLE, and `cslc` on PATH. When SDK is present, `--min-csl-runtime-ready N` is enforced; when absent, the threshold is informational. Wired into `bench/runners/run_blocking_gates.py` via `--with-wgsl-backend-matrix-gate` + `--wgsl-backend-matrix-min-csl-runtime-ready N`. This is user priority #1 â€” prevents regressions across the shared WGSL emitter path as more Gemma kernels land, without gating on hosts that don't have the Cerebras SDK installed.

**Matrix after push:** 9 rows, Vulkan SPIR-V 9/9, Metal MSL 9/9, D3D12 HLSL+DXIL 9/9, **CSL runtime 9/9**. All Gemma HostPlan kernel-pattern outcomes relevant to 270M/E2B are now both compile-green and runtime-parity-verified on the Cerebras WSE-3 simulator.

**Gates green:** `csl_runtime_fixture_gate --require-ready-receipts` (9 fixtures), `schema_gate`, `wgsl_backend_matrix_gate --min-csl-runtime-ready 9 --sdk-optional --require-vulkan/metal/d3d12-ready`, `csl_fixture_mirror_gate`, `csl_operation_graph_gate`.

**Next under user's priority list:** fused_gemv_dequant runtime (still has async-send stall in a different code path), then E2B full-graph lane, then model-level runtime receipt, then 31B memory-plan migration + SdkLayout streaming runtime.

## Push: CSL tiled_matmul bit-exact runtime parity + registry row (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Landed:** iteration 43 closed out the SUMMA tiled_matmul kernel to **bit-exact numerical parity** (max_abs_err=0.0) on the Cerebras SDK 1.4 simulator for 16x16 @ 16x16 on a 2x2 PE grid, and registered it as the 6th runtime-ready CSL fixture.

**Root cause (emitter-side, not host-side):** Doe's `emit_csl_matmul.zig` was positioning A_dsd per-k via `.offset = k*Mt` inside `@get_dsd(mem1d_dsd, .{ .base_address = Ap, .extent = Mt, .offset = ... })`. No canonical SDK example uses that field in the constructor; the value was silently mis-interpreted. The canonical SUMMA pattern (`csl-extras/examples/benchmarks/gemm-collectives_2d/pe.csl`) declares A_dsd outside the k-loop via `.tensor_access = |i|{Mt} -> A_tile[i]` + `@set_dsd_base_addr(A_dsd, Ap)` and advances at end of each k via `A_dsd = @increment_dsd_offset(A_dsd, Mt, f32)`. Prior diagnosis wrongly blamed host tile placement (iter-31 row-major gave max_abs_err=15.7; iter-43 canonical col-major gave 16.9 â€” larger, not smaller, confirming the bug was emitter-side).

**Contract changes:**

- `config/doe-wgsl-simulator-plan.schema.json`: added optional `compileTargets[*].compileParams` object so kernels that declare top-level layout params beyond width/height (tiled_matmul needs P:2,Mt:8,Kt:8,Nt:8) keep the governed plan as the single source of truth.
- `runtime/zig/tools/csl_sdk_driver.py`: honors `compileParams`, appending `key:value` pairs to the cslc `--params` argument.
- `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_csl_simulator.zig`: the Zig sim-runner plan parser now uses `ignore_unknown_fields = true` so the shared schema can carry driver-only metadata (sourceWgslPath, compileParams) without breaking the Zig consumer.

**New fixture artifacts:**

- `runtime/zig/examples/simulator/tiled-matmul-runtime/{host-plan.json, runtime-config.json, simulator-plan.template.json, compile/tiled-matmul/*.csl}`
- `bench/runners/csl-runners/tiled_matmul_sim_runner.py` (uses shared `common.py`)
- `bench/out/dual-compile-evidence/governed-lane-sdk-handoff/sim-success-tiled-matmul/{governed-lane-report.json, driver-result.json, trace.json, host-plan.json}`
- Added entry in `config/csl-runtime-fixtures.json` (now 7 fixtures, 6 runtime_ready).

**Matrix summary** (regenerated `bench/out/cross-backend-matrix/wgsl-backend-matrix.json`): 7 rows, Vulkan SPIR-V 7/7, Metal MSL 7/7, D3D12 HLSL+DXIL 7/7, CSL runtime **7/7** after the parallel GELU bump (tanh approximation, runtimeMaxAbsErr=9.5e-07 on 16 PE Ã— 1024 f32).

**Gates green:** `csl_runtime_fixture_gate --require-ready-receipts` (7 fixtures), `schema_gate`, `wgsl_backend_matrix_gate --min-csl-runtime-ready 6 --require-vulkan-ready --require-metal-ready --require-d3d12-ready`, `zig build test`, `zig build test-wgsl`.

**Remaining work under user's iter-42 plan #4:** attention_tiled, attention_decode, fused_gemv_dequant need the same runtime-ready bump. attention_tiled likely inherits the same emitter fix (shares the c2d/SUMMA skeleton). fused_gemv_dequant still has an async-send stall in a different code path.

## Push: WGSL backend matrix + CSL runtime fixture registry (2026-04-18 UTC)

Added a first-class registry for governed CSL runtime fixtures:
`config/csl-runtime-fixtures.json` + schema. The registry binds the
runtime-ready CSL fixtures for elementwise, gather, rope, attention-linear, and
reduction, plus the compile-ready GELU fixture, to their WGSL source, HostPlan,
runtime config, runner, governed-lane report, driver result, and trace
artifacts.

Added `bench/gates/csl_runtime_fixture_gate.py` so the registry checks the
referenced simulator plans, HostPlans, runtime commands, runner scripts, and
ready governed-lane reports. The gate supports a stricter
`--require-ready-receipts` mode for SDK-backed environments.

Added HLSL and native DXIL emitter CLIs (`doe-emit-hlsl`, `doe-emit-dxil`) next
to the existing SPIR-V and MSL tools. `bench/tools/build_wgsl_backend_matrix.py`
now builds a matrix keyed by the same WGSL source and can emit MSL/HLSL/DXIL
artifacts while reporting Vulkan SPIR-V and CSL governed-lane evidence. The
generated report schema is `config/wgsl-backend-matrix-report.schema.json`, and
`bench/gates/wgsl_backend_matrix_gate.py` validates the result with optional
per-backend readiness requirements.

The CSL runtime runners now share `bench/runners/csl-runners/common.py` for
argument parsing, endpoint handling, max-error computation, and
`explicit_simulator_trace` writing. This is the first runner-template surface
before promoting tiled matmul, attention tiled/decode, and fused GEMV dequant.

## Push: CSL simulator hard gate accepts runtime numerical traces (2026-04-18 UTC)

Promoted the first SDK simulator-success receipt into the hard-gate contract.
`config/doe-wgsl-simulator-trace.schema.json` now accepts both the original
`compile_run_smoke_summary` trace and the new `explicit_simulator_trace`
runtime numerical trace shape emitted by the elementwise-double
`cs_python`/`SdkRuntime` fixture. The runtime trace contract requires
`runtimePassed=true`, target execution mode, element counts, max absolute error,
and input/expected/actual samples.

`bench/gates/csl_simulator_gate.py` now treats `explicit_simulator_trace` as a
real runtime receipt and fails if `runtimePassed` is not true. This lets
`--require-ready` validate the new elementwise-double success receipt instead
of only validating compile-smoke traces.

**Changed (3 of 7):**

- `browser/chromium/scripts/check_module_prototypes.py`: `stable_hash(first)` was called twice â€” once inside the determinism check (`stable_hash(first) == stable_hash(second)`) and again when populating the `resultHash` row field. Hoisted the first call into `first_hash = stable_hash(first)` and reused it on both lines. Micro-efficiency, zero behavior change.
- `browser/chromium/scripts/check-browser-milestones.py`: `main`'s `if args.emit_json: ... else: ...` pair used 2-space indent on the two `print` / `emit_text(summary)` bodies while the rest of the file uses 4-space PEP 8 style. Restored to 4 spaces. Pure style, no behavior change.
- `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep_exports.cc`: the `DOE_ORT_EP_EXPORT` macro definition had three branches â€” `_WIN32` (uses `__declspec(dllexport)`), `__APPLE__` (uses `__attribute__((visibility("default")))`), and `else` (also uses `__attribute__((visibility("default")))`). The `__APPLE__` and fallback branches were byte-identical, so the `__APPLE__` arm was dead. Collapsed into a two-branch `_WIN32` / else macro. 7 lines â†’ 5, identical expansion on every platform.

**Already clean, no change (4 of 7):**

- `browser/chromium/scripts/cleanup-browser-artifacts.py`: 70-line timestamped artifact-pruner; well-factored.

Thirteenth 7-files-per-fire batch, mixed Zig data-type modules + bench reduction-order runners.

**Changed (2 of 7):**

- `bench/runners/run_reduction_order_counterexample.py`: `summarize_lane` built the `{entry["outputValueF32"] for entry in per_variant}` set inline for `uniqueOutputValueCount` and again (identical comprehension) for `counterexampleObserved: len(...) > 1`. Hoisted to a single `unique_values` local and reused for both; also hoisted `unique_digests` for `uniqueDigestCount` for consistency. No behavior change, one fewer double-pass over `per_variant` per lane summary.

Replaced the second call-site with the already-stored local. No behavior change, avoids a second scan over the case's repeat list.

**Already clean, no change (5 of 7):**

- `runtime/zig/src/doe_native_shared_types.zig`: 53-line namespace of `BackendKind`, `MAX_*` size constants, `BindingInfo`, and compile-time `NativeVulkanRuntime` alias. Clean data surface.

Verbose by policy (JSON I/O boundary). Every parse helper uses an internal `commandKindEqualsFn(raw, name)` wrapper around `std.ascii.eqlIgnoreCase` â€” the name is a misnomer (no helper is command-kind specific), but inlining or renaming would touch 50+ call sites. Also, numeric return codes (`0x00000001`, `0x00000002` â€¦) are WGPU ABI values inline rather than named constants. Both are noted as follow-up candidates.
- `runtime/zig/src/doe_native_object_types.zig`: 342-line file with 20 `Doe*` struct definitions, each getting its own `MAGIC_*` u32 tag. Every struct uses `pub const TYPE_MAGIC = MAGIC_X; magic: u32 = TYPE_MAGIC,` â€” can't be compressed without losing the runtime-cast check `cast(T, p)` uses in `doe_native_object_helpers.zig`.
- `bench/runners/run_reduction_order_logit_flip.py`: 172-line sibling of the counterexample runner. Each `flipObserved` set comprehension appears once (no double-build to hoist); `build_claim`'s `any(...)` generators are used once each. The `[logits[index] - exact_reference_logits[index] for index in range(len(logits))]` comprehension could become `zip`-based, but `zip` silently truncates on length mismatch whereas `range(len(logits))` would raise `IndexError` â€” kept the indexed form as a defensive guard.

Validation: `python3 -m py_compile bench/runners/run_reduction_order_counterexample.py bench/runners/enrich_sampled_decode_rows.py` â†’ OK. (No Zig source touched this fire, so `zig build test` was not re-run.)

## Push: 7-file review batch, `SemVer.cmp` via `std.math.order` (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Changed (1 of 7):**

Replaced each pair with `std.math.order(self.X, other.X)` â€” the stdlib's own comparison helper â€” and short-circuit return when `.eq` fails. 8 if-statements collapse to a three-step `order` / early-return / `order` chain. All 7 existing `SemVer` tests (parse variants + ordering combinations) pass unchanged.

The `as_core_command` / `as_full_command` switches could be comptime-generated via `inline for` over union fields, but the explicit listing is greppable and matches the CoreCommand/FullCommand partition definition directly.

## Push: optional CSL simulator gate and CM endpoint plumbing (2026-04-18 UTC)

Added the opt-in CSL simulator receipt gate to `run_blocking_gates.py` via
`--with-csl-simulator-gate`. The gate validates the governed CSL report and its
referenced simulator/driver/trace artifacts when present, but only requires
`laneStatus=ready` when `--csl-simulator-require-ready` is set. This keeps
hosts without the Cerebras SDK in the explicit `blocked` diagnostic path instead
of making SDK absence a default blocking failure.

`run_csl_governed_lane.py` now accepts `--csl-sdk-root` and resolves `cslc` /
`cs_python` from that SDK root unless explicit executable flags are supplied.
It also forwards `--csl-cmaddr IP_ADDRESS:PORT` through `$DOE_CSL_CMADDR` so
the SDK runtime command can target a CS system. Driver receipts record
`executionTarget` and `cmaddrProvided`, and persisted command arrays redact the
actual endpoint as `$DOE_CSL_CMADDR`; credentials remain external SDK
environment state.

The runtime-config schema now permits `mode="sdk-runtime-command"` with an
explicit command template, while preserving existing `compile-only` fixtures.
Docs in `docs/process.md`, `docs/csl-architecture.md`, and `bench/README.md`
now describe the optional simulator gate, simfabric default, and CS-system
endpoint handoff.

## Push: `command/command_parse_dispatch.zig` dispatch-dimension parse collapse (2026-04-18 UTC)

Tenth random-file review fire. `runtime/zig/src/command/command_parse_dispatch.zig::parseDispatchDimensions` had three parallel branches picking the dispatch grid source: first `raw.workgroupCount`, then `raw.workgroups`, then per-axis `raw.x` / `raw.y` / `raw.z` with `orelse 1` fallbacks. The first two branches were byte-identical three-line array copies.

Both `workgroupCount` and `workgroups` are typed `?[3]u32` on the raw payload (verified at `runtime/zig/src/command_json_raw.zig:293-294`), so the whole cascade collapses into a single `orelse` chain:

```zig
const dims: [3]u32 = raw.workgroupCount orelse raw.workgroups orelse .{
    raw.x orelse 1,
    raw.y orelse 1,
    raw.z orelse 1,
};
```

22 lines down to 9. Same precedence (workgroupCount > workgroups > x/y/z), same zero-dim rejection, same return shape. Other files scanned this fire (`command/command_kind.zig`, `doe_queue_submit_shared.zig`) were already in DRY form â€” the `matchesAny` helper dedupes the string-alias handling, and the backend switch in `flush_pending_work_dropin_sync` already uses the same shape as the `doeNativeQueueRelease` cleanup from fire 10.

Validation: `zig build test` â†’ PASS; `zig build test-wgsl` â†’ PASS.

## Push: matvec RADV ISA investigation â€” clamp removal broke MLP (2026-04-18 UTC)

Paired clamped-vs-elided SPIR-V investigation of `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_naive_swizzle0`, which regressed p50/p95/p99 by ~11.6% on the 2026-04-18T20:02:10Z AMD Vulkan release claim despite the proof-backed elided SPIR-V having ~15% fewer bytes and 18 fewer scalar ops. Full artifact bundle at `bench/out/matvec-radv-investigation/20260418T212609Z/` with `investigation.json`, `spirv-diff.md`, both SPIR-V binaries + `spirv-dis` output, RADV/ACO dumps from `RADV_DEBUG=shaders` on a Radeon 8060S (STRIX_HALO, Mesa 26.0.3, RDNA 3.5), and the loop-body NIR for each variant.

Finding: the regression is not a proof-pipeline defect. At the ACO level both variants emit **identical** ssbo-load counts (10), identical FMA counts (32), identical `s_waitcnt` counts (6), and identical max-VGPR pressure (v[23]). Scalar pressure drops by 4 registers in the elided form (s[19] â†’ s[15]), confirming the clamp was real SALU work, not a dead-code no-op.

The NIR loop-body diff reveals the actual cause. In the clamped form, the four matrix-row addresses are computed from four independent pre-staged base registers (`%20`, `%24`, `%26`, `%28`), one per row; the four matrix loads are thus independent in the dataflow and the hardware can issue them as 4-way memory-level parallel requests. In the elided form, NIR's stride-collapse pass proves the four row addresses form a strided `{base, base+0x2000, base+0x4000, base+0x6000}` series and rewrites each row's address as an `iadd` chained from the previous row's address `%29`. Matrix loads now serialize through that chain, and the ~11.6% regression is consistent with losing 4-way MLP on the critical matrix-read path.

The clamp was not dead code at the scheduler level: `umin(base + k, N)` is not commutative with `iadd` when the sum exceeds `N`, so its presence blocked stride-collapse and implicitly preserved MLP. Removing it was correct-by-semantics but traded MLP for instruction count, which on RDNA 3.5 is the wrong trade for this kernel shape. `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` and `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` both remain claimable because their matrix access patterns don't rely on independent row addresses for MLP.

Follow-up recommendation: accept the naive regression as an RDNA scheduler artifact rather than reintroduce the clamp or add a stride-collapse fence. The optimized swizzle1 / workgroupshared variants benefit from the same proof chain and claim fine; the naive variant is the uninteresting baseline. Alternative paths (WGSL-level anti-optimization barrier; upstream ACO heuristic; matrix pre-swizzle) are recorded in `investigation.json` as follow-up options but not prioritized.

## Push: `bench_synthetic_assets.zig` slice simplification (2026-04-18 UTC)

Eighth random-file review fire, small surgical change.

`runtime/zig/src/bench_synthetic_assets.zig::readAssetWords` was reading little-endian u32s from a byte buffer via `std.mem.readInt(u32, bytes[byte_index .. byte_index + @sizeOf(u32)][0..@sizeOf(u32)], .little)`. The `[byte_index .. byte_index + @sizeOf(u32)][0..@sizeOf(u32)]` double-slice expresses the same array-pointer type as `[byte_index..][0..@sizeOf(u32)]` but requires computing and sub-slicing the explicit end index. Simplified to the open-ended form; Zig derives the `*const [4]u8` type purely from the second `[0..@sizeOf(u32)]`. Identical bytes read, identical endianness handling, one fewer arithmetic op per loop iteration.

Other files scanned this fire (`doe_label_store.zig`, `runtime/threading_contract.zig`) were already clean â€” small, focused contract / C-ABI files with nothing to collapse. Survey pass, not every file is a target.

Validation: `zig build test` â†’ PASS; `zig build test-wgsl` â†’ PASS.

## Push: `full/surface_api.zig` DRY cleanup (2026-04-18 UTC)

Second random-file style review fire. `runtime/zig/src/full/surface_api.zig` had two tightenable spots:

`full_only_coverage_ledger` was calling `full_only_command_kind_names()` into a scratch array just to index `kind_names[i]` inside the subsequent `inline for` â€” but the same loop already has `field.name` in scope. Removed the scratch array and reached `field.name` directly. The public `full_only_command_kind_names` helper stays unchanged for its external test callers (`runtime/zig/tests/full/surface_api_test.zig`).

`combined_coverage_ledger` built its output by two hand-rolled `for (slice, 0..) |entry, i|` copy loops. Replaced both with `@memcpy(combined[0..CORE_COMMAND_COUNT], &core_ledger);` + `@memcpy(combined[CORE_COMMAND_COUNT..], &full_ledger);`. Same semantics â€” `CoverageEntry` is a plain struct of two `[]const u8` slice headers plus a `CoverageStatus` enum, so memcpy of the struct is identical to field-by-field assignment â€” but expresses intent in one line per segment.

Validation: `zig build test` â†’ PASS (all five existing surface_api tests still green: accepts/classifies/total-count/combined-ledger-exhaustive/domain-classification/command-count-matches-partition); `zig build test-wgsl` â†’ PASS.

## Push: bench/lib DRY cleanup â€” `canonical` / `canonical_source`, `load_taxonomy_*` (2026-04-18 UTC)

Random-file style review starting with `bench/lib/bench_utils.py` and `bench/lib/compare_axes.py`. Both changes keep the public surface and function names intact; only the bodies collapse.

`bench_utils.py`: `canonical(source: str)` and `canonical_source(source: Any)` held the same three-line body â€” strip any `+`-suffixed qualifier, empty-string fallback â€” with `canonical_source` adding a stricter `isinstance(source, str)` guard. Merged the two by widening `canonical` to `Any` with the stricter guard and making `canonical_source` a one-line alias that forwards to it. Both existing callers continue to work: `bench/gates/timing_policy_gate.py` imports `canonical`, and `bench/gates/comparable_runtime_invariants_gate.py` imports `canonical_source`. Behavioral check: `canonical("gpu+cpu") == "gpu"`, `canonical("") == ""`, `canonical(None) == ""`, `canonical(42) == ""` â€” no behavior change for any pre-existing input.

`compare_axes.py`: `load_taxonomy_products` and `load_taxonomy_surfaces` each re-open and re-parse `config/compare-taxonomy.json` with identical code, differing only in the axis key they look up. ## Push: DXGI_FORMAT spec-diff audit (4 latent bugs), D3D12 const consolidation (2026-04-18 UTC)

Extended the programmatic-diff audit to DXGI texture formats and more D3D12 enum families. Found **4 more latent bugs** in hand-transcribed DXGI_FORMAT values, all two swapped pairs:

- `DXGI_FORMAT_R16_UINT`: 58 â†’ **57** (was encoding R16_SNORM)
- `DXGI_FORMAT_R16_SNORM`: 57 â†’ **58** (was encoding R16_UINT)
- `DXGI_FORMAT_R8_UINT`: 63 â†’ **62** (was encoding R8_SNORM)
- `DXGI_FORMAT_R8_SNORM`: 62 â†’ **63** (was encoding R8_UINT)

Any render or vertex-input path that binds an R8Snorm or R16Snorm surface would have produced the wrong DXGI format â€” R8Snorm became R8_UINT, R8Uint became R8_SNORM, etc. Latent for the compute-only cohort but visible as validation errors on any texture/vertex path. The test fixture `runtime/zig/tests/backend/d3d12_descriptors_formats_test.zig` that previously codified the wrong values was corrected to the canonical mapping.

Consolidation pass: duplicated D3D12 consts in `resources/d3d12_depth_stencil.zig` (4 DXGI format consts), `commands/d3d12_copy.zig` (2 RESOURCE_STATE consts), and `commands/d3d12_render.zig` (2 INPUT_CLASSIFICATION consts) now re-export from `d3d12_constants.zig` / `d3d12_formats.zig` so the spec-diff parser has a single source of truth.

**Session running audit total: 34 latent bugs** (17 SPIR-V spec + 7 Vulkan constants + 2 D3D12 resource-state + 4 D3D12 SRV dimension + 4 DXGI format).

## Push: ORT EP session-smoke cases land Softmax + LayerNormalization end-to-end (2026-04-18 UTC)

Extends `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep_session_smoke.cc` with two new session-smoke cases that exercise the attention-shape ops added in the earlier ORT EP breadth push: `softmax` (rank-2 float32 along axis=-1, opset 13) and `layernorm` (rank-2 float32 with a 1-D scale, opset 17, axis=-1, epsilon=1e-5, no bias). Each case builds an in-memory ONNX model via the Model Editor API (`CreateUnaryModelAtOpset` for Softmax and a dedicated `CreateLayerNormModel` helper for the two-input form), runs the session through the Doe EP, and validates the output against a CPU reference baked into `BuildSmokeCases`. Both cases pass with `outputsMatch=true` and `routedThroughDoe=true`; the regenerated artifact is at `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/artifacts/20260418T170000Z/doe-ort-ep-session-smoke.json` with 14/14 cases successful and session-level `success: true`.

The `--case` selector now accepts `softmax`, `layernorm`, `concat` (plus the previously undocumented `sigmoid`, `tanh`, `gelu`), and the help string was updated to list them. `SmokeModelKind` gained `kSoftmax`, `kLayerNorm`, and `kConcat` along with the supporting name/input-count/claim-count/input-names switches.

**Concat blocker (deferred).** The Concat case is claimed and executed end-to-end by the Doe EP, but its session-smoke model build needs an integer `axis` attribute passed through `api->CreateOpAttr` to `model_editor_api->CreateNode`. Invoking that combo segfaults inside `libonnx.so.1` on `ReleaseOpAttr` despite the public header docs stating "OrtOpAttr instances are copied" â€” ownership semantics between `CreateOpAttr` and `CreateNode` still need to be pinned down. The smoke runner therefore keeps all Concat plumbing (enum entry, switch cases, `CreateBinaryConcatModel` helper) but omits the Concat `SmokeCaseSpec` from `BuildSmokeCases` so the full smoke suite runs clean. Follow-up: test the pattern against a pinned ORT 1.24/1.25 or look at how Chromium's WebNN ORT path drives the same combo, then re-enable the Concat case.

Validation: `zig build ort-plugin-ep ort-plugin-ep-session-smoke` â†’ PASS; `doe-ort-ep-session-smoke --case all` â†’ 14 cases successful, top-level `success: true`; `zig build test` â†’ PASS; `zig build test-wgsl` â†’ PASS.

## Push: loop-only `vectorData[col]` proof contract closes sixth matvec clamp (2026-04-18 UTC)

Closes the last of the six matvec clamps named in the earlier matcher push. New Lean theorem `loop_index_affine_inbounds_when_loop_fits_tight` in `pipeline/lean/Doe/Shader/ComputeBounds.lean` proves `i * loop_stride + offset < array_length` given `i < limit` and the tight precondition `(limit - 1) * loop_stride + offset + 1 â‰¤ array_length`. Matching matcher contract `loop_affine_matcher_contract_sound_tight` in `pipeline/lean/Doe/Shader/BoundsElisionMatcher.lean` with inductive `MatchesLoopAffine expr loop_stride offset` for the pattern `(.add (.mul .loopIndex (.lit loop_stride)) (.lit offset))`. Both theorems registered in `pipeline/lean/Doe/Extract.lean` (theorems list + bounds-elimination manifest) and picked up by the regenerated `pipeline/lean/artifacts/proven-conditions.json`.

Zig wiring: new `BoundsPattern.loop_1d_storage_buffer_affine` in `runtime/zig/src/lean_proof.zig`, gated on the tight contract string. New `DispatchPreconditionKind.loop_component` in `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/ir.zig`. `runtime/zig/src/dispatch_preconditions.zig` gains a `.loop_component` branch that computes `((loop_limit - 1) * loop_limit_multiplier + element_offset + 1) * element_stride_bytes` â€” dispatch-geometry independent â€” with an empty-loop short-circuit returning 0 bytes. `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/dispatch_proof_match.zig` gains `match_loop_only_affine_plus_offset` (reuses the existing `collect_additive_loop_terms` but requires `gid_multiplier == 0`) and a new `try_elide_storage_index` branch that ties it to `loop_match.find_bounded_loop_limit`. Three variant-count tests updated to expect 5 instead of 4 `DispatchPreconditionKind`s and the new `BoundsPattern` entry in the stability table.

End-to-end verification: running the rebuilt `zig-out/bin/doe-emit-spirv --shader-path bench/kernels/matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_naive_swizzle0.wgsl` under `-Dlean-verified=true` yields a 2548-byte SPIR-V with zero `OpArrayLength` / `OpExtInst UMin` sites (previously 2640 bytes with two clamp ops on `vectorData[col]`). `spirv-val` accepts the output. The checked-in `bench/kernels/*.spv` was intentionally NOT regenerated â€” the existing AMD Vulkan release receipt at `bench/out/amd-vulkan/20260418T193328Z/` remains the source of truth, and the 6-of-6 elision lands on the next AMD rerun.

Validation: `bash pipeline/lean/check.sh` â†’ `lean-check: ok`; `bash pipeline/lean/extract.sh` â†’ artifact written; `python3 pipeline/lean/test_proof_pipeline.py` â†’ 49/49 PASS; `zig build test` â†’ PASS; `zig build test-wgsl` â†’ PASS; `zig build test -Dlean-verified=true` â†’ PASS; `zig build test-wgsl -Dlean-verified=true` â†’ PASS; `spirv-val /tmp/matvec_proven.spv` â†’ PASS.

Added a medium-length DistilBERT sentiment shape (`sentiment_medium`) to the repo-only browser ORT WebGPU compare surface, between the existing short and longform shapes. Schema gate and spec-diff gate still pass.

This is a mechanical breadth add, not the ambitious Gemma 270M or full Transformers.js LLM shape originally proposed. Those remain out-of-scope for a single-session push because they require:

- Vendoring the `onnx-community/gemma-3-270m-it-ONNX` model + tokenizer into the jetstream Transformers.js tree (same pattern as the existing Xenova DistilBERT and Whisper entries).
- Refactoring the Playwright `runTask` closure so it is not hard-coded to a classification-shape output (logits â†’ argmax â†’ `["NEGATIVE","POSITIVE"]` labels). An LLM path needs either prefill-only shape (single forward pass, accept hidden-state outputs) or a full prefill+decode generation loop with token sampling.
- Parameterizing output validation per task type so non-classification tasks do not fail the existing expected-labels check.

The Whisper encoder is already vendored at `browser/chromium/src/third_party/jetstream/main/transformersjs/build/models/Xenova/whisper-tiny.en/` and is the lowest-friction next Transformers.js family to add (encoder-only is still a single forward pass), after the runTask refactor.

## Push: ORT EP attention-shape op breadth (Softmax, LayerNorm, Concat) (2026-04-18 UTC)

Extended the repo-only ONNX Runtime plugin EP to claim, compile, and execute three new same-shape float32 ops beyond the existing Identity/Add/Relu/Sigmoid/Tanh/Gelu/MatMul/Gemm cohort:

- **Softmax** (opset 13+): unary, last-axis reduction with the standard numerically-stable subtract-max formulation. Claim requires `SameTypeAndShape(input, output)`.
- **LayerNormalization** (opset 17): binary (`input`, `scale`), last-axis normalization with `epsilon=1e-5` and no bias slice in this pass. Claim requires the scale input to be 1-D and match `input.dims.back()`.
- **Concat** (opset 13+): binary, axis attribute read via `ReadOptionalIntAttribute` at claim time; validation rejects any pair whose non-axis dims disagree or whose axis is out of range. Kernel recovers the axis at compute time from the input-shape difference.

Bumped the EP compatibility-info version from `doe-ort-basic-ops-ep-v6` to `v7` to reflect the schema change.

Session-smoke counter serialization extended: `claimed_softmax_nodes`, `claimed_layernorm_nodes`, `claimed_concat_nodes` and the matching `compiled_*_groups` / `compute_*_calls` counters are now written into `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/artifacts/{timestamp}/doe-ort-ep-session-smoke.json`. Existing session-smoke cases (Add/Relu/MatMul/fusions) remain green â€” fresh artifact captured at `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/artifacts/20260418T160000Z/doe-ort-ep-session-smoke.json`.

Reshape was explicitly excluded from this pass: its INT64 shape tensor cannot traverse the EP's existing float32-only `DescribeSupportedTensorValue` path, and routing a second type through that helper is a separate refactor worth staging independently. RMSNormalization deferred for the same reason we defer scale-and-bias LayerNorm bias support: scoping.

Follow-up scope on the next iteration: (1) session-smoke test cases that build in-memory ONNX models with Softmax/LayerNormalization/Concat nodes using the OrtModel / OrtNode editor APIs, (2) matching bench/vendor-native command JSONs and `workloads.native.ort-doe-ep-smoke.json` entries, (3) adding the LayerNormalization bias input (ternary form) and Reshape once `DescribeSupportedTensorValue` accepts a caller-supplied accepted-type list.

Validation: `zig build ort-plugin-ep` â†’ PASS, `zig build ort-plugin-ep-session-smoke` â†’ PASS, existing session smoke with `--case all` â†’ PASS (all operations green, selected EP `DoeExecutionProvider`, 3 discovered devices), `zig build test` â†’ PASS, `zig build test-wgsl` â†’ PASS.

## Push: D3D12 SRV_DIMENSION audit (4 latent bugs), spec-diff parser extension (2026-04-18 UTC)

Extended the programmatic-diff audit pattern to D3D12 view-dimension, descriptor-heap, and descriptor-range constants. Found 4 latent bugs in hand-transcribed `D3D12_SRV_DIMENSION` values at `runtime/zig/src/backend/d3d12/resources/d3d12_texture_view.zig` lines 60-65:

- `SRV_DIMENSION_TEXTURE1D`: 3 â†’ **2** (was encoding TEXTURE1DARRAY)
- `SRV_DIMENSION_TEXTURE3D`: 7 â†’ **8** (was encoding TEXTURE2DMSARRAY)
- `SRV_DIMENSION_TEXTURECUBE`: 8 â†’ **9** (was encoding TEXTURE3D)
- `SRV_DIMENSION_TEXTURECUBEARRAY`: 9 â†’ **10** (was encoding TEXTURECUBE)

Every SRV create call through `map_view_dimension_to_srv` for a 1D, 3D, cube, or cube-array texture wrote the wrong `ViewDimension` into the `D3D12_SHADER_RESOURCE_VIEW_DESC`. Latent for the compute-only cohort that doesn't exercise SRVs today, but would have surfaced on any render/texture workload reaching this path.

Centralized `SRV_DIMENSION_*`, `DESCRIPTOR_HEAP_TYPE_*`, `DESCRIPTOR_RANGE_TYPE_*`, and `RESOURCE_DIMENSION_*` constants in `runtime/zig/src/backend/d3d12/d3d12_constants.zig` so they are governable. Updated `d3d12_texture_view.zig`, `d3d12_descriptors.zig`, and `d3d12_runtime_compute.zig` to import from the central file, removing three duplicated local copies of descriptor heap/range constants.

Extended `bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py` to resolve `NAME = ( OTHER + N )` enum-arithmetic canonical definitions in a second pass after literal values are collected. DirectX headers use this form for most enum continuations (e.g. `D3D12_DESCRIPTOR_RANGE_TYPE_UAV = ( D3D12_DESCRIPTOR_RANGE_TYPE_SRV + 1 )`), so without this the gate could only audit the first literal of each enum family. Iterates to fixed point so chained references resolve.

Registered four new spec-diff targets in `config/spec-diff-targets.json`: `d3d12_srv_dimension` (11 fields), `d3d12_descriptor_heap_type` (4 fields), `d3d12_descriptor_range_type` (4 fields), and `d3d12_resource_dimension` (5 fields). All pass against the in-tree Chromium directx-headers copy at `browser/chromium/src/third_party/dawn/third_party/directx-headers/src/include/directx/d3d12.h`.

**Session running audit total: 30 latent bugs** (17 SPIR-V spec + 7 Vulkan constants + 2 D3D12 resource-state + 4 D3D12 SRV dimension).

Validation: `python3 bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py` â†’ PASS (all 26 targets); `python3 bench/gates/schema_gate.py` â†’ PASS; `zig build test` â†’ PASS; `zig build test-wgsl` â†’ PASS.

## Push: Vulkan matvec proof matcher closes hot-loop clamp gap (2026-04-18 UTC)

The Vulkan lane now structurally closes the remaining proof-integration gap in
`compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_naive_swizzle0`: the bounds-elision matcher
recognizes matvec-style guarded loops whose trip count is a const global and
whose loop increment is the final body statement, and normalizes scaled affine
terms such as `((4 * rowBy4 + 2) * kPackedCols) + col` into the existing
gid-plus-loop-affine proof contract.

Baseline `-Dlean-verified=false` emission for the governed matvec shader was
2980 bytes with `minCount=6`, `dispatchPreconditions=0`, and six
`OpArrayLength` / `UMin` clamp sites in the disassembly. After the matcher fix,
`-Dlean-verified=true` emission is 2640 bytes with `minCount=1` and
`dispatchPreconditions=5`. The four hot-loop `matrixData[...]` clamps and the
final `outData[rowBy4]` clamp are removed; the only remaining clamp is the
`vectorData[col]` runtime-sized load, which needs a separate loop-only storage
buffer proof contract before it can be safely elided.

No AMD Vulkan timing claim is made from this shell. Strict AMD Vulkan preflight
is blocked here because `/dev/dri/renderD128` is unavailable, the user is not in
the `render` group, Dawn only exposes SwiftShader/CPU, and Doe selects
llvmpipe/non-AMD. The evidence from this pass is SPIR-V structure plus
validation, not a comparable governed benchmark row.

Validation: `spirv-val` passed on the proof-backed matvec SPIR-V;
`zig build test-wgsl -Dlean-verified=true`, `zig build test-wgsl`,
`zig build test -Dlean-verified=true`, `zig build test`, and
`zig build -Doptimize=ReleaseFast -Dlean-verified=true` passed under
`runtime/zig`.

## Push: CSL operation graph contract and v1.4 parser fix validation (2026-04-18 UTC)

Added `config/csl-operation-graph.schema.json` as the additive receipt shape
for CSL host/device orchestration. The schema is discriminated by
`orchestrationMode`: `memcpy` for direct `cslc` plus `SdkRuntime.memcpy_*` /
`launch` flows, and `sdklayout` for Python `SdkLayout` code regions, ports,
connections, streams, and async `send` / `receive` flows. This keeps Gemma 4
E2B on the direct memcpy ladder while reserving a schema-backed path for 31B
streaming.

Registered two SDK-grounded memcpy samples:
`examples/csl-operation-graph.gelu-rpc-launch.sample.json` for the
`rpc_launch` path and `examples/csl-operation-graph.gemv-streaming.sample.json`
for the `streaming_memcpy_driven` path. The streaming graph targets memcpy
colors rather than exported device symbols for streamed tensors, mirroring
GEMV 9 / checkerboard. Tiny local CSL source fixtures live under
`examples/csl/` so source-level unblock checks are gateable without depending
on external docs pages.

`executionPattern` is now the memcpy-mode discriminator, and
`reservedResources` ships as optional day-one metadata for colors, queues,
task IDs, and memcpy channels. Added `bench/gates/csl_operation_graph_gate.py`
and wired it into `bench/runners/run_blocking_gates.py` after the schema and
fixture mirror gates. The gate checks exported-symbol or memcpy-color
references, memcpy ROI bounds against the declared PE grid, pattern-specific
presence of launch or streaming memcpy-color operations, required
`sys_mod.unblock_cmd_stream()` completion for RPC-launch memcpy functions, and
SdkLayout stream/port/region referential integrity. Updated
`docs/csl-architecture.md`, `docs/process.md`, and `bench/README.md` to make
the operation graph contract a named source of truth.

The CSL v1.4 parser fix was also applied to the checked-in Gemma 3 270M
manifest smoke compile fixture so the governed lane no longer feeds
`[chunk_size][4]f32` declarations to `cslc`. The source emitter already emits
`[chunk_size * 4]f32` for vector-backed runtime storage buffers and scalar
`[*]f32` exported pointers; the simulator fixture now matches that declaration
shape.

The governed 270M lane was rerun without a configured SDK compiler. It failed
closed as expected: host-plan parity matched, compile status was `blocked` with
reason `compiler_unavailable`, run status was `blocked` with reason
`compile_not_ready`, and the materialized `/tmp/compile/gemv/pe_program.csl`
contained only the flattened storage declarations. A real SDK v1.4 retry still
requires `DOE_CSLC_EXECUTABLE` or `--cslc-executable`.

Validation: `python3 bench/gates/schema_gate.py`,
`python3 bench/gates/csl_fixture_mirror_gate.py`,
`python3 bench/gates/csl_operation_graph_gate.py`,
`python3 bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py`,

## Push: CSL fixture mirror gate (2026-04-18 UTC)

Added a schema-backed CSL fixture mirror registry at `config/csl-fixture-mirrors.json`, validated by `config/csl-fixture-mirrors.schema.json`. The registry declares byte-identical `examples/` to `runtime/zig/examples/` mirror pairs, path-context mirrors with explicit ignored JSON pointers, and runtime-only fixtures.

Added `bench/gates/csl_fixture_mirror_gate.py` and wired it into `bench/runners/run_blocking_gates.py` after the schema hard gate. The gate verifies canonical mirrored fixtures are schema-target registered, runtime-local `doe-wgsl-*.json` fixtures are declared, byte-identical pairs match exactly, and path-context mirrors match after removing only their declared JSON pointers. The Gemma 4 E2B simulator plan declares `/driver/executablePath` as the sole path-context field because the driver path is resolved relative to each simulator-plan copy.

Updated `docs/csl-architecture.md`, `docs/process.md`, and `bench/README.md` so the mirror contract points to the registry and hard gate instead of relying on prose-only byte-identity guidance. `docs/csl-architecture.md` also now records the SDK complete-program implication: CSL evidence must bind layout code, PE programs, compile params, exported symbols, memcpy rectangles, RPC launches, routing resources, task IDs, and command-stream completion requirements rather than treating generated PE code as the whole artifact. It also records the likely 31B streaming contract direction: SdkLayout-style code-region graphs, ports, stream IDs, demux/mux regions, async send/receive ordering, and tensor-to-PE sharding maps require a future schema migration instead of hidden driver behavior.

Flattened vector storage-buffer declarations emitted by the shared CSL IR walker from nested `[chunk_size][N]T` syntax to `[chunk_size * N]T`, because SDK v1.4 accepts comma-separated multidimensional array syntax but rejects chained bracket array types. The architecture note also records the GEMV 9 streaming constraint that memcpy stream order can be semantic and must be captured in receipts.

Validation: `python3 bench/gates/schema_gate.py`, `python3 bench/gates/csl_fixture_mirror_gate.py`, `python3 bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py`, `python3 -m py_compile bench/gates/csl_fixture_mirror_gate.py bench/runners/run_blocking_gates.py`, and `git diff --check` passed.

## Push: SPIR-V artifact persistence, Dawn preflight fix, matvec bounds-elision Lean tightening (2026-04-18 UTC)

Three targeted changes aimed at unblocking the release pipeline and the one remaining AMD Vulkan regression.

**(1) Real SPIR-V artifact persistence behind `shader_artifact_gate.py --require-spirv-validation`.** Extended `runtime/zig/src/backend/common/shader_artifact_manifest.zig` with `StageArtifact` + `emit_shader_artifact_manifest_for_signature_with_artifacts`: the emitter now writes a sibling `.spv` file next to each manifest when the backend has the compiled SPIR-V bytes and records the file path in the `ir_to_spirv` stage record. Plumbed through the Vulkan backend (`runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/native_runtime.zig` stores `pending_spirv_bytes_owned`, `vk_pipeline.zig` captures words after `vkCreateShaderModule`, `mod.zig` exposes `pending_spirv_bytes_view` / `release_pending_spirv_bytes` methods on `ZigVulkanBackend` so the shared emitter can `@hasDecl`-gate the feature). Smoke: a fresh `doe-zig-runtime --execute --trace-meta /tmp/m.json` run emits `bench/out/shader-artifacts/vulkan_shader_artifact_2.json` with `ir_to_spirv.artifactPath=vulkan_shader_artifact_2.spv` plus a sibling 228-byte `.spv`; `spirv-val` accepts the binary (exit 0). Manifest still validates against `config/shader-artifact.schema.json` (artifactPath was already optional in the stage record).

**(2) Dawn sidecar preflight library-name drift fixed.** `bench/runners/preflight_bench_host.py` was looking for `bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/libwebgpu.so` and `libwgpu_native.so`. Current vendored Dawn output is `libwebgpu_dawn.so` (the Zig runtime's dlopen loader at `runtime/zig/src/core/abi/wgpu_loader.zig` tries that first Dawn candidate) and `libwgpu_native.so` was a wgpu-native alternative-impl check unrelated to the Dawn-vs-Doe path. Preflight updated to check `libwebgpuDawn` only; `run_release_pipeline.py --dry-run` now plans cleanly through preflight â†’ compare â†’ gates, and `preflight_bench_host.py --strict-amd-vulkan` reports 10/10 ok including the Dawn adapter identity probe.

**(3) Matvec regression: tight-precondition Lean theorem landed.** Spirv-dis of the current `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_naive_swizzle0` SPIR-V shows the inner loop still carries 4Ã— `OpArrayLength` + `OpExtInst UMin` robustness clamps per iteration (one per unrolled matrix row). Those access patterns match `MatchesGidLoopAffine` but the current Lean theorem `gid_affine_plus_scaled_loop_index_inbounds_when_dispatch_fits` uses the over-approximate precondition `total * gid_stride + limit * loop_stride + offset â‰¤ array_length`, which for the matvec shape (total=8192, gid_stride=2048, limit=512, loop_stride=1) computes `16,777,728` â€” exceeds the exactly-packed 256 MB / 16,777,216-vec4f buffer by `gid_stride + loop_stride - 1 = 2048` elements. Elision therefore does not fire and RADV still schedules around the clamps.

Proven a tight-precondition variant `gid_affine_plus_scaled_loop_index_inbounds_when_dispatch_fits_tight` (and its matcher contract `gid_loop_affine_matcher_contract_sound_tight`) that uses `(total - 1) * gid_stride + (limit - 1) * loop_stride + offset + 1 â‰¤ array_length` â€” the strict supremum of the indexed range plus one. For matvec this evaluates to `16,775,680 â‰¤ 16,777,216` âœ“, unlocking elision. Both theorems added to `Doe/Extract.lean` and regenerated into `pipeline/lean/artifacts/proven-conditions.json`; `bash pipeline/lean/check.sh` â†’ `lean-check: ok`; `python3 pipeline/lean/test_proof_pipeline.py` â†’ 49/49 pass.

Wired Zig to the tight variant: `lean_proof.boundsProven(.gid_1d_storage_buffer_loop_affine)` now gates on `gid_loop_affine_matcher_contract_sound_tight`, and `dispatch_preconditions.required_buffer_bytes` for `.gid_component` kinds computes the tight formula (with an empty-dispatch short-circuit returning 0 bytes). Updated the 8 Zig preconditions tests to the tight expected values; both `zig build test` and `zig build test-wgsl` (and their `-Dlean-verified=true` variants) pass.

Does not include a fresh matvec benchmark â€” that requires a bench run on the AMD Vulkan host and is not part of this change. Expected impact: the 4Ã— inner-loop UMin clamps become no-ops at SPV generation time in the `-Dlean-verified=true` build, removing ~4Ã— `OpExtInst UMin` + 4Ã— `OpArrayLength` + 4Ã— `OpISub` per inner iteration Ã— 512 iterations Ã— 8192 rows from the hot path.

Validation: `python3 bench/gates/schema_gate.py` â†’ PASS; `python3 bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py` â†’ PASS; `python3 pipeline/lean/test_proof_pipeline.py` â†’ 49/49 PASS; `zig build test` + `zig build test-wgsl` (both with and without `-Dlean-verified=true`) â†’ PASS; `python3 bench/runners/preflight_bench_host.py --strict-amd-vulkan` â†’ 10/10 ok.

## Push: spec-diff CI gate + render-lane option (b) audit (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Spec-diff gate landed.** New `bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py` drives the programmatic-diff pattern from the earlier spec-audit passes as a blocking gate. Targets are declared in `config/spec-diff-targets.json` (validated by `config/spec-diff-targets.schema.json` and registered in `config/schema-targets.json`). The gate parses canonical identifiers from the in-tree chromium-sysroot headers (`browser/chromium/src/third_party/spirv-headers/src/include/spirv/unified1/spirv.h`, `vulkan-headers/.../vulkan_core.h`, `dawn/third_party/directx-headers/src/include/directx/d3d12.h`) and diffs their numeric values against the named Zig constants under matched namespaces in `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_spec.zig`, `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_constants.zig`, and `runtime/zig/src/backend/d3d12/d3d12_constants.zig`. Added to `docs/process.md` as a blocking gate alongside the schema hard gate.

First-run found one new latent bug (audit total: 27):

- `ImageOperandsMask.Offset`: 0x4 â†’ **0x10**
- `ImageOperandsMask.Grad`: 0x8 â†’ **0x4**
- `ImageOperandsMask.ConstOffset`: 0x10 â†’ **0x8**

Three-way permutation in `spirv_spec.zig`. Callers live in `emit_spirv_texture.zig` (OpImageSampleExplicitLod / OpImageSampleDrefExplicitLod / OpImageFetch with explicit gradients, const offsets, or runtime offsets). Latent in the compute-only cohort â€” storage-image paths do not emit these operands â€” but any texture-sampling shader using those operand modes would have written the wrong operand bitset into the generated SPIR-V word. Fixed to canonical values; `zig build test` + `zig build test-wgsl` green.

**Render-lane option (b) audit.** The prior session's wrap-up flagged "~10 `implementation_gap` rows with 'timing sources differ between sides'" as mechanically fixable by per-row timing-source alignment. Current-state audit across every catalog under `bench/workloads/` finds exactly 4 such rows (all in `workloads.amd.vulkan.json`), and none are pure timing-source issues:

- `render_pixel_local_storage_barrier`, `render_pixel_local_storage_barrier_500`: Dawn reports `dispatch counts differ for row/success=(1, 1): [1] vs [0]` â€” Dawn delegate does not execute the workload. Option (a) class, not option (b).
- `render_draw_indexed_200k`, `render_draw_redundant_pipeline_bindings_200k`: `baseline execution unsuccessful on some samples`, `baseline execution reported errors`, `row/success shape sets differ`, `execution shape (dispatch/row/success counts) differs`. Dawn partially-fails; the gap is not timing-instrument skew.

Conclusion: option (b) is not actionable against the current catalog. The addressable render rows (DrawCallPerf DynamicBindGroup_RenderBundle / DynamicPipeline_DynamicBindGroup_RenderBundle variants) were already promoted to `comparable` in commit 45cabfade. No workload edits were made in this pass â€” forcing timing alignment on rows with execution-shape mismatch or Dawn-side partial failure would mask real comparability failures and violate the structural-work-equivalence discipline.

**Lean matcher contracts.** The wrap-up's item 4 (add gid+offset, loop-affine, tiled, flat 2D/3D, texture contracts) is already in-tree: `pipeline/lean/Doe/Shader/BoundsElisionMatcher.lean` defines `MatchesGidOffset`, `MatchesGidStrideOffset`, `MatchesGidLoopAffine`, `MatchesGidTiled`, plus `flat_{2,3}d_{,offset_}matcher_contract_sound` and `texture_{1,2,3}d_{identity,affine,tiled}_matcher_contract_sound`. `python3 pipeline/lean/test_proof_pipeline.py` â†’ 49/49 pass. No new proofs needed from this angle.

Validation: `python3 bench/gates/schema_gate.py` â†’ PASS; `python3 bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py` â†’ PASS; `python3 pipeline/lean/test_proof_pipeline.py` â†’ 49/49 PASS; `zig build test` + `zig build test-wgsl` â†’ PASS.

## Push: remove SPV-local folds + d3d12 state-constant audit (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Two bounded cleanup passes executed after the concurrent-session IR rewrite pass landed.

**(1) Removed the SPV-local const-fold and identity-fold.** The concurrent session's `ir_opt_rewrite.apply()` runs over the module before every emit path (production via `doe_wgsl.translate()`, bench via `prepare_module_for_emit()` at emit-site 391/429/467/508/606). Once that's proven to cover the op set the SPV-local folds handled, keeping both copies is pure duplication. Deleted `try_fold_const_binary` and `try_fold_identity_binary` from `emit_spirv_fn.zig::emit_value_expr` and removed the orphaned `emit_spirv_fn_folds.zig` entirely. 27 tracked SPVs regenerated; all 27 bit-identical to the pre-removal set â€” confirming the IR rewrite is a strict superset of the per-emitter fold logic. `zig build test` / `test-wgsl` green.

**(2) Audited d3d12_constants.zig with the same programmatic-diff pattern that found 24 bugs earlier in the session.** Diffed 19 D3D12 / D3D constants against `d3d12.h` / `d3dcommon.h` in the Chromium directx-headers tree. Two off-by bugs found:

- `RESOURCE_STATE_COPY_DEST`: 0x800 â†’ **0x400**
- `RESOURCE_STATE_COPY_SOURCE`: 0x400 â†’ **0x800**

These were **swapped**. Any texture transitioning into or out of a copy state from Doe's Zig D3D12 backend would have passed the wrong state constant; the D3D12 runtime would interpret "COPY_DEST" requests as "COPY_SOURCE" and vice versa, triggering validation errors on debug devices. Latent for the compute-only cohort but would surface on any render or copy-heavy workload.

Also fixed a locally-duplicated copy of the same swap in `src/backend/d3d12/commands/d3d12_copy.zig:108-109`. The compound `RESOURCE_STATE_GENERIC_READ` expression (hardcoded bitmask) is unaffected because it uses literal bit values rather than the named constants.

**Session running audit total: 26 latent bugs** (17 SPIR-V spec + 7 Vulkan constants + 2 D3D12 resource-state). `csl_spec.zig` and `dxil_spec.zig` would need vendor SDK / LLVM 3.7 bitcode headers to run the programmatic diff; left for later.

## Push: fix 2 wrong VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE values (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Applied the same audit pattern that turned up the SPIR-V spec bugs to `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_constants.zig`. Programmatic diff of all 43 `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_*` values against the canonical `vulkan_core.h` in the tree surfaced two mismatches:

- `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_MEMORY_ALLOCATE_INFO`: 17 â†’ **5**. Collided with `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_PIPELINE_CACHE_CREATE_INFO`. Every `vkAllocateMemory` call in `vk_resources.zig` / `vk_upload.zig` / `vk_render.zig` was passing `sType=17`. The AMDGPU driver silently tolerated it because validation layers are off in release and `VkMemoryAllocateInfo`'s first four fields (sType, pNext, allocationSize, memoryTypeIndex) happen to line up with `VkPipelineCacheCreateInfo`.
- `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_PIPELINE_RASTERIZATION_DEPTH_CLIP_STATE_CREATE_INFO_EXT`: 1000102000 â†’ **1000102001**. The wrong value is actually `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_PHYSICAL_DEVICE_DEPTH_CLIP_ENABLE_FEATURES_EXT` per the header. Not exercised by the current cohort.

Test that had baked in the wrong value (`vulkan_upload_test.zig:750` asserted 17 for MEMORY_ALLOCATE_INFO) updated to 5. Matvec bench post-fix: 7/7 success, p50=2098.76ms â€” consistent with prior runs, confirming the corrected sType does not change driver behavior on this host.

**Running session spec-audit total: 19 latent bugs fixed** (17 SPIR-V + 2 Vulkan struct types). The pattern generalizes well â€” a programmatic diff against canonical headers catches what isolated test fixtures miss, especially when those fixtures have historically frozen the wrong values.
