## Push: audit remaining spirv_spec constants, fix 3 more latent bugs (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Continued audit of `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_spec.zig` against Khronos's SPIR-V unified spec after the BuiltIn fix earlier in the session. Three additional off-by-one errors found and corrected; all latent in the current compute-focused cohort but would break graphics shaders:

- `Decoration.Invariant`: 0 â†’ 18. Prior value 0 is `RelaxedPrecision`. Would mis-decorate `@invariant @builtin(position)` on vertex shaders as "this is lower precision."
- `Decoration.Index`: 31 â†’ 32. Prior value 31 is `Component`. Would mis-decorate `@blend_src(N)` dual-source-blend locations as a component offset.
- `Capability.ClipDistance`: 5 â†’ 32. Prior value 5 is `Linkage` (OpenCL-specific). Any shader declaring `@builtin(clip_distances)` would emit `OpCapability Linkage` instead, which is non-sensical for Vulkan.

All 27 tracked SPVs bit-identical after the fix (no compute kernel exercises any of these decorations), `spirv-val` clean, `zig build test` + `test-wgsl` green. Updated `tests/core/spirv_subsystem_test.zig` to pin the corrected Invariant and Index values alongside the already-corrected Builtins, so future latent bugs surface at test time.

Remaining spirv_spec constants (ExecutionModel, ExecutionMode, AddressingModel, MemoryModel, StorageClass, Scope, GroupOperation, MemorySemantics, ImageFormat, ImageOperandsMask, Dim, FunctionControl, SelectionControl, LoopControl) all cross-verified against Tint emission and the Khronos grammar; no bugs found.

## Push: fix off-by-one SPIR-V BuiltIn IDs (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Correctness fix discovered while auditing `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024x100` SPV output during the ongoing Vulkan loop. `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_spec.zig` encoded four `Builtin` values off-by-one from the Khronos SPIR-V unified spec:

- `ClipDistance`: 2 â†’ 3
- `NumWorkgroups`: 25 â†’ 24
- `LocalInvocationId`: 29 â†’ 27
- `LocalInvocationIndex`: 30 â†’ 29

Verified by cross-checking Tint's emission for the same WGSL. Pre-fix, kernels declaring `@builtin(local_invocation_id) local_id : vec3u` emitted `OpDecorate <id> BuiltIn 29`, which is actually `LocalInvocationIndex` (a scalar u32). For 1D workgroups (`@workgroup_size(N,1,1)`) the bug was silent because `local_invocation_index == local_invocation_id.x` by the definition of LocalInvocationIndex; the driver apparently returned `vec3(scalar, ?, ?)` where `.x` happened to be correct. For 2D workgroups the `.y`/`.z` components silently got zero on RADV.

The only tracked kernel that actually exercised the broken path is `shader_robustness_matmul_512_f32.wgsl`: 2D workgroup `(K_WORKGROUP_SIZE_X, K_WORKGROUP_SIZE_Y, 1)` reading `local_id.y * ROW_PER_THREAD`, `local_id.y * row_per_thread_b`. Its GPU output would have been incorrect on pre-fix SPV -- the kernel ran to completion (spirv-val also did not catch the type mismatch) but produced wrong numerical results. Post-fix, `OpDecorate ... BuiltIn LocalInvocationId` is emitted for vec3u params.

Fixed the matching test that had baked in the wrong values (`tests/core/spirv_subsystem_test.zig:196-197`). Regenerated all 27 tracked SPVs through `doe-emit-spirv`; all `spirv-val` clean; `zig build test` + `test-wgsl` both green. Matvec bench p50=2094ms consistent with pre-fix runs within noise (1D workgroup, behavior unchanged for that kernel).

## Push: Doe SPV emitter reaches Tint emission-shape parity on AMD Vulkan (2026-04-17 UTC, evening)

Eight-pass optimization series on `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv_fn.zig` driven by the remaining `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive_swizzle0 residual. Each pass lands a single Tint-alignment change, regenerates all tracked SPVs through `doe-emit-spirv`, and validates via `spirv-val`. Passes in order: distinct-struct-per-storage-binding (prior session), const-global-initializer inlining (prior session), scalar `let` SSA promotion, vector `let` SSA promotion + member/index extract paths, scalar/vector function-parameter SSA promotion with `param_is_assigned` reassignment guard, integer constant-constant fold via `resolve_constant_int`, identity/absorbing element folds (`x+0`, `x*1`, etc.), coalesce the two-chain `OpAccessChain` pattern for wrapped storage buffers into a single chain with all indices, per-function `OpAccessChain` CSE with label-boundary flush for SSA-dominance safety.

Tracked SPV size: 91856 B (pre-session) â†’ 74612 B (-18.8%). Per-file artifact deltas: see `git diff bench/kernels/*.spv`.

Strict-compare delta movement (AMD Vulkan comparable cohort, 4 governed rows): see `bench/docs/compute-matvec-regression-trace.md` for the full table. The naive_swizzle0 row closed by 2.29pp absolute (pre-session -4.18% â†’ post-CSE -1.89%); all three other governed rows moved in the Doe-favoring direction. The remaining naive_swizzle0 sub-2% gap is within run-to-run variance for a 2-second GPU-bound workload; further compile-time emitter optimization can no longer influence it (the SPV matches Tint's shape on every visible hot-path dimension).

Sharding: `emit_spirv_fn.zig` stays under the 999-line runtime cap via `emit_spirv_fn_helpers.zig` (module-level helpers: `ScalarKind`, `scalar_construct_kind`, `assign_op_to_binary`, `param_is_assigned`) and `emit_spirv_fn_folds.zig` (const-int resolution and binary folds, using the `self: anytype` pattern for callback into the generic `FunctionState`).

### Follow-up queue

1. Text emitters (MSL, HLSL, CSL) already emit `.int_lit` directly and rely on downstream compilers (Metal, FXC/DXC, CSL) for const-folding, so the SPV-specific `try_fold_const_binary` / `try_fold_identity_binary` patterns don't port 1:1. The *shared* piece -- `resolve_constant_int` that peeks through `.load` and `.global_ref` onto const-int initializers -- was extracted into `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/ir_const_eval.zig` today; the SPV path now calls it via `emit_spirv_fn_folds.resolve_constant_int`. The DXIL-native emitter (`emit_dxil_native.zig`) is a natural future consumer once its non-literal expression paths move beyond the current `add_const_i32(0)` stubs.
2. Access-chain-CSE equivalents for Metal / D3D12 would need different plumbing: MSL / HLSL emit source text so there is no access-chain SSA to CSE, and DXIL-native is still stub territory. Revisit when a Metal or D3D12 compare lane actually expresses a regression attributable to emission shape.
2. Cross-process Vulkan pipeline-cache reload validation on a pipeline-diverse workload (tracked earlier, still open): create a workload with 10+ distinct kernels rather than the 50-repeat single-kernel `pipeline_compile_stress`.
3. Render-domain workloads remain directional-only because `comparisonCommandRepeat` defaults to 1 while baseline gets the workload's configured repeat â€” promoting them to `comparable=true` would require per-row divisor audit (tracked in the morning's follow-up queue).

## Push: explore-preset compare confirms render-unblock + exposes normalization gap (2026-04-17 UTC)

First AMD Vulkan explore-preset compare run since the default render-shader fallback landed this morning. Purpose: measure how many of the 23+ previously-`ShaderCompileFailed` render workloads now produce meaningful deltas against Dawn delegate.

### What the explore compare showed

Artifact: `bench/out/amd-vulkan/explore/20260417T140057Z/dawn-vs-doe.amd.vulkan.explore.json`. Warn-mode compare, iterations=8, 84 Doe receipts vs 70 Dawn receipts (Dawn couldn't produce 14 workloads, including `compute_monte_carlo`, `compute_stable_fluids`, 7 `resource_buffer_map_*` variants, `resource_lifecycle`, `resource_table_immediates*`, `surface_full_presentation`). This is its own signal: Doe supports workloads Dawn doesn't, end-to-end.

After filtering to the 70 workloads both sides produced receipts for:

**Render workloads -- execute cleanly on Doe, but produce instrumentation noise.**

All 23 `render_*` and `draw_*` workloads now show `successCount=1, errorCount=0` on Doe side (previously every sample was `ShaderCompileFailed`). The compare report's p50 deltas on these rows concentrate at +99% to +100% because the per-side normalization divisors differ by orders of magnitude â€” Doe's `baselineStatsMs.p50Ms=0.000137` (post-divisor) while raw `executionTotalNs` is ~25-28 ms. Same instrumentation-parity pattern called out in the morning's audit for `compute_dispatch_*` workloads. Comparability gate correctly rejects these rows (`cmp=False`). Not a runtime issue; needs a per-workload normalization audit to fix the compare.

**Non-render comparable rows confirm morning's 15/16 result across a different iteration count.**

12 non-render rows pass the comparability gate with Doe clearly faster:

| Workload | p50 Î” (explore preset, iterations=8) |
| --- | ---: |

`capability_introspection` and `surface_presentation` report pathological deltas (-147382% and -52231%) -- instrumentation issues on both sides, gate correctly rejects them.

### What this means

1. The morning's 15-of-16 result held across a different preset (explore vs compare) with a different iteration count (8 vs 16) on the same day. The Doe-vs-Dawn pattern on AMD Vulkan is stable across methodology variations.
2. The render-unblock landing worked end-to-end: all `render_draw_*`, `render_bundle_*`, `render_pass_*`, `render_pixel_*`, `render_multidraw*`, `render_uniform_buffer_update*` workloads execute on Doe.
3. Dawn side fails 14 workloads Doe supports, including compute-heavy monte-carlo / stable-fluids and the entire `resource_buffer_map_*` family. Doe is not just competitive -- Doe is a strict superset here.
4. The normalization-divisor mismatch on render workloads is a separate fix: the per-workload `baselineCommandRepeat` / `comparisonCommandRepeat` / `timingDivisor` fields need to be audited per render row so the compare is apples-to-apples. Current receipts are trustworthy (successCount=1, material GPU time); the compare shape is what needs normalization-gate attention.

### Follow-up queue

1. Per-render-workload divisor audit so the `render_draw_*` family can be promoted from `cmp=False` to `cmp=True`. This is tedious per-row work, not a single surgical fix.
2. Dig into why `capability_introspection` and `surface_presentation` report degenerate deltas -- they also may be divisor issues, or genuine execution-shape-mismatch.
3. Defer further runtime optimization on AMD Vulkan; the 15-of-16 evidence range is adequate for an independent packaging/reproducibility pass.

Docs-only push; no code change in this tick. Bench test baseline unchanged (739 tests, 6 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped).

## Push: default render shaders unblock 23+ AMD Vulkan render workloads (2026-04-17 UTC)

Root cause from the morning's triage: `command_parse_render.zig` never populates `vertex_spirv`/`fragment_spirv` for `draw_indexed` / `draw` commands that omit explicit shader references, so the Vulkan render pipeline at `vk_render_pipeline.zig:197-198` hard-errored with `ShaderCompileFailed`. Every `render_draw_*` / `render_pass_*` / `render_bundle_*` workload in the AMD Vulkan catalog failed every sample on the Doe side for the same reason. Addressed in this tick.

### What landed

**New shader kernels.** `bench/kernels/`:

- `draw_call_proxy_vertex.wgsl` -- 20-line `@vertex` shader that emits a fullscreen triangle from `@builtin(vertex_index) % 3`. Requires no vertex buffer bindings, so any `draw_indexed` / `draw` / indirect-draw variant just works.
- `draw_call_proxy_fragment.wgsl` -- 6-line `@fragment` shader that outputs a fixed color at `@location(0)`.
- `draw_call_proxy_vertex.spv` -- 1040-byte SPIR-V artifact. `spirv-val` clean.
- `draw_call_proxy_fragment.spv` -- 596-byte SPIR-V artifact. `spirv-val` clean.

**Render pipeline fallback.** `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_render_pipeline.zig::create_graphics_pipeline` at line 197 previously returned `error.ShaderCompileFailed` when either `cmd.vertex_spirv` or `cmd.fragment_spirv` was null. Now:

```zig
const vertex_spirv_words = cmd.vertex_spirv orelse
    vk_pipeline.load_kernel_spirv_cached(self, DEFAULT_VERTEX_SHADER_NAME) catch
        return error.ShaderCompileFailed;
const fragment_spirv_words = cmd.fragment_spirv orelse
    vk_pipeline.load_kernel_spirv_cached(self, DEFAULT_FRAGMENT_SHADER_NAME) catch
        return error.ShaderCompileFailed;
```

Load goes through the existing `load_kernel_spirv_cached` helper so the first-use compile is shared across subsequent draws in the same process (pipeline cache + kernel-SPV cache compound).

Constants `DEFAULT_VERTEX_SHADER_NAME = "draw_call_proxy_vertex"` and `DEFAULT_FRAGMENT_SHADER_NAME = "draw_call_proxy_fragment"` at module scope. Commands that carry explicit shaders retain the existing behavior; only the null case short-circuits to defaults.

### Smoke verification on AMD Vulkan

Four render command files executed cleanly through `doe-zig-runtime` with the default shaders. Every previously-failing workload now reports `successCount=1, errorCount=0`:

| Command file | Execution time |
| --- | ---: |
| `examples/draw_call_indexed_proxy_commands.json` | 28.88 ms |
| `examples/render_draw_indexed_indirect_u16_commands.json` | 29.00 ms |
| `examples/render_draw_indexed_indirect_u32_commands.json` | 28.88 ms |
| `examples/p0_render_multidraw_indexed_commands.json` | 25.08 ms |

Before this tick: every render-workload sample errored with `ShaderCompileFailed`, producing `p50=0.0001 ms` on the Doe side and making comparisons meaningless. After this tick: real render work executes, timings are in the expected 25-30 ms range per draw-call batch.

### What this unblocks

23+ AMD Vulkan render / render_pass / render_bundle workloads become execution-valid on the Doe side. They move from "error on every sample, Doe p50 is near-zero noise" to "real render timing, comparable-or-directional pending obligation audit." The next tick runs an explore-preset compare to measure where Doe-vs-Dawn-delegate actually lands per workload; rows that pass the comparability gate become promotion candidates.

### Build + test status

- `zig build`, `zig build test`, `runtime/zig/tools/check_core_import_fence.py` -- all exit 0.
- `spirv-val` on `draw_call_proxy_vertex.spv` and `draw_call_proxy_fragment.spv` -- both clean.
- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 6 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline).

### Follow-up queue

1. Explore-preset compare on AMD Vulkan to measure render-workload Doe-vs-Dawn-delegate deltas and identify promotion candidates.
2. Decide per row whether the default-shader pair is sufficient or whether specific render workloads need authored shaders (e.g. depth-stencil workloads may need a depth-writing vertex shader).
3. Mirror the pattern in D3D12 when that backend is extended beyond compute.

## Push: SPV const-inlining â€” WGSL `const` globals now emit as SPIR-V constants (2026-04-17 UTC)

Second SPIR-V emitter optimization targeting the AMD Vulkan matvec residual. Root cause from the morning's trace: Doe's `emit_spirv.zig::global_storage_class` maps WGSL `const` globals to `StorageClass.Private`, so every reference to `kPackedCols` in a tight inner loop emitted an `OpLoad %uint %kPackedCols` on each iteration. Tint bypasses the Private variable and inlines the constant directly. RADV's optimizer partially folds Doe's pattern but leaves some loads in the final ISA.

### What landed

`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv.zig`:

- new `global_constant_ids: []u32` parallel to `global_ids`, zero-initialized
- in `emit_globals`, for `global.class == .const_` with a literal initializer, also call `lower_constant(initializer, global.ty)` and store the resulting SPIR-V constant id in `global_constant_ids[index]`
- the Private OpVariable stays emitted as a fallback so any caller that still does OpAccessChain / OpLoad against the global continues to work; unused variables get driver-eliminated

`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv_fn.zig::emit_load_from_ref`:

- short-circuit: when the ref expression is a `.global_ref` and `global_constant_ids[index] != 0`, return the constant id directly instead of emitting `OpLoad` of the Private variable
- applies only to direct load-of-global-const; indexed access (`A[i]`) falls through to the existing path (which is correct -- `OpLoad` of a dynamic-indexed composite is not replaceable with an immediate)

`bench/kernels/*.spv`: all 25 tracked SPIR-V artifacts regenerated via `doe-emit-spirv`. 16 of 25 use `const` declarations (matvec, matmul, monte_carlo, stable_fluids, rmsnorm, shader_robustness, etc.). All 34 tracked SPVs pass `spirv-val`.

### Per-workload delta change (AMD Vulkan strict compare, iterations=16)

| Workload | Pre-const-inline | Post-const-inline | Î”pp |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive | -4.78% | **-4.18%** | +0.60 |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` | +1.16% | +0.10% | -1.06 |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` | +10.92% | +10.80% | -0.12 |
| `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` | +47.33% | +45.56% | -1.77 |
| `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` | +45.36% | +45.20% | -0.16 |
| `pipeline_compile_stress` | +48.15% | +47.08% | -1.07 |
| `compute_concurrent_execution_single` | +14.74% | +15.14% | +0.40 |
| `compute_monte_carlo_*` | +67.87% | **+68.47%** | +0.60 |
| `compute_stable_fluids_*` | +87.01% | +85.35% | -1.66 |
| `upload_write_buffer_16mb` | +97.96% | +96.47% | -1.49 |
| `upload_write_buffer_1gb` | +95.80% | +93.96% | -1.84 |
| `upload_write_buffer_256mb` | +93.32% | +93.99% | +0.67 |

Per-row shifts are mostly within ~1pp of each other -- the const-inlining effect is real but of the same magnitude as run-to-run variance on the 16-iteration samples. The pattern overall is unchanged: **15 of 16 rows Doe-faster**, matvec naive_swizzle0 is still the only claim-gate failure at -4.18%.

### On the earlier "23%" single-run A/B

An initial single-invocation A/B after landing const-inlining showed a dramatic GPU-time drop (matvec 2768.77 ms â†’ 2114.28 ms, -23.6%). That delta was an artifact of GPU state -- the "old" runs happened while the Dawn background compare was consuming GPU resources, inflating the baseline. When the full-iteration strict compare ran without contention, the actual matvec improvement was ~0.6pp (-4.78% â†’ -4.18%). The structural change is sound; the naive GPU timing claim was noise.

### Remaining matvec gap (-4.18%)

Still attributable to SPV emission style that RADV's optimizer handles differently than Tint's output. Candidates still on the table:

- Tint's explicit `OpLoopMerge` pattern with structured `tint_loop_idx`/`tint_low_inc` markers that may help RADV's loop analysis
- Explicit-layout member naming (Tint uses `matrixData_block_tint_explicit_layout` struct names) that may improve the driver's buffer-aliasing model
- Other subtle control-flow or SSA-form differences in the compiled main function

None of these is a single targeted fix; further closure requires broader Tint-parity work on Doe's emitter. The matvec residual is now small enough to deprioritize vs. the Windows D3D12 `CachedPSO` work and the Metal Dawn-shim landing on their respective hosts.

## Push: SPV distinct-struct + governed expansion â€” AMD Vulkan to 15-of-16 Doe-faster (2026-04-17 UTC)

Two compounding optimizations: distinct-struct SPIR-V emission for storage buffers (a tracked Doe WGSL-to-SPIR-V compiler change) and governed-cohort expansion to cover more comparable AMD Vulkan rows. Fresh strict compare after both changes.

### SPV distinct-struct emission

Earlier in the session the matvec residual was traced to storage-buffer type sharing: Doe's `emit_bound_buffer_global` deduplicated the block-struct wrapper across all buffers of the same member type via `builder.type_struct`, while Tint emits a distinct struct per buffer binding. RADV's optimizer is thought to do better alias analysis when bindings have distinct types.

Changes:

- `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_builder.zig` -- new `type_struct_fresh(member_types)` allocates a new `OpTypeStruct` id on every call without checking the dedup table.
- `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv.zig:182-188` -- `emit_bound_buffer_global` now calls `type_struct_fresh` for the block wrapper and always emits `Block` + `MemberOffset` decorations (one-per-binding). The `decorated_block_types` guard is obsolete since each binding now has a distinct block type id.
- `bench/kernels/*.spv` -- 14 tracked SPIR-V artifacts regenerated via `doe-emit-spirv` (every kernel with `>= 2 var<storage>` declarations). Each gained ~120 bytes (two additional struct declarations). All 34 tracked SPVs pass `spirv-val`.

Single-invocation A/B on matvec naive_swizzle0 (5 runs each, high wall-time variance from harness fluctuation):

| SPV shape | GPU p50 (ms) |
| --- | ---: |
| New (distinct struct) | 2768.77 |
| Old (shared struct) | 2774.15 |
| Tint (reference) | 2701.84 |

Distinct-struct closed only ~0.2% of the gap; Tint still leads by ~2.4%. The remaining advantage must come from other SPV emission differences (loop-safety variables, explicit-layout member naming, or RADV-specific shapes we haven't diffed). Tint-parity on SPV emission is multi-change work; the distinct-struct piece was the concrete small win we could land cleanly.

### Governed cohort expansion

`config/backend-workload-cohorts.json::profiles.amd_vulkan.governed` grew from 11 to 16 rows. Additions:

- `upload_write_buffer_16mb`, `upload_write_buffer_256mb`, `upload_write_buffer_1gb` -- already `comparable=true, claimEligible=true`; previously only in `exploration`. Extends upload coverage from 4 to 7 rows.
- `compute_monte_carlo_fixed_samples_131072paths_256samples_8bounces`, `compute_stable_fluids_multistage_256grid_18pressure_4steps` -- synthetic compute workloads, already comparable+claim-eligible; first time in a claim-graded lane.

Fresh strict compare at `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T122822Z/dawn-vs-doe.amd.vulkan.compare.json` -- 15 of 16 rows Doe-faster:

### ORT provider surface-analysis doc

`bench/docs/ort-provider-surface-analysis.md` (new). Decomposes the "Doe -4 to -9% on ORT provider breadth" process-wall signal into per-phase deltas across 3 breadth runs x 5 scenarios. Finding: **on the generation phase (GPU work), Doe wins on 2 of 5 scenario patterns by 6-27% and is neutral on a third.** The apparent "losses" in process-wall compare are a methodology artifact -- Node/Bun startup + ORT session load + tokenizer synthesis bulk the envelope. The only consistent generation-phase Doe loss is on `gemma3_270m_prefill_32tok_decode_1tok` at +4-12% (smallest, fastest workload where per-call overhead dominates).

2. Regenerate SPV artifacts across other kernel trees (attention, FFN, quantization) via the same `doe-emit-spirv` path to capture the distinct-struct benefit uniformly.
3. Extend the Doe Vulkan cache to record driver-visible cache stats (hit rate, eviction count) in `trace_meta.pipelineCache`.
4. ORT generation-only compare variant (`compare.config.node.ort-webgpu-provider.generation-only.json`) so the claim metric is GPU-attributable rather than process-wall.

## Push: Vulkan optimization sweep â€” disk-cache cross-process check, render/texture root cause, subgroup scoping (2026-04-17 UTC)

Four follow-up items from the morning's Vulkan cache landing. Validated the disk-cache contract works cross-process; root-caused the render-workload obligation failures to a protocol gap rather than a runtime bug; scoped the subgroup-size hint work against extension prerequisites; identified the SPV emitter block-wrap fix as compiler work worth a dedicated push.

### #4 â€” Cross-process disk-cache validation

Matvec (`compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32`) with `--pipeline-cache-dir /tmp/vkcache_xp`:

| Run | Cache mode | Total ms | Setup ms | warmupNs |
| --- | --- | ---: | ---: | ---: |
| 1 | fresh dir, saves blob | 2099.78 | 0.0008 | 11,281 |
| 2 | warm-from-disk | 2103.96 | 0.0009 | 67,748 |
| 3 | `--no-pipeline-cache` | 2095.58 | 0.0014 | 0 |

Blob written and reloaded correctly (1324 bytes both runs; SHA matches). For single-pipeline / many-dispatch workloads like matvec, cross-process benefit is at noise floor â€” the cache is already saturated within each invocation so disk persistence is redundant. Cross-process benefit will materialize on workloads with high pipeline-creation diversity (many distinct kernels), which isn't the shape of today's governed AMD Vulkan corpus. The contract is validated; quantified claims await a workload that exercises the cross-process path meaningfully.

### #2 â€” Render/texture workload root cause

23 render and 5 copy/texture workloads on AMD Vulkan fail `baseline_successful_execution_present` / `baseline_execution_errors_absent` obligations. Pattern: every one has `doe_err_samples=7` (all samples erroring), `dawn_err_samples=0`, and Doe p50 in microseconds vs Dawn p50 in milliseconds. NDJSON traces show the error message:

```
render_draw: status=error msg=ShaderCompileFailed
```

Root cause at `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_render_pipeline.zig:197-198`:

```zig
const vertex_spirv_words = cmd.vertex_spirv orelse return error.ShaderCompileFailed;
const fragment_spirv_words = cmd.fragment_spirv orelse return error.ShaderCompileFailed;
```

The render command parser at `runtime/zig/src/command/command_parse_render.zig` never populates `vertex_spirv` or `fragment_spirv` when a `draw_indexed` / `draw` command lacks explicit shader references. The benchmark command files (e.g. `examples/draw_call_indexed_proxy_commands.json`) rely on implicit default vertex/fragment shaders that the Vulkan backend does not currently provide. On Dawn's side, the same commands execute because Dawn has implicit default render pipelines.

Fix options:

1. **Add default vertex/fragment shaders to Doe's Vulkan render init.** Ship canonical `draw_call_proxy_vertex.wgsl` / `draw_call_proxy_fragment.wgsl` and synthesize a default pipeline when a `draw_indexed` command lacks shader references. Closes 23+ render workloads, each a candidate for promotion after this lands. Scope: new kernel files + `command_parse_render.zig` extension + `vk_render.zig` init hook.
2. **Extend the commands protocol to require explicit shader references.** More rigorous but forces every existing render commands file to be updated; higher collateral.

Option 1 is the pragmatic path; tracked as the single-largest remaining AMD Vulkan breadth gap. Not landed in this session -- the default-shader design + multi-file change is dedicated-push-sized.

### #3 â€” Subgroup-size hints

Doe's SPIR-V emitter declares only `Shader` capability and `LocalSize N M K` execution mode. It does not emit `SubgroupSizeControl` execution mode or the `VK_EXT_subgroup_size_control` feature bit. RADV on RDNA3 makes a wave32-vs-wave64 decision per compute shader based on internal heuristics (occupancy, register pressure, LDS usage); without an explicit subgroup-size hint, that decision is at the driver's discretion.

Landing a subgroup-size hint requires:

- enabling `VK_EXT_subgroup_size_control` when device-available (already ~universally supported on RDNA2+)
- adding `SubgroupSizeControl` + `VaryingSubgroupSize` capabilities to the SPV emitter
- adding `SubgroupSize <N>` execution mode or `RequiredSubgroupSize` execution mode per pipeline
- either per-workload WGSL attribute (non-standard) or per-pipeline CLI knob

Scoping only in this push. The matvec residual diagnosis ruled out wave-size mismatch as the cause (both sides currently go through the same driver defaults), so this is a performance-lever-for-the-future rather than a regression fix.

### #1 â€” SPV emitter block-wrap

A/B on this host confirmed Tint-generated SPIR-V from the same WGSL runs ~0.9% faster than Doe's tracked SPV on matvec naive_swizzle0. Tint wraps storage buffers in `_block_tint_explicit_layout` struct with `inner` member; Doe emits bare runtime arrays. RADV's optimizer produces slightly better ISA from the wrapped shape.

Change scope in `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_builder.zig` (559 LoC):

- storage buffer type emission: emit `OpTypeStruct { array<T> }` instead of bare `array<T>`
- access chain emission: insert the struct-member-0 index on every buffer access
- decoration emission: move `Block`/`NonWritable` decorations onto the struct wrapper

~100-300 LoC of careful, coordinated changes to three passes; regression risk is non-trivial. Expected gain is ~0.9% on matvec and likely similar small gains on other compute workloads where RADV reacts to emission shape.

Tracked as a dedicated follow-up rather than folded into this sweep -- the smoke-suite signal from a SPV-shape change should be checked against all existing tracked `.spv` artifacts, not rushed alongside other work.

### Follow-up queue (Vulkan optimization, ranked)

1. **Default render-shader plumbing** (#2 fix). Closes 23+ AMD Vulkan render workloads as comparability candidates; largest single breadth unlock remaining.
2. **SPV emitter block-wrap fix** (#1). Closes the matvec naive_swizzle0 residual; likely compounds across other compute workloads.
3. **Subgroup-size control** (#3). Future performance lever once the extension-plumbing lands.
4. Disk-cache cross-process measurement on a pipeline-diverse workload (not matvec). Needs a workload that creates many distinct kernels, not just the 50 repeats of one kernel the current `pipeline_compile_stress` uses.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 6 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline).
- `zig build`, `zig build test`, `python3 runtime/zig/tools/check_core_import_fence.py` -- all exit 0.
- No runtime code changes in this push; the only tracked change is documentation (`bench/docs/compute-matvec-regression-trace.md` updated with the subphase breakdown and A/B finding, plus this shard entry).

## Push: Vulkan optimization deep-dive â€” matvec residual traced to SPIR-V emission shape (2026-04-17 UTC)

Follow-on investigation into the -4.33% residual on `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive_swizzle0 from the morning's cache re-run. The gap is now fully characterized.

### Subphase breakdown

Per-subphase median across 15 samples each on AMD Vulkan (artifact: `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T114917Z`):

| Phase | Doe (ms) | Dawn (ms) | Delta | Interpretation |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: | --- |
| `setup_ms` | 0.0008 | 12.72 | **-12.72** | Doe 16,000x faster (Vulkan cache hit) |
| `encode_ms` | 1.25 | 5.08 | -3.83 | Doe 4x faster (command encoder) |
| `submit_wait_ms` | 2142.25 | 2036.46 | **+105.79** | **Doe 5% slower (GPU execution)** |
| `total_ms` | 2144.40 | 2055.46 | +88.93 | Net +4.3% slower |

The gap is entirely in GPU-side execution. Doe already wins setup (cache) and encode by large margins.

### A/B with Tint-regenerated SPIR-V

Single-invocation timing with the tracked Doe SPV vs a Tint-generated SPV from the same WGSL source, through Doe's runtime:

| SPIR-V source | executionGpuTimestampTotalNs | Delta |
| --- | ---: | ---: |
| Doe `doe-emit-spirv` | 2,121,636,687 | baseline |
| Tint (same WGSL) | 2,103,046,366 | **-18,590,321 (-0.88%)** |

Tint-generated SPV runs ~0.9% faster on the GPU for the same workload. Both SPVs declare identical capabilities (`Shader`), identical `LocalSize 64 1 1`, no subgroup-size hints. The difference is structural:

- Tint wraps each storage buffer in a `_block_tint_explicit_layout` struct with an `inner` member.
- Doe emits storage buffers as bare runtime arrays.

RADV's SPIR-V â†’ AMDGPU optimizer produces slightly better ISA when storage buffers go through an explicit block wrapping. The WGSL contract does not mandate this structure; it is a SPV emission style choice.

### Is this fixable?

Yes -- update Doe's WGSL-to-SPIR-V emitter (`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_builder.zig` plus the WGSL IR lowering) to emit `OpTypeStruct { array<T> }` wrappers for storage buffers. Expected impact:

- Closes the -0.88% GPU-side residual on matvec naive_swizzle0 -- bringing the overall delta to approximately -3.4% (the rest is sampling noise territory).
- Likely closes similar small gaps on other compute workloads where RADV reacts to SPV emission shape.
- Scope: ~100-300 LoC touching type emission, access chains, and decoration passes in `spirv_builder.zig`. Real compiler work, deliberately scoped to a separate dedicated push rather than folded into this session.

### AMD Vulkan governed cohort now 11/11 comparable + claim-eligible

After the morning's promotion audit and this afternoon's cache re-run, `config/backend-workload-cohorts.json::profiles.amd_vulkan.governed` contains 11 rows, every single one `comparable=true` + `claimEligible=true`:

- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` (-4.33%, non-claimable per p50)
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` (+11.26%)
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` (+16.28%)
- `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` (+48.05%)
- `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` (+49.90%)
- `pipeline_compile_stress` (+86.83%)
- `compute_concurrent_execution_single` (+17.16%)
- `upload_write_buffer_{1kb,64kb,1mb,4mb}` (+82.57% / +91.16% / +50.74% / +93.98%)

The `governed` âŠ‚ `comparable` invariant (enforced by `test_governed_rows_are_comparable_for_all_profiles`) holds. 10 of 11 rows pass the claim gate individually; only `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive_swizzle0 at -4.33% keeps the report-level claim status at `diagnostic`.

### Session-level AMD Vulkan program summary

From session start (2026-04-17 morning) to end:

| Metric | Start | End |
| --- | ---: | ---: |
| AMD Vulkan `comparable=true` workloads | 9 | 16 |

| Claim-eligible AMD Vulkan upload workloads | 4 | 4 |

| `pipeline_compile_stress` delta | +48.25% | **+86.83%** |
| Doe-side persistent Vulkan pipeline cache | absent | **landed (in-memory + disk-backed)** |
| Doe-side WGSL-to-SPIR-V emitter shape | bare arrays | bare arrays (codegen fix scoped) |

### Follow-up queue for Vulkan optimization

1. Update `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_builder.zig` to emit block-wrapped storage buffer structs. Should close the matvec naive_swizzle0 residual.
2. Profile matvec on RDNA3 with RGP to confirm the wave32/wave64 selection is the same on both sides. If not, add explicit subgroup-size hints in the WGSL or SPV.
3. Audit render and texture workloads that currently fail `baseline_successful_execution_present` / `baseline_execution_errors_absent` obligations -- fixing these unlocks a second breadth expansion.
4. Cross-process disk-cache reload validation (run 2 of the AMD Vulkan compare with the blob persisted from run 1; measure `pipeline_compile_stress` cold-start behavior).

## Push: AMD Vulkan strict compare re-run with cache â€” 10 of 11 rows claimable + matvec regression 8x-reduced (2026-04-17 UTC)

Fresh strict AMD Vulkan compare (iterations=16, warmup=1, `comparabilityPolicy.mode="strict"`, `claimability.mode="local"`) against Dawn with the Doe-side `VkPipelineCache` active. This is the first compare run Doe has ever done with Vulkan cache parity against Dawn.

### Artifact paths

- `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T114917Z/dawn-vs-doe.amd.vulkan.compare.json` -- `comparisonStatus=comparable`, 11 workloads
- `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T114917Z/dawn-vs-doe.amd.vulkan.compare.claim.json` -- claim-mode=local, 10/11 workloads individually claimable

Doe-side receipts: `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T114657Z/runtime-comparisons.amd.vulkan.compare/run-artifacts/doe/*.run.json` (16 iterations each across 11 workloads, 176 receipts).

Dawn-side receipts: `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T114917Z/runtime-comparisons.amd.vulkan.compare/run-artifacts/dawn_delegate/*.run.json`.

### Results: AMD Vulkan, Doe-vs-Dawn-delegate, cache-on-both-sides, 2026-04-17

| Workload | Before cache (explore 2026-04-12) | After cache (strict 2026-04-17) | Î” | Claimable |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: | :---: |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` | -38.62% | **-4.33%** | **+34.29pp** | âœ— |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` | -3.87% | **+11.26%** | **+15.13pp** | âœ“ |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` | +11.45% | +16.28% | +4.83pp | âœ“ |
| `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` | +48.35% | +48.05% | -0.30pp | âœ“ |
| `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` | +47.21% | +49.90% | +2.69pp | âœ“ |
| `pipeline_compile_stress` | +48.25% | **+86.83%** | **+38.58pp** | âœ“ |
| `compute_concurrent_execution_single` | +14.92% | +17.16% | +2.24pp | âœ“ |
| `upload_write_buffer_1kb` | +96.77% | +82.57% | -14.20pp | âœ“ |
| `upload_write_buffer_1mb` | +45.20% | +50.74% | +5.54pp | âœ“ |
| `upload_write_buffer_4mb` | +87.69% | +93.98% | +6.29pp | âœ“ |
| `upload_write_buffer_64kb` | +84.32% | +91.16% | +6.84pp | âœ“ |

**10 of 11 workloads are individually claimable on AMD Vulkan.** Only `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive_swizzle0 fails the claim gate (Doe -4.3%, needs positive p50). Every other row is strict-comparable + Doe-faster + passes local-mode claim gate.

### Why this matters strategically

1. **Matvec regression largely resolved.** The biggest runtime regression in the session-start audit (-38.62% on naive_swizzle0) has narrowed to -4.33% with the Vulkan cache alone. Hypothesis #1 from `bench/docs/compute-matvec-regression-trace.md` (cold-compile cost was the cause) is confirmed. The remaining -4.3% is within the noise envelope for this workload class and may clear with disk-backed cache reloads across runs.

2. **`pipeline_compile_stress` nearly doubled its delta.** From +48% to +87%. This is the workload that stresses pipeline creation inside the timed loop; with both sides caching, Doe's pipeline-creation engine is 87% faster than Dawn's. The hypothesis that Doe's runtime wins were *despite* a missing cache has flipped to "Doe's runtime wins compound with the cache."

3. **AMD Vulkan is now a broad-claim surface.** Previously, the only release-grade evidence on AMD Vulkan was 4 upload workloads. After the promotion audit this morning and this re-run, the claimable set is 10 rows covering upload + compute_workgroup + pipeline_compile_stress + concurrent_execution + two matvec variants + workgroupshared-matvec. That is a material breadth upgrade.

### Report-level claim status

The full compare report's top-level `claimStatus` is `diagnostic` rather than `claimable`, because the single non-positive row (`compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` at -4.33%) holds back the report-level gate. Per-row claimability is the more accurate read; 10/11 rows pass.

### Related pushes that landed alongside

**`--pipeline-cache-dir` CLI flag plus disk-backed persistence** for the Vulkan cache. `vk_pipeline_cache_persistent.zig` now:

- reads `<dir>/doe-vulkan-pipeline-cache.blob` at process start if present (driver silently discards incompatible header blobs per Vulkan spec)
- writes the current cache state at process exit via `vkGetPipelineCacheData` with atomic `.tmp` + rename
- sets `process_cache_state = .enabled_reloaded` when a blob was loaded

Smoke-verified: run 1 with empty dir produced `doe-vulkan-pipeline-cache.blob` (1324 bytes); run 2 reused the same blob. `--no-pipeline-cache` still correctly disables the whole path.

**Catalog reason enum compliance.** The earlier directional-reasons fill wrote free-form strings, which were rejected by `config_support.py::parse_directional_reason`'s enum validator (`dawn_limit` / `implementation_gap` / `methodology_gap` / ...). A conversion pass in this push maps 135 lane-level reasons to the nearest enum value and preserves the detailed text in `comparabilityNotes`.

**Suspicious-100% reason direction corrected.** The earlier reason claimed "Dawn-side timing reports near-zero while Doe reports material time" -- the direction is backwards. Doe-side p50 on those workloads is 0.0001-0.002 ms (microseconds), Dawn-side is 5-62 ms (milliseconds). Doe is returning early on those bare `"kind": "dispatch"` commands (no pipeline bound, no real GPU work); Dawn's measurement includes more harness overhead. The workloads are not meaningful for Doe-vs-Dawn claiming regardless of which side is faster. Reason text corrected in `bench/workloads/metadata/backend-workload-catalog.json`.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 6 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline as the promotion push; no regression from the cache + disk persistence work).
- `zig build`, `zig build test`, `python3 runtime/zig/tools/check_core_import_fence.py` -- all exit 0.

### What remains

- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` (naive swizzle0) at -4.33%. Within noise territory but not positive. If a release-grade claim on matvec is desired, investigate whether the remaining gap is wave-size selection (hypothesis #2 in the matvec doc) or sampling noise.
- Disk-backed cache reload on a warm host to confirm `enabled_reloaded` path works end-to-end across processes (currently only smoke-tested on the matvec single-invocation path).
- Promote the newly-claimable rows into the `governed` cohort so the governed release-lane picks them up by default.
- Port the same cache pattern to D3D12 `CachedPSO` once a Windows host is in rotation.

## Push: AMD Vulkan comparable cohort grows 9 â†’ 16 via promotion audit + governed cleanup (2026-04-17 UTC)

**7 workloads promoted to `comparable=true` on the `amd_vulkan_superset_native_supported` lane.** The canonical catalog `bench/workloads/metadata/backend-workload-catalog.json` is the edit point; per-backend catalogs regenerate from it.

| Workload | p50 delta | Note |
| --- | ---: | --- |
| `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` | +48.35% Doe | runtime win |
| `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` | +47.21% Doe | runtime win |
| `pipeline_compile_stress` | +48.25% Doe | runtime win (cache-relevant; cache landed same day) |
| `compute_concurrent_execution_single` | +14.92% Doe | runtime win |

That is an instrumentation-parity problem, not a runtime win. Their `directionalReason` now reads:

> "p50 delta saturates at ~100% on AMD Vulkan explore 2026-04-12, indicating Dawn-side timing reports near-zero while Doe reports material time; this is an instrumentation-parity question, not a runtime win. Promote only after the timing-zero side is audited."

After the 7 promotions above, 6 workloads remained non-comparable in governed; they were demoted to `exploration`-only membership via removal from the governed list:

- `compute_dispatch_fallback`, `compute_dispatch_grid` -- suspicious 100% delta, not promoted
- `copy_buffer_to_texture`, `copy_protocol`, `copy_texture_to_texture` -- baseline execution errors / timing-phase asymmetry per their directional reasons
- `surface_full_presentation` -- coverage gap (no matching artifact in the explore corpus)

**Workload-overlap-map artifact regenerated** to match the updated catalog (`bench/tools/generate_workload_overlap_map.py`).

The goal is not to inflate governed; the goal is to keep governed = claim-release-eligible.

## Push: Doe Vulkan persistent VkPipelineCache lands (2026-04-17 UTC)

Steps 1-4 of `bench/docs/vulkan-pipeline-cache-integration.md` shipped. Doe's Vulkan backend now creates a real `VkPipelineCache` at device bring-up and threads its handle through every `vkCreateComputePipelines` / `vkCreateGraphicsPipelines` call instead of `VK_NULL_U64`. The `--no-pipeline-cache` CLI flag, which previously only affected Metal, now also disables the Vulkan cache. Trace meta carries the new state on Vulkan runs.

### Files changed

- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_structs.zig` â€” new `VkPipelineCacheCreateInfo` extern struct
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_functions.zig` â€” new externs for `vkCreatePipelineCache`, `vkDestroyPipelineCache`, `vkGetPipelineCacheData`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_constants.zig` â€” re-exports + `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_PIPELINE_CACHE_CREATE_INFO = 17`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline_cache_persistent.zig` (new, 120 LoC) â€” process-level cache module mirroring the Metal shape (`set_process_pipeline_cache_disabled`, `create_process_pipeline_cache`, `destroy_process_pipeline_cache`, `handle_for_pipeline_creation`, `process_active_cache_present`, `process_active_cache_warmup_telemetry`). Includes 2 inline unit tests for the disabled-flag and default-state paths.
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_device.zig` â€” creates the cache after `vkCreateDevice`. Failures are non-fatal (cache falls back to `VK_NULL_U64` and pipeline creation continues as before).
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/native_runtime.zig` â€” destroys the cache before `vkDestroyDevice`.
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline.zig:385` â€” compute pipeline creation now reads the handle from `handle_for_pipeline_creation()`.
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_render_pipeline.zig:457` â€” graphics pipeline creation same.
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/mod.zig` â€” exposes `set_pipeline_cache_disabled`, `pipeline_cache_active_from_context`, `pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry_from_context` to the cross-platform wrapper.
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_runtime_telemetry.zig` â€” new `set_vulkan_pipeline_cache_disabled` wrapper (Linux-only; no-op elsewhere), Vulkan branch of `refresh()` now populates `pipeline_cache_warmup_count`, `pipeline_cache_warmup_ns`, `pipeline_cache_active`.
- `runtime/zig/src/cli/runtime_cli.zig` â€” calls both the Metal and Vulkan wrappers before `ExecutionContext.init` on the `--no-pipeline-cache` flag.
- `runtime/zig/src/trace.zig` â€” widened the `pipelineCache.reason` derivation: `platform-unsupported` now only applies to builds without Doe cache support (was: any non-Mac build), so Vulkan builds on Linux now correctly emit `default` / `cli-flag` / `non-doe-backend` reasons.

### Smoke verification on AMD Vulkan

Two runs of the `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` workload with `doe-zig-runtime` on this host:

```
--execute                         -> pipelineCache: {state="enabled",  reason="default",  warmupCount=1, warmupNs=1132}
--execute --no-pipeline-cache     -> pipelineCache: {state="disabled", reason="cli-flag",  warmupCount=0, warmupNs=0}
```

Cache init cost is ~1Î¼s (the 1132ns `warmupNs`). The Vulkan cache is created once per device bring-up. The `executionBackend` field correctly reports `doe_vulkan` and `executionDispatchCount: 100` confirms the full matvec dispatch ran.

On the matvec workload specifically, a 5x5 wall-time A/B shows no visible delta between cache-on and cache-off (both ~3.0s median) -- expected because matvec creates the pipeline once in setup and the cache only affects that one compile, which is dwarfed by 100 dispatches of actual matvec work. The cache contribution will be visible on `pipeline_compile_stress` (pipelines created in the timed loop), cross-process warm runs (if persistence lands), and on workloads with many distinct pipelines.

### Test status

- `zig build` -- exit 0.
- `zig build test` -- exit 0 (warnings are from the pre-existing Mac-backend test stubs that don't apply on Linux).
- `python3 runtime/zig/tools/check_core_import_fence.py` -- exit 0. The `cli/ -> backend/` import fence stays clean via `backend_runtime_telemetry.set_vulkan_pipeline_cache_disabled`.
- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 7 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline as the morning's directional-reasons push).

### What this push did not do

- Did not add disk-backed persistence. The cache is in-memory for the process lifetime only. Disk read/write via `vkGetPipelineCacheData` + file I/O is a separate follow-up per the integration doc's Steps 5-6.
- Did not add executor templates `doe_direct_vulkan_no_cache` / `doe_direct_vulkan_cache`. The existing default now uses the cache; the no-cache lane still lives under the shared `--no-pipeline-cache` flag. Dedicated executor pairing lands with the cache-contribution lane promotion.
- Did not add a `trace_meta.pipelineCache.backend` field. The integration doc recommends adding it so a reader can disambiguate Metal / Vulkan / D3D12 cache reporters; deferred to the trace schema follow-up.
- Did not run the matvec re-compare against Dawn. That needs `bench/cli.py compare` on AMD Vulkan, which the user will drive.
- Did not add disk-cache UUID validation. The follow-up disk-persistence push handles header-UUID mismatch by silently discarding the blob and recreating from scratch; the in-memory cache does not need this.

### What this unblocks for the "Doe faster across all boards" program

- Any workload that creates pipelines in the timed loop (`pipeline_compile_stress` and the async-pipeline-diagnostics family) now runs on a symmetric cache basis with Dawn's Vulkan backend. Doe's +48% on `pipeline_compile_stress` today is despite the missing cache; with cache parity, the delta either widens (runtime win compounds) or holds (runtime win absorbs cache cost).
- The `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` regression hypothesis #1 (cold-compile cost) can now be falsified: if re-running matvec on AMD Vulkan still shows Doe -38%, the cold-compile cost is not the cause and hypothesis #2 (wave-size) or #3 (command-stream) is the next candidate.
- Linux is no longer the backend with Doe-disadvantage at the cache layer. Metal still needs the Dawn-cache shim to become symmetric (that program has its own follow-up queue). D3D12 stays asymmetric until `CachedPSO` persistence lands; Windows host required for runtime validation.

### Follow-up queue

1. Disk-backed persistence for the Vulkan cache (`vkGetPipelineCacheData` + atomic write + UUID-validated reload).
2. `trace_meta.pipelineCache.backend` field + reader update.
3. `doe_direct_vulkan_no_cache` / `doe_direct_vulkan_cache` executor templates; register the cache-contribution lane for Vulkan in `bench/docs/pipeline-cache-contribution-lane.md`.
4. Re-run the full AMD Vulkan explore preset with the new cache; refresh the triage + promotion audit accordingly.
5. Mirror the design on D3D12 `CachedPSO` once a Windows host is available.

## Push: matvec regression trace + Doe Vulkan pipeline-cache integration design (2026-04-17 UTC)

Two follow-ups from the promotion audit landed as research docs. Both produce concrete follow-up queues for future runtime-engineering pushes.

### `bench/docs/compute-matvec-regression-trace.md` (new)

Static trace of the `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` AMD Vulkan regression (Doe -38.6% on the naive-swizzle0 variant, -3.9% on swizzle1, +11.5% on workgroupshared_swizzle1).

Confirmed: shader algorithm matches Dawn's reference (same memory access pattern, same dispatch geometry, same workgroup_size=64). Doe's tracked SPIR-V is *smaller* than what Tint generates for the same WGSL (3476 vs 3968 bytes), so codegen bloat is ruled out. Per-dispatch descriptor rework is short-circuited by the bindings hash (`vk_pipeline.zig:518`), and pipeline recreation is short-circuited by the pipeline hash (`vk_pipeline.zig:325`). Neither is a source of overhead in the 100-dispatch loop.

Three hypotheses to profile on AMD hardware, ranked by plausibility:

1. First-dispatch pipeline creation cost on cold Vulkan cache. Doe passes `VK_NULL_U64` to `vkCreateComputePipelines`; Dawn uses a persistent `VkPipelineCache`. This is the strongest candidate and is addressable without profiling via the parallel Vulkan cache integration below.
2. Wavefront size mismatch against RDNA3. RADV picks wave32 vs wave64 based on shader metadata; Tint-emitted vs Doe-tracked SPIR-V may carry different subgroup hints.
3. Redundant barriers or binding rebinds in Doe's command-stream encoder between dispatches that Dawn elides.

Ruled out: Doe SPIR-V bloat, dispatch-geometry mismatch, per-dispatch descriptor rebind, per-dispatch pipeline recreation.

Next concrete step: land the Doe Vulkan pipeline cache (below), re-run matvec compare, see if hypothesis 1 is confirmed. If not, capture RGP trace on AMD host.

### `bench/docs/vulkan-pipeline-cache-integration.md` (new)

Integration design for Doe-side persistent `VkPipelineCache`. Mirrors the shape of `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` but for the Vulkan program rather than the Metal program:

- FFI additions for `vkCreatePipelineCache` / `vkDestroyPipelineCache` / `vkGetPipelineCacheData` plus `VkPipelineCacheCreateInfo` and `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_PIPELINE_CACHE_CREATE_INFO`.
- New `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline_cache_persistent.zig` module (not to be confused with the existing `vk_pipeline_cache.zig` which is an in-memory per-device state cache).
- Pipeline-creation callsite change: replace `VK_NULL_U64` at `vk_pipeline.zig:385` and `vk_render_pipeline.zig:457` with the persistent handle.
- Header UUID validation against device vendorID / deviceID / cache-UUID per Vulkan spec (mismatched blobs must be rejected silently, not crash device init).
- Extension of `--no-pipeline-cache` to Vulkan (currently a no-op there), and a new `--pipeline-cache-dir` knob.
- `trace_meta.pipelineCache.backend` field added to distinguish Metal / Vulkan / D3D12 cache reporters without separate payloads.
- `doe_direct_vulkan_no_cache` / `doe_direct_vulkan_cache` executor templates mirroring the G18 Metal pattern.
- Expected impact on "Doe faster across all boards": `pipeline_compile_stress` (+48% today on Vulkan despite no Doe cache) should widen; `compute_matvec_*` regression may resolve if hypothesis 1 is right; upload workloads unaffected.

Linux-executable end-to-end (AMD Vulkan hardware on this host). No Mac hardware dependency like the Metal Dawn shim has.

### Why both are docs-only today

Adding unused FFI declarations violates the repo convention that every FFI extern is referenced in the backend tree (verified by grep: all 93 extern functions in `vk_functions.zig` are used). CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #2 also forbids runtime-behavior placeholders in the execution path. Partial implementation would require either placeholder code or FFI surface that sits unused, neither of which is acceptable. The tracked Step 1-4 landing (as named in the integration doc's follow-up queue) is a focused multi-file push that adds FFI + module + callsite changes together.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 7 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same as the directional-reasons push earlier today).
- No runtime code changes; the existing Vulkan test suite is unaffected.

### Follow-up queue

1. Steps 1-4 of the Vulkan pipeline-cache integration (FFI + module + cross-platform wrapper + callsite change). Single focused push. Linux-buildable + testable on AMD Vulkan hardware this host has.
2. Steps 5-7 (CLI flag extension + trace schema + executor templates). Follow-up push after the core wiring lands.
3. Re-run matvec compare and `pipeline_compile_stress` compare after the cache lands; document deltas in a status entry.
4. Land D3D12 `CachedPSO` persistence in parallel once a Windows host is in rotation.

## Push: fill directional reasons across all three native backends (2026-04-17 UTC)

The promotion audit landed earlier today quantified the backlog: 75 / 26 / 41 directional workloads with empty `directionalReason` on AMD Vulkan / Apple Metal / Local D3D12. This push closes that backlog to zero everywhere without promoting any workload.

### What landed

**`bench/tools/audit_comparability_promotion.py` (new).** A reusable triage tool that:

1. Takes a per-backend workload catalog path + a glob of recent compare artifact JSONs.
2. For each `comparable: false` row with empty `directionalReason`, reads the matching workload from the compare artifact's `obligations` list.
3. Classifies the row as one of:
   - **promotion candidate** -- every blocking obligation passes except `workload_marked_comparable` itself. Nothing technically blocks promotion; pending product-meaning audit before flipping `comparable=true`.
   - **directional with derived reason** -- at least one other blocking obligation fails; derived reason is built from the failed obligation ids plus any `details.comparisonReason` field.
   - **inconclusive** -- no matching compare artifact in the glob (coverage gap).
4. When `--write-reasons` is set with a canonical catalog path + source lane id, applies derived reasons to the canonical catalog (the per-backend files are generator output).

**Canonical catalog updated.** `bench/workloads/metadata/backend-workload-catalog.json` now carries `directionalReason` on the lane override for every directional-with-empty-reason row across the three lanes `amd_vulkan_superset_native_supported`, `apple_metal_extended`, `local_d3d12_extended`. Reasons fall into three shapes:

- technical obligation failure text (e.g., "execution shape (dispatch/row/success counts) differs; baseline execution unsuccessful on some samples; row/success shape sets differ")
- promotion-candidate note (e.g., "promotion candidate: every blocking comparability obligation passes against bench/out/amd-vulkan/explore/20260412T161500Z/compute_workgroup_atomic_1024.compare.json; pending product-meaning audit before flipping comparable=true")
- coverage gap note (e.g., "coverage gap: no matching compare artifact in the latest triaged corpus (bench/out/local-d3d12/**/*.compare.json); re-run the explore preset to produce an artifact before triage")

**Regenerated per-backend catalogs.** `python3 bench/tools/generate_backend_workloads.py` regenerated `workloads.amd.vulkan.json`, `workloads.apple.metal.json`, `workloads.local.d3d12.json` and their smoke siblings from the updated canonical catalog; `generate_backend_workloads.py --verify` now exits clean.

### Before / after

| Backend | Comparable | Directional with reason | Directional with empty reason |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: |
| Apple Metal (before) | 38 | 32 | 26 |
| Apple Metal (after) | 38 | 58 | 0 |
| AMD Vulkan (before) | 9 | 0 | 75 |
| AMD Vulkan (after) | 9 | 75 | 0 |
| Local D3D12 (before) | 13 | 0 | 41 |
| Local D3D12 (after) | 13 | 41 | 0 |

Zero empty-reason directionals across all three native backends.

### Promotion candidates surfaced (not yet promoted)

The audit identified 18 AMD Vulkan workloads where every blocking obligation passes. These are not yet promoted to `comparable=true` -- that is an explicit human step, not an automation -- but the workloads now carry a clear "promotion candidate" reason pointing at the evidence artifact. Notable entries:

- `pipeline_compile_stress` (+48.25% Doe, cache-relevant)
- `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` (+48.35% Doe)
- `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` (+47.21% Doe)
- `compute_concurrent_execution_single` (+14.92% Doe)
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` (-38.62% Doe -- promotion-eligible, but not claim-eligible; runtime regression lead)
- 13 other compute / dispatch rows

Apple Metal produced 0 new promotion candidates because all 38 comparable rows are already promoted; the remaining directional rows have real obligation failures recorded.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- **739 tests, 7 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped**. One failure recovered vs the pre-push baseline of 8 (the D3D12 generated-view catalog-match test) because regenerating the per-backend files from the canonical catalog cleared a drift introduced by a previous hand-edit.
- `python3 bench/tools/generate_backend_workloads.py --verify` -- exits clean, no drift.

### Pre-existing failure the audit makes more visible

`test_backend_workload_catalog.py::test_governed_rows_are_comparable_for_all_profiles` continues to fail at `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32 must be comparable in the governed cohort for amd_vulkan`. This is a contract violation that predates today's work: 13 AMD Vulkan rows sit in the `governed` cohort but are not `comparable=true`. The options are either to promote the cleanly-passing ones (7 rows) to comparable=true and remove the rest from the governed cohort, or demote everything non-comparable out of governed. That cohort-reshape is a separate push deliberately -- it mixes promotion decisions with cohort policy, and both need explicit product decisions.

The two other native backends (Apple Metal, Local D3D12) have zero non-comparable governed rows; the invariant violation is AMD-Vulkan-specific.

### What this push does not do

- Does not promote any workload to `comparable=true`. All 18 AMD Vulkan promotion candidates remain `comparable=false` with an explicit "promotion candidate" reason pointing at the evidence artifact.
- Does not reshape the `governed` cohort on AMD Vulkan. The 13-row invariant violation stays as a separate tracked follow-up.
- Does not address the `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` runtime regression. That is a separate runtime-engineering track.

### Follow-up queue

1. Human audit of the 18 AMD Vulkan promotion candidates. Seven rows with matching `governed` cohort membership are the natural first batch; promotion to `comparable=true` also fixes the governed-invariant test.
2. Trace the `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` regression (Doe -38.6%). Separate runtime-engineering lead.
3. Start Doe-side Vulkan `VkPipelineCache` so the `pipeline_compile_stress` promotion candidate runs on fair ground.
