## Push: pipeline-cache contribution lane + comparability promotion audit (2026-04-17 UTC)

Two coordinated docs landed together. The pipeline-cache contribution lane documents the Doe-vs-Doe diagnostic (cache off vs cache on, same runtime, same hardware) as its own first-class taxonomy entry distinct from Doe-vs-Dawn fair-cold and fair-warm lanes. The comparability promotion audit quantifies where breadth is actually bottlenecked across the three native backends.

### A -- Pipeline-cache contribution lane

`bench/docs/pipeline-cache-contribution-lane.md` (new). Defines the Doe-vs-Doe lane: baseline Doe `--no-pipeline-cache` vs comparison Doe cache-active, same workload, same hardware. The lane is explicitly diagnostic-grade, not claim-grade, and is distinct from:

- Doe-vs-Dawn fair-cold (current Metal default; both sides cache-disabled) -- claim-eligible
- Doe-vs-Dawn fair-warm (future Metal, once Dawn shim lands; both sides cache-enabled) -- claim-eligible

Per-backend applicability: Apple Metal is available today via `doe_direct_metal` (cache off) + `doe_direct_metal_cache` (cache on) executor templates already in `bench/native_compare_modules/executor_registry.py`. AMD Vulkan and Local D3D12 lanes land when Doe-side caching lands on those backends.

The doc pins what the cache actually covers (driver-level IR->GPU-ISA compile plus PSO finalization) vs what it does not (WGSL parsing, Tint translation, runtime execution, descriptor-set updates), and names the workload-shape heuristic for where the delta lands (setup_ns for one-time-pipeline-creation workloads; main-phase timing for `pipeline_compile_stress` and similar).

### B -- Comparability promotion audit

`bench/docs/comparability-promotion-audit.md` (new). Cross-backend maturity snapshot pulled from the tracked workload catalogs on 2026-04-17:

| Backend | Total | `comparable=true` | `governed` cohort | Directional (no reason) | Directional (with reason) |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: | ---: | ---: |
| Apple Metal | 96 | 38 | 27 | 26 | 32 |
| AMD Vulkan | 84 | 9 | 17 | 75 | 0 |
| Local D3D12 | 54 | 13 | 11 | 41 | 0 |

Finding: "Doe faster than Dawn across all boards" is not bottlenecked by runtime quality on AMD Vulkan or D3D12. It is bottlenecked by a process gap -- the vast majority of directional workloads on those backends have no stated `directionalReason`, meaning no audit has decided whether they can be promoted to `comparable=true` or whether they are legitimately directional-only.

All 75 AMD Vulkan directional workloads and all 41 Local D3D12 directional workloads carry empty `directionalReason` fields. The existing `explore` corpus artifacts show both Doe and Dawn executing these workloads, so this is an audit-promotion backlog, not a runtime-execution issue.

First-pass promotion candidates on AMD Vulkan (heuristic match against `bench/out/amd-vulkan/explore/20260412T161500Z/` -- not pre-cleared, just starting points for the actual audit):

- `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` -- Doe +48.35%
- `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` -- Doe +47.21%
- `compute_concurrent_execution_single` -- Doe +14.92%
- `pipeline_compile_stress` -- Doe +48.25% (cache-relevant; would benefit most from Doe Vulkan caching landing)
- `render_bundle_dynamic_pipeline_bindings_200k` -- Doe +65.50%
- `render_draw_redundant_pipeline_bindings_200k` -- Doe +26.00%

Runtime-engineering lead (not a contract issue): `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` shows Doe -38.6% slower, `_swizzle1` shows -3.9% slower, `_workgroupshared_swizzle1` shows +11.5%. The matvec regression is in Doe's expected strong area (compute-heavy, cache-irrelevant) and deserves a dedicated trace.

Rough sizing of the promotion work: ~30-40 engineer-hours on AMD Vulkan, ~20-25 engineer-hours on Local D3D12 (gated on Windows host), ~10 engineer-hours to fill the 26 Apple Metal directional rows with stated reasons. Largest single-lever Linux-executable breadth work available today.

### Strategic framing

Before this audit, the implicit plan for "Doe faster than Dawn across all boards" was running to land the Metal Dawn-cache shim plus Doe Vulkan/D3D12 caching. Those are both real programs, but the Linux-executable breadth work ahead of them is the promotion audit -- most of the corpus on Vulkan and D3D12 is not in the comparable contract, and no runtime change will unlock it. Audit first, runtime-engineering second.

### Test status

- Docs-only push on the Python side; `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` remains at 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same pre-push baseline).
- No schema changes, no runtime changes, no test changes.

### Follow-up queue

1. Run the AMD Vulkan promotion audit on the listed first-pass candidates. Writes decisions into `bench/workloads/workloads.amd.vulkan.json` per row. Largest single strategic win.
2. Trace the `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` regression -- runtime-engineering follow-up, separate track from the audit.
3. Fill empty `directionalReason` on the 26 Apple Metal directional rows (contract-only cleanup).
4. Local D3D12 promotion audit once a Windows host is in rotation.

## Push: three-backend pipeline-cache audit â€” asymmetry reverses on Vulkan and D3D12 (2026-04-16 UTC)

Source-level audit of Doe's and Dawn's pipeline caching across Metal / Vulkan / D3D12 backends, motivated by scoping "Doe faster than Dawn across all boards". The audit changes the strategic framing: the fair-warm Dawn-cache shim work (Push 4 design) is Metal-only. On Vulkan and D3D12 the asymmetry reverses -- Dawn caches, Doe does not -- and the corrective work there is to give Doe a cache, not Dawn.

### What landed

**`bench/docs/pipeline-cache-backend-audit.md` (new).**

Per-backend findings:

- **Metal.** Doe opens `MTLBinaryArchive` at `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/metal_native_runtime.zig:380-402` when `HAS_PIPELINE_CACHE` (macOS 11+) and `--no-pipeline-cache` is not passed. Dawn delegate path does not. Fair-cold currently enforced on both sides; fair-warm requires the Push 4 shim.
- **Vulkan.** Doe passes `VK_NULL_U64` (VK_NULL_HANDLE) as the `pipelineCache` arg to every `vkCreateComputePipelines` / `vkCreateGraphicsPipelines` call (`runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline.zig:385`, `vk_render_pipeline.zig:457`). The misleadingly-named `vk_pipeline_cache.zig` is an in-memory descriptor-state cache, not a persistent VkPipelineCache. Dawn's Vulkan backend implements `PipelineCacheVk` (`bench/vendor/dawn/src/dawn/native/vulkan/PipelineCacheVk.{h,cpp}`) and uses it on the delegate path.
- **D3D12.** Doe's `d3d12_bridge.c:174-192` (compute) and `:820`/`:930` (graphics) pipeline creation paths zero-initialize the pipeline state descriptor and never populate `CachedPSO.pCachedBlob`. Dawn's D3D12 backend populates `CachedPSO.pCachedBlob` / `.CachedBlobSizeInBytes` in `ComputePipelineD3D12.cpp:103-104` and `RenderPipelineD3D12.cpp:449` when a cached blob is available.

Direction summary:

| Backend | Doe cache | Dawn cache |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Metal | `MTLBinaryArchive` (bench-manifest-specific) | none in Doe's delegate path |
| Vulkan | `VK_NULL_U64` -- no cache | `PipelineCacheVk` active |
| D3D12 | No `CachedPSO` set | `CachedPSO.pCachedBlob` populated when available |

### Strategic implications

"Doe faster than Dawn across all boards" is two independent programs, not one:

1. **Metal -- Dawn catches up.** The integration plan in `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` promotes Doe's existing Metal cache wins from diagnostic to claim-grade. Build machinery already proven buildable on Linux (see `bench/tools/regenerate_dawn_component_build.py`).
2. **Vulkan + D3D12 -- Doe catches up.** Implement persistent pipeline caching in Doe's Vulkan and D3D12 backends. Independent of the Metal shim and independent of Dawn.

The existing AMD Vulkan claimable evidence survives this audit. Every current AMD Vulkan Doe-vs-Dawn compare is running strictly cache-disadvantaged on the Doe side, so Doe wins observed today are runtime-engineering wins despite the cache gap. Adding Doe-side Vulkan / D3D12 caching can only remove a hidden disadvantage; it cannot invalidate existing wins.

### Why this is a finding, not a push

No runtime code changes in this push. The audit documents what is, not what should be. Implementation of Doe Vulkan `VkPipelineCache` and Doe D3D12 `CachedPSO` persistence are two separate follow-up pushes enumerated at the end of the audit doc. Both are Linux-executable on the Zig + bridge side (Vulkan has hardware locally; D3D12 needs a Windows host for runtime validation but Linux builds stay green).

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same pre-push baseline; docs-only push).
- The audit's source-line references were verified by direct `grep` / file inspection; no build or symbol check was required.

### Follow-up queue

1. Implement Doe Vulkan persistent `VkPipelineCache` with CLI flag + trace_meta schema slot parallel to Metal's.
2. Implement Doe D3D12 `CachedPSO` persistence with the same CLI + schema pattern.
3. Complete the Metal Dawn-cache shim (ongoing, has its own follow-up queue in `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md`).
4. Re-run AMD Vulkan + D3D12 compare lanes under the new caches to confirm Doe's wins remain or grow.

## Push: Dawn component-build durability â€” tracked regenerator script (2026-04-16 UTC)

Closes the "make the rebuild contract durable" item on the Dawn cache integration follow-up queue. The ComponentTest build directory is gitignored via `bench/vendor/` (so the `.so` artifacts stay ephemeral), but the build *contract* -- the `args.gn` contents, the target list, and the expected-symbol invariants -- now lives in a tracked Python tool under `bench/tools/`.

### What landed

**`bench/tools/regenerate_dawn_component_build.py` (new).**
- Writes the canonical `args.gn` into `bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/` (or the `--out-name` override) and runs `gn gen`.
- `--build` runs `ninja` for `src/dawn/platform:shared` and `src/dawn/native:shared`, producing `libdawn_platform.so` and `libdawn_native.so` with the C++ surface exposed.
- `--verify` checks the built `.so` files for a required-symbol whitelist: `dawn::platform::Platform::Platform()`, `~Platform()`, `GetCachingInterface()`, `dawn::platform::CachingInterface::CachingInterface()`, `~CachingInterface()`, `dawn::native::DawnInstanceDescriptor::DawnInstanceDescriptor()`, `dawn::native::Instance::SetPlatformForTesting(dawn::platform::Platform*)`. Missing symbols return exit code 2 with a per-symbol reason.
- `--summary-out` emits a JSON summary with `argsGnPath`, `buildDir`, `gnGenOk`, `builtTargets`, and `missingSymbols` for audit / CI use.
- The canonical `args.gn` contents live as a single `CANONICAL_ARGS_GN` constant in the script, so any future change to the build-config contract is a one-place edit.

**Default invocation semantics.**
- `python3 bench/tools/regenerate_dawn_component_build.py` â€” rewrite `args.gn`, run `gn gen`, exit 0 if successful. No compile work; safe to run at any time.
- `python3 bench/tools/regenerate_dawn_component_build.py --build --verify` â€” end-to-end rebuild + symbol verification. ~13 minutes on a warm libc++ cache, longer on a cold build.

### Why it is in `bench/tools/` rather than elsewhere

`bench/vendor/` is fully gitignored -- nothing inside it can be committed, so the build config cannot live as a vendored args file. `bench/tools/` is the canonical home for repo-only Python tooling (precedent: `bootstrap_dawn.py`, `cts_baseline_*.py`, `build_claim_rehearsal_artifacts.py`, etc.). That directory is tracked, follows `bench/STYLE.md`, and is invoked by other tooling without path gymnastics.

### What this does not do

- Does not run the rebuild automatically. The expensive build step (`--build`) stays opt-in; a CI hook that invokes it is a separate follow-up.
- Does not land the tracked Step 1 shim. `bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/dawn_cache_shim_skeleton.cpp` remains the compile-check skeleton only; the real shim lands with `dawn_cache.zig`, `--dawn-cache-dir`, and `TraceRunSummary.dawnPipelineCache` as a single change.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same pre-push baseline; the new script is tool code with no test dependencies introduced).
- `python3 bench/tools/regenerate_dawn_component_build.py --verify` against the already-built ComponentTest `.so` files -- exit 0, "symbol verify: all required symbols exported".

## Push: Dawn libdawn_native.so + shim skeleton â€” Step 1 proven buildable on Linux (2026-04-16 UTC)

Extension of the component-build push above. With `libdawn_platform.so` already proved, the full pair of shared libraries the shim needs plus a compile-check of the shim skeleton itself now exist on Linux.

### libdawn_native.so built

`ninja -C bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest src/dawn/native:shared` completed 1158/1158 steps (the libc++ rebuild from the prior push is cached, so the native delta was smaller than the fresh-build estimate) and produced:

```
bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/libdawn_native.so  (11,915,168 bytes)
```

`nm -D --defined-only | c++filt` confirms the full Step 1 surface:

- `dawn::native::DawnInstanceDescriptor::DawnInstanceDescriptor()` â€” the chained-descriptor constructor the shim needs
- `dawn::native::Instance::Instance(WGPUInstanceDescriptor const*)` and the `wgpu::InstanceDescriptor` / `InstanceBase*` overloads
- `dawn::native::Instance::SetPlatformForTesting(dawn::platform::Platform*)` â€” fallback platform-injection hook
- `dawn::native::InstanceProcessEvents(WGPUInstanceImpl*)` â€” event-pumping surface

### Shim proof-of-build

A compile-check skeleton at `bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/dawn_cache_shim_skeleton.cpp` (gitignored, local-only) was authored. It subclasses `dawn::platform::CachingInterface` and `dawn::platform::Platform`, exposes four `extern "C"` entry points (`doe_dawn_install_persistent_cache`, `doe_dawn_teardown_persistent_cache`, `doe_dawn_get_platform_ptr`, `doe_dawn_cache_entry_count`), and was verified by:

- compile against the Dawn headers plus the generated `gen/include/` tree (clang 23 bundled with Dawn, `-std=c++20 -fPIC -fvisibility=hidden`)
- link as a shared library against `libdawn_platform.so` â€” all four C ABI entry points export as `T`, all required `dawn::platform::*` references resolve through the `.so`
- `nm -D` inspection confirms the shim's ABI is exactly the four C functions and nothing else

Exact compile / link commands and the header-include quirk (the generated `gen/include/` path is required because `DawnPlatform.h` transitively pulls in `webgpu.h`) are documented in `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` under the new "Shim proof-of-build (2026-04-16)" section.

### Why the skeleton is not tracked in runtime/zig/

CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #2: "runtime behavior placeholders are not allowed in Zig execution paths; implement fully or fail with explicit unsupported taxonomy." The skeleton's `LoadData` / `StoreData` are no-ops. It lives under `bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/` (gitignored via the `bench/vendor/` wildcard) as a compile-check artifact, not as a tracked runtime component. The tracked Step 1 landing implements real file-backed persistence and wires the shim into `dawn_cache.zig` + `cli/runtime_cli.zig` in a single push; this push's role is to prove that push is buildable.

### What is now proven on Linux

1. Dawn can be rebuilt with exposed C++ visibility on this host (`is_component_build = true` + `use_custom_libcxx = true`).
2. Both `libdawn_platform.so` and `libdawn_native.so` export the full surface the integration plan needs.
3. A shim compiled against Dawn's headers links cleanly against those shared libraries.
4. The shim's C ABI is the only externally visible surface, which is what Doe's Zig FFI will call.

### Remaining Step 0 / Step 1 work

- durability: vendor the ComponentTest args.gn at a tracked path, or add a repo-only regenerator script, so the build contract does not rely on ad-hoc operator steps
- Step 1 proper: implement real file-backed `LoadData` / `StoreData`, wire `dawn_cache.zig` + `cli/runtime_cli.zig`, land the `--dawn-cache-dir` CLI flag with typed unsupported taxonomy for builds without the shim, and extend `TraceRunSummary` with `dawnPipelineCache.{state, reason, entryCount}`
- Mac verification: re-run the component build on `mac.lan` to confirm whether `use_custom_libcxx = true` is needed there (Apple toolchain default sysroots may already ship libc++ with `atomic::wait`)

## Push: Dawn component-build Linux proof-of-build â€” libdawn_platform.so links with exported C++ symbols (2026-04-16 UTC)

Extension of the earlier Dawn verification push. After confirming the default vendored `libwebgpu_dawn.so` hides all C++ symbols, a Linux rebuild under `bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/` proved the integration plan's Step 0 is achievable on this host.

### Build args and attempt sequence

First attempt (`use_custom_libcxx = false`, the conservative default) reached 254/258 steps before `src/dawn/platform/WorkerThread.cpp` failed to compile with `error: no member named 'wait' in 'std::atomic<bool>'`. Root cause: Dawn's bundled Debian bullseye sysroot at `bench/vendor/dawn/build/linux/debian_bullseye_amd64-sysroot/usr/include/c++/10/atomic` ships libstdc++ 10, which does not implement C++20 `atomic::wait` / `notify_all` (added in libstdc++ 11). Dawn's bundled clang 23 supports `-std=c++20` but uses the sysroot's stdlib.

Second attempt with the full args:

```
is_debug = false
is_component_build = true
dawn_complete_static_libs = false
use_custom_libcxx = true
dawn_use_swiftshader = false
angle_enable_swiftshader = false
```

completed 1451/1451 steps in ~13 minutes. The extra ~1200 steps are Chromium's in-tree libc++ / libc++abi rebuild, which implements `atomic::wait`.

### Build product and symbol verification

```
bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/libdawn_platform.so  (37,648 bytes)
```

`nm -D --defined-only | c++filt` confirms every C++ symbol the shim needs is exported as `T`:

- `dawn::platform::Platform::Platform()` and `~Platform()` â€” constructor / virtual destructor
- `dawn::platform::Platform::GetCachingInterface()` â€” the hook the shim will override
- `dawn::platform::CachingInterface::CachingInterface()` and `~CachingInterface()` â€” constructor / virtual destructor the shim will subclass
- all other `dawn::platform::Platform` member functions that the shim leaves default-implemented (`AddTraceEvent`, `MonotonicallyIncreasingTime`, `IsFeatureEnabled`, the Histogram* family, etc.)

This proves the integration plan's Step 0 is achievable on this Linux host. The ComponentTest directory is gitignored via the `bench/vendor/` wildcard, so this is a disposable proof-of-build artifact, not a tracked rebuild.

### What this changes about the integration plan

The Push 4 design doc's "Step 0" section now has empirical backing for Option A (rebuild Dawn with exposed C++ visibility) on Linux. The specific args.gn contents are documented in `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` so the next session can reproduce. Mac hosts may or may not hit the libstdc++ 10 issue â€” Apple toolchain overrides differ and Chromium's default sysroot for Mac is newer â€” so the Mac verification is a separate follow-up.

### Remaining Step 0 work

- Make the rebuild contract durable: either vendor the ComponentTest args.gn at a tracked path, or add a repo-only tool/script that regenerates it on demand. The current tracked default is `bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/args.gn` with only `is_debug = false`, which does not expose the C++ surface.
- Verify `libdawn_native.so` similarly links under the same args (1417 ninja steps estimated before the libc++ rebuild, longer on the full component build). This is the next single verification step.
- Decide the build-product location contract: `ComponentTest/` is fine for a verification fixture, but the shim's linker search path needs a stable directory once Step 1 (the C++ shim) lands.
- On Mac: re-verify whether the Apple toolchain default sysroot exposes `atomic::wait`; if it does, the `use_custom_libcxx = true` override may be unnecessary there.

### What this push did not change

- No Doe-side runtime code. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #2 still forbids runtime-behavior placeholders in the Zig execution path; Zig stays untouched until Step 1 (the C++ shim) lands on a durable build contract.
- No tracked Dawn build artifacts. The ComponentTest output directory is gitignored and local-only.

## Push: Dawn cache integration verification â€” vendored libwebgpu_dawn.so blocks the designed shim (2026-04-16 UTC)

Push 6 from the "do it all" execution sequence: a binary audit of the vendored Dawn build to confirm whether the Push 4 integration-design shim is buildable. It is not, in the current form, and the design doc is updated with the concrete finding and the three options that unblock it.

### What was verified

- `nm -D --defined-only bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/libwebgpu_dawn.so` returns 507 dynamic symbols; every globally-exported text symbol is in the `wgpu*` C ABI family.
- `nm --defined-only` locates `dawn::platform::Platform::GetCachingInterface()` (`_ZN4dawn8platform8Platform19GetCachingInterfaceEv`) as a lowercase `t` (local text) â€” the symbol is compiled into the binary but hidden from dynamic linking.
- No `dawn::*` or `dawn_*` C++ symbols are dynamically exported. The `DAWN_NATIVE_EXPORT` macro in `bench/vendor/dawn/include/dawn/native/dawn_native_export.h` only expands to `__attribute__((visibility("default")))` when both `DAWN_NATIVE_IMPLEMENTATION` and `DAWN_NATIVE_SHARED_LIBRARY` are set at Dawn build time; the vendored `args.gn` is minimal (`is_debug = false`) and the default monolithic-shared build produces C ABI only.
- `DawnInstanceDescriptor.platform = dawn::platform::Platform*` is the documented integration hook (`DawnNative.h:117-121`), but constructing a subclass against it requires linking base-class vtable slots and constructors that the current vendored binary does not expose.
- `dawn/dawn_proc.h` offers `dawnProcSetProcs(const DawnProcTable*)` as the only C ABI escape hatch; this redirects `wgpu*` calls but cannot install a `CachingInterface`.

### What this changes about the Push 4 plan

The original integration design assumed a C++ shim in Doe's tree could link against the vendored `libwebgpu_dawn.so`, subclass `dawn::platform::Platform` and `dawn::platform::CachingInterface`, and install the object via `DawnInstanceDescriptor.platform`. That shim will not link against the current binary.

Three options unblock the integration (all detailed in `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` under the new "Vendored Dawn build verification" and "Step 0" sections):

- Option A â€” rebuild Dawn with exported C++ visibility (`is_component_build = true` / equivalent). Recommended default: smallest change, no source patch, brings the build into line with Dawn's intended shared-library configuration.
- Option B â€” build Dawn's separate `libdawn_native` / `libdawn_platform` component form. Equivalent result, different GN config surface.
- Option C â€” patch Dawn source to add an `extern "C"` cache-installation function in-tree. Survives Dawn rebuilds but needs a stable patch-apply step in the vendor-refresh workflow.

All three require a Dawn-side rebuild. Steps 1-7 of the integration plan (C++ shim, Zig FFI surface, CLI flag, trace schema, executor templates, resolver change, docs) cannot proceed until Step 0 lands.

### What this push did not change

- No Doe-side code. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #2 still forbids runtime-behavior placeholders in the Zig execution path, so the Zig side stays untouched until the Dawn rebuild unblocks a real shim.
- No Dawn-side rebuild yet. The vendored `args.gn` is unchanged, the vendored `libwebgpu_dawn.so` is unchanged, and the design-doc-only nature of the Push 4 landing is preserved.

### What this push did change

- `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` â€” new "Vendored Dawn build verification (2026-04-16)" section with the binary-audit findings, new "Step 0" section with the three unblock options and the recommended default, and the "Risks and open questions" first bullet updated to reflect the answered question.

### Note on Mac-host Dawn build

This verification was run on Linux against the committed vendored build. If a separate Dawn build lives under `bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/` on `mac.lan` or any other Mac host, it must be re-verified there â€” different `args.gn` could produce a binary that already exports the C++ surface, or not.

## Mac fair-cold evidence recovers four of the seven cache-asymmetric Metal workloads as strict claimable (2026-04-16 UTC)

The Mac-hardware step that was blocked across every April 16 push (G18 / D13-C10 / Linux-follow-ups) has landed. A fresh `mac.lan` compare against the apple-metal compare preset with the fair-cold defaults (both sides `--no-pipeline-cache`, both sides `pipelineCache.state="disabled" reason="cli-flag"`) produced a strict comparable artifact in which the pipeline-cache auto-flag correctly suppressed `pathAsymmetry: true` on every row because neither side opened an `MTLBinaryArchive`.

### Artifact path

- `bench/out/apple-metal/compare/20260416T212500Z/dawn-vs-doe.apple.metal.compare.json` â€” strict comparable compare report, 7 workloads, `comparabilityPolicy.mode="strict"`, `comparabilityCoherence.status="pass"`, both participants carry the new nested `pipelineCache` object with `state="disabled" reason="cli-flag"`, every workload has `pathAsymmetry: false`
- `bench/out/apple-metal/compare/20260416T212500Z/dawn-vs-doe.apple.metal.compare.claim.json` â€” claim report, `comparisonStatus=comparable`, `claimStatus=claimable`, `claimPolicy.mode="local"`, `claimPolicy.minTimedSamples=15`
- 16 run-artifacts under the workspace root (Doe + Dawn-delegate for 7 workloads apiece, plus the expected `.compare-dev` and per-run metadata)

### What this substantiates

Of the 7 cache-asymmetric compute workloads auto-disclosed in the 2026-04-16 apple-metal pipeline-cache-asymmetry push, **4 are in this fresh compare and all 4 are strict claimable** with Doe faster:

| Workload ID | p50 delta |
| --- | --- |
| `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` | +9.6% |
| `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` | +10.9% |
| `compute_zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_256` | +69.1% |
| `compute_concurrent_execution_single` | +4.3% |

These replace the 2026-04-15 "23/25 wins" reading for these four rows: the delta is now measured under both-sides-cache-disabled, so the positive deltas are runtime-engineering wins rather than cache-asymmetry artifacts.

Three additional non-cache-asymmetric rows rode along in the same preset and are also strict claimable in this run: `pipeline_compile_stress` (+42.2%) plus two directional-only dispatch rows (`compute_dispatch_fallback` +60.5%, `compute_dispatch_grid` +66.9%, both `claimEligible=false`).

### End-to-end schema round-trip confirmed on Mac

Every artifact in the workspace carries the new nested `pipelineCache` object introduced by the A1 push today:

```
pipelineCache: { state: "disabled", reason: "cli-flag", warmupCount: 0, warmupNs: 0 }
```

This is the first Mac-observed artifact set that proves the Zig-side telemetry plumbing (`TraceRunSummary` -> `backend_runtime_telemetry.refresh` -> `metal_pipeline_cache.process_active_cache` -> `trace_meta` JSON) round-trips into the Python reader and into the comparability gate. Linux-observed round-trips previously showed `state="disabled" reason="platform-unsupported"` because Linux cannot host Metal; this pass confirms the `cli-flag` branch on the Mac path.

### Partial-retraction scope narrowed

The 2026-04-16 partial retraction of the 2026-04-15 "Doe faster on 23/25" reading applied to all 7 cache-asymmetric compute workloads. With this push, the retraction scope narrows to the three still-missing matvec workloads:

- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32`
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1`
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1`

Until these three have a fair-cold Mac rerun under `--no-pipeline-cache`, any "Doe faster on X" reading involving their 2026-04-15 numbers remains retracted. The other four cache-asymmetric workloads are fully unretracted by the artifact above.

### Not released-graded

`claimPolicy.mode="local"` â€” this is claim-grade-local evidence, not a release-grade result. `releaseMinTimedSamples=15` is met at the sample level, but release mode additionally requires positive `p99` (per `reliability.releaseRequiredPositivePercentiles` in `config/benchmark-methodology-thresholds.json`) and the artifact stays in local mode for now. A release-mode rerun with explicit release claim policy is a separate follow-up.

### Follow-up queue

1. Mac rerun of the 3 matvec workloads under `--no-pipeline-cache` to complete the 7-row set.
2. Release-grade rerun of the 4 now-claimable rows if a release-mode compare lane is wanted.
3. Dawn-cache shim landing (Push 4 design doc) so the fair-warm equivalent lane becomes available for the same 7 rows.

## Push: Dawn delegate cache integration design doc (fair-warm lane scoping) (2026-04-16 UTC)

Scopes the follow-on engineering that makes Apple Metal Dawn-vs-Doe compute comparisons fair-*warm* instead of only fair-*cold*. The fair-cold default lane is already in place (G18 push: both sides under `--no-pipeline-cache`, both record `pipelineCache.state="disabled"`). The fair-warm lane requires a Dawn-side persistent cache equivalent to Doe's `MTLBinaryArchive`; this push records the integration surface so the next dedicated push does not re-derive it.

### What landed

**`bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` (new).**
- Names the Dawn caching surface: `dawn::platform::CachingInterface::LoadData` / `StoreData` reached through `dawn::platform::Platform::GetCachingInterface()` in `bench/vendor/dawn/include/dawn/platform/DawnPlatform.h:48-189`. Flush hook is `dawn::native::PerformIdleTasks()` in `bench/vendor/dawn/include/dawn/native/DawnNative.h:361-363`.
- Identifies the integration gap: Dawn's cache is a C++ virtual contract, not a C ABI; the standard `webgpu.h` that Doe loads via `runtime/zig/src/wgpu_loader.zig` does not expose cache installation. A small in-tree C++ shim linked against `libdawn_native` is therefore required.
- Enumerates the seven-step landing plan: (1) `runtime/zig/src/backend/dawn/dawn_cache_shim.cpp` C++ shim; (2) `runtime/zig/src/backend/dawn/dawn_cache.zig` cross-platform FFI surface parallel to `metal_pipeline_cache.zig`; (3) `--dawn-cache-dir` CLI flag with typed unsupported error when the shim is absent; (4) `TraceRunSummary.dawnPipelineCache.{state,reason,entryCount}` schema addition; (5) `dawn_delegate_metal_cache` executor template; (6) `run_artifact.py::_resolve_metal_cache_asymmetry` extension to consult both caches; (7) docs updates.
- Platform-scoping table records which steps are Linux-executable (1-4, 6-7 as compile-green contract + unit tests) vs Mac-only (5 live execution and the full end-to-end validation against the 7 cache-asymmetric compute workloads held diagnostic pending Mac re-run).
- Calls out four risks: Dawn build shape (does `libdawn_native` export the platform hook in this repo's vendored build?), cache keyspace overlap verification (Doe's manifest is named, Dawn's keys are hashed), idle-flush ordering (must drive `PerformIdleTasks` deterministically before process exit), Mac-only validation scope.
- States explicitly that this doc is the only deliverable in this push: no runtime, bench harness, or runtime-visible doc changes. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #2 forbids runtime-behavior placeholders in the Zig execution path, so the Zig side intentionally stays untouched until the shim lands.

**`bench/docs/metal-pipeline-cache-policy.md` â€” cross-link added.**
- The existing fair-cold policy doc now points at the new integration design for the fair-warm follow-on lane.

### Why scope the integration this way

The `--dawn-cache-dir` flag is tempting to land as a no-op on non-Mac. That would be a placeholder. CLAUDE.md #2: "runtime behavior placeholders are not allowed in Zig execution paths; implement fully or fail with explicit unsupported taxonomy." So the flag is deliberately *not* in the CLI today; it lands in the push that also lands the shim, the FFI surface, the trace schema field, and the cross-platform-safe wrapper that routes through the existing `cli/ -> backend/` import fence.

### Test status

- No code changes in this push. No runtime, bench Python, or schema changes.
- Existing test baseline unchanged: 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same as after Pushes 1-3 today).

### Follow-up queue

1. Verify the vendored Dawn build exports `dawn::platform::Platform` (compile-check the shim shape against `bench/vendor/dawn/include/`). Linux-executable.
2. Land the C++ shim + Zig FFI surface + trace schema addition in a single push that stays green on Linux via the "dawn-delegate-not-in-build" / "platform-unsupported" branches. Linux-executable.
3. Land executor templates, resolver changes, and unit tests. Linux-executable.
4. On Mac: run the 7 cache-asymmetric compute workloads under the fair-warm lane with both sides' caches warm. Recovers the compute-cache wins as claim-grade evidence. Mac-only.
5. Expand to broader Metal compute coverage beyond the initial 7 workloads. Mac-only.

Closes the "Proof-backed shader metric collection currently lives in a scratch evidence bundle rather than a promoted benchmark lane" item on the status front door. The stable mirror at `bench/out/proof-metrics/latest/` has existed since 2026-04-10; what was missing was the `bench/README.md` section that named it as the front door, named the structural reporter entrypoint, distinguished the reproducible structural half from the Vulkan-hardware timing half, and documented the refresh pattern.

### What landed

**`bench/README.md` â€” "Proof-backed shader metric front door" section.**
- Identifies `bench/out/proof-metrics/latest/proof_metrics_summary.{json,md}` as the stable mirror (and notes both files are `.gitignore`-allowlisted so external writeups can link the stable path).
- Names the reporter entrypoint: `zig build runtime-compile-report` builds `doe-runtime-compile-report`, emitter source at `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/runtime_compile_report.zig`.

- Previous line framed proof-metrics as scratch-only evidence awaiting a promoted benchmark lane. The stable mirror has been live since April 10; the new line points at that mirror and calls out the remaining work (a fresh Vulkan-host timing pass).

- Does not introduce a new orchestrator script or a promoted-compare-catalog entry. The proof-metrics pattern is Doe-only (build-flavor vs build-flavor) and does not fit the baseline-vs-comparison executor schema used by the promoted catalog; a front-door README section plus the stable mirror is the right shape for this evidence class.
- Does not add the shader scope broadening. Extending beyond the three-shader pass requires both reporter-side invocation list changes and mirror-schema updates in lockstep; out of scope for this push.

## Push: contract-centralization â€” per-surface exemption table + ad-hoc scope docstring (2026-04-16 UTC)

Closes the "centralize comparability contract across ad-hoc compare scripts" item that has been open since the E14 shared ad-hoc gating module landed. The shared `bench/lib/adhoc_claim_gating.py` module already unified sample-floor / required-percentile / timer-overhead gating; what was missing was an explicit per-surface contract table that records what each surface enforces, what it exempts, and why.

### What landed

**`bench/docs/package-browser-ort-fairness-audit.md` â€” per-surface contract exemption table.**
- New section enumerates every contract layer (comparability mode, report-level coherence, execution-shape parity, phase-asymmetry gate, two-tier sample-floor, required positive percentiles, timer-overhead budget, path-asymmetry) against every surface (native GPU, package Node/Bun, browser, ad-hoc CPU-only, ad-hoc GPU).
- Each cell records Required / Exempt / N/A plus the reason for an exemption.
- Residual-limits section is tightened with three concrete watchouts: wall-time-only package comparisons must be marked diagnostic; JS dispatch bridges that do not surface dispatch/row counts block structural equivalence; new ad-hoc GPU scripts without construction-guaranteed parity must route through `bench/cli.py compare` rather than emit their own `.claim.json`.

**`bench/lib/adhoc_claim_gating.py` â€” scope docstring.**
- Docstring now names the three contract layers the module does NOT cover (execution-shape parity, timing-phase asymmetry, hardware-path asymmetry disclosure) and documents the construction-guarantee-or-migrate rule for ad-hoc GPU scripts.
- Links to the fairness-audit doc as the authoritative per-surface exemption table.

### Why this closes the contract-centralization risk

The strategic risk logged with E14 was: "the next person adding a comparison surface will copy whatever's nearby, not the canonical contract." The fix is not more code sharing -- E14 already extracted the sharable parts -- it is making the remaining per-surface exemptions legible in one place. A new surface author now has a single-page table answering "what do I still have to enforce myself?" and a module docstring answering "what does importing `adhoc_claim_gating` buy me, and what stays my responsibility?"

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline as after the smoke-floor push; zero new regressions).
- Docs-only and docstring-only change path; no runtime behavior change.

### What this does not do

- Does not migrate `compare_subgroup_kernels.py` off its ad-hoc emission path. Subgroup has structural parity by construction (hardcoded 100-dispatch per side, same WGSL). The fairness-audit table records this as an accepted construction guarantee, not a blanket exemption.
- Does not add a runtime check for wall-time-only package/browser comparisons. The table marks them `diagnostic` by policy; a programmatic assertion in `comparability_runtime.py::assess_timing_phase_equivalence` is a future item if wall-time fallback turns out to recur.

## Push: smoke-lane comparability floor (two-tier sample-floor policy) (2026-04-16 UTC)

Closes the deferred "smoke-lane sample-floor bump" follow-up from the 2026-04-16 pipeline-cache-state and Linux-follow-ups pushes. The existing comparability floor (`comparabilityDefaults.minTimedSamples=7`) only fired on `claimEligible=true` workloads, so `count:2` smoke artifacts were able to land `comparability.comparable=true` at the report level even though they are never claim-eligible.

### What landed

**Schema v3 â€” two-tier sample-floor policy.**
- `config/benchmark-methodology-thresholds.json` bumped to `schemaVersion: 3` and gains `comparabilityDefaults.smokeMinTimedSamples: 3`.
- `config/benchmark-methodology-thresholds.schema.json` bumped to `const: 3`; `comparabilityDefaults` now requires both `minTimedSamples` and `smokeMinTimedSamples`.
- Policy loader validates `smokeMinTimedSamples >= 0` and `smokeMinTimedSamples <= minTimedSamples` so the smoke tier can never silently outrank the claim-eligible tier.

**Coherence gate â€” two-tier floor application.**
- `bench/lib/comparability_coherence.py::assess_workload` now takes both `min_timed_samples` and `smoke_min_timed_samples`. Claim-eligible workloads apply the claim floor (reason tag `comparability`); non-claim-eligible workloads apply the smoke floor (reason tag `smoke-comparability`). Existing tags are preserved so downstream log grep stays compatible.
- `assess_report` plumbs both floors and emits `smokeMinTimedSamples` alongside `minTimedSamples` on the coherence payload.

**Plumbing.**
- `BenchmarkMethodologyPolicy` gains `smoke_comparability_min_timed_samples` (default `0`).
- `bench/native_compare_modules/compare_from_artifacts.py::build_compare_report` plumbs the smoke floor into the inline coherence assessment.
- `bench/gates/comparability_coherence_gate.py` reads the new field and prints it on the summary line.
- `bench/cli.py` passes the new field from the loaded policy into `build_compare_report`.

**Tests â€” `bench/tests/test_comparability_coherence_smoke_floor.py` (9 new tests).**
- Claim-eligible below floor fails with `comparability floor 7` reason; claim-eligible at floor passes; smoke `count:2` fails with `smoke-comparability floor 3`; smoke `count:3` passes; asymmetric counts only flag the failing side; report-level demotes `count:2` smoke; report-level accepts `count:3` smoke.
- Policy loader test reads the shipped config and verifies the tiered values; rejection test confirms `smoke > main` is rejected with a message naming `smokeMinTimedSamples`.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` â€” 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped. +9 passing vs the pre-push baseline (the 14 pre-existing failures/errors are the same schema-drift and numeric-fragility-corpus items noted in earlier April entries; zero new regressions introduced by this push).
- `zig build`, `zig build test` â€” exit 0.
- Threshold config validates against the new schema v3.

### What this does not do

- Smoke lanes have not been re-run against the new floor; smoke configs still carry `iterations: 2` by design, and the coherence gate will now correctly demote any `comparable:true` smoke rows at the report level.
- The comparability coherence gate was already default-on in `run_blocking_gates.py` after the D13/C10 push on 2026-04-16; no runner change is needed.

## Push: pipelineCache state field, fair-cold executor templates, gate auto-flag relaxation, structural-equivalence default-on (2026-04-16 UTC)

Five-item plan landed end-to-end on Linux (Mac re-run still blocked on hardware). Closes the gap between "we can run with --no-pipeline-cache" (CLI mechanism) and "the artifact records *whether* the cache was active and the comparability gate honors that signal" (verifiable apples-to-apples).

### What landed

**A1 â€” `trace_meta.pipelineCache.{state,reason,warmupCount,warmupNs}` nested object.**
- Zig: `TraceRunSummary` gains `pipeline_cache_active: bool` (populated by `backend_runtime_telemetry.refresh` from the active Metal backend's process-level `process_active_cache` pointer) and `pipeline_cache_disabled: bool` (set from `RunOptions.no_pipeline_cache` in `cli/runtime_cli.zig` before `writeTraceMeta`).
- `BackendTelemetry` gains `pipeline_cache_active`; `metal_pipeline_cache.zig` exports `process_active_cache_present()`; `metal/mod.zig` adds `pipeline_cache_active_from_context()`. Same routing as the existing warmup count/ns plumbing â€” no new import-fence breaks.
- `trace.writeTraceMeta` now emits a single nested `pipelineCache` object. State derivation:
  - `state="enabled"` only when Doe's Metal native runtime actually opened an MTLBinaryArchive (`pipeline_cache_active == true`)
  - `state="disabled"` otherwise
- Reason values: `"default"` (Mac, cache active), `"cli-flag"` (Mac, --no-pipeline-cache), `"non-doe-backend"` (Mac, dawn_delegate Metal â€” Doe cache not in code path), `"platform-unsupported"` (non-Mac).
- The legacy top-level `pipelineCacheWarmupCount`/`pipelineCacheWarmupNs` fields are removed from the new shape; the Python reader retains backwards-compat fallback.
- Verified on Linux: `pipelineCache.state="disabled" reason="platform-unsupported"` regardless of CLI flag (Linux can't host Metal).

**A2 â€” `doe_direct_metal_no_cache` + `dawn_delegate_metal_no_cache` executor templates.**
- Added to `bench/native_compare_modules/executor_registry.py`. Both pass `--no-pipeline-cache` to `doe-zig-runtime`. Dawn-side template carries the flag for command symmetry; the flag is a no-op there because Dawn's Metal backend doesn't open Doe's archive.
- The harness can now dispatch a fair-cold lane via these templates and the comparison artifact's both-sides `pipelineCache.state == "disabled"` is the verifiable evidence.

**A3 â€” Comparability gate auto-flag relaxation.**
- `bench/native_compare_modules/run_artifact.py::_resolve_metal_cache_asymmetry` now consults `trace_meta.pipelineCache.state`. When state is `"disabled"` (any reason: cli-flag, non-doe-backend, platform-unsupported), the cache-membership auto-flag is **skipped** â€” the workload is in the manifest but no cache was loaded on this side, so flagging `pathAsymmetry: true` would be incorrect.
- Workloads that explicitly declared `pathAsymmetry: true` (e.g. UMA upload) are preserved unconditionally â€” auto-detection only ever escalates, never demotes.
- Both `build_run_artifact` and `_normalize_legacy_artifact` get the same treatment, so legacy artifacts loaded from disk also get correct disclosure.

**A4 â€” Reader plumbing surfaces `runtimeIdentity.pipelineCache`.**
- `_pipeline_cache_telemetry()` in `run_artifact.py` reads the new nested object. Backwards-compat: falls back to legacy top-level `pipelineCacheWarmupCount`/`Ns` for older artifacts (returns `state="unknown" reason="unknown"` so a reader can distinguish "old artifact, schema slot empty" from "new artifact, known state").
- Surfaced under `runtimeIdentity.pipelineCache` in both build and legacy normalization paths.

**A5 â€” 14 unit tests in `bench/tests/test_pipeline_cache_state.py`.**
- 4 reader tests (nested, legacy fallback, absent, partial)
- 7 cache-asymmetry resolver tests (all four state/reason combinations Ã— declared/non-declared edge cases)
- 3 executor template tests (no-cache variants present + flag, default executors don't carry the flag)

**C9 â€” Structural equivalence gate default-on.**
- `bench/runners/run_blocking_gates.py:155` changed `--with-structural-equivalence-gate` from `store_true` (default false) to `BooleanOptionalAction` (default true). Opt-out is `--no-with-structural-equivalence-gate`, gated to diagnostic-only runs that legitimately fail structural parity (e.g. directional coverage lanes).
- `--with-claim-gate` + `--no-with-structural-equivalence-gate` is now a hard error per CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #10 ("execution-shape parity checks must apply to ALL domains" â€” claim eligibility cannot exist without structural validation).

### What this closes

- The previous-audit "structural-equivalence is opt-in" loophole (Priority 3 in the original audit list) is closed: every default `compare` invocation through `run_blocking_gates.py` now runs structural parity.
- The fair-cold lane substantiation scaffolding is complete on Linux: when run on Mac, both sides can be invoked with `--no-pipeline-cache`, the trace_meta will carry `pipelineCache.state="disabled" reason="cli-flag"` on both sides, the run artifacts won't auto-flag pathAsymmetry, and the resulting compare-report will be apples-to-apples.

### Test status

- `zig build`, `zig build test`, `zig build import-fence` â€” all exit 0.
- 727 Python tests (+14 from this push), 7 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped â€” same baseline 13 issues, zero regressions.

### Deferred

- D13 sample-count floor: the existing `claimability.assess_claimability` floor (`localMinTimedSamples=7`, `releaseMinTimedSamples=15` from `config/benchmark-methodology-thresholds.json`) already prevents low-sample artifacts from reaching claim status. Adding a comparability-side floor (so `count: 2` smoke artifacts can't be marked `comparable: true` either) requires a new config field and obligation entry; deferred to next push.
- C10 cross-layer coherence gate: a single final assertion that `comparable: true` implies obligation-parity, runtime phase-asymmetry, and structural-equivalence all passed for the same workload+sample set. With C9 default-on this is partially covered (structural is now always evaluated when comparable is computed), but a dedicated coherence assertion across all three layers is still missing. Next push.
- D11/D12 package and browser lane fairness audits â€” never traced to native-lane depth.
- E14 `compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py` adoption of `adhoc_claim_gating.py` â€” explicitly deferred (committed claim-report format).
- F17 erratum/sidecar for the historical 7 cache-asymmetric "23/25 wins" artifacts â€” auto-detection covers new artifacts; historicals carry old shape.
- G18 strategic decision on whether `bench/kernels/doe_pipeline_archive.metallib` should be tracked in git long-term â€” open.

## Follow-up push: Zig cache telemetry in trace_meta, --no-pipeline-cache flag, tightened 10% phase-asymmetry threshold, shared ad-hoc claim-gating module (2026-04-16 UTC)

Four items from the prior follow-up queue landed in one push. Item #3 (re-run 7 cache-asymmetric workloads) remains blocked on Mac hardware.

### #1 â€” Zig trace_meta emission for Apple Metal pipeline cache warmup telemetry

The reader side was plumbed in the previous turn (`run_artifact.py::_pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry`) but trace_meta didn't carry the fields. Now wired end-to-end through the existing telemetry surface, respecting the `cli/ -> backend/metal/` import fence:

- `runtime/zig/src/trace.zig` â€” added `pipeline_cache_warmup_count` and `pipeline_cache_warmup_ns` to `TraceRunSummary`; emitted as top-level fields `pipelineCacheWarmupCount`/`pipelineCacheWarmupNs` in the trace_meta JSON (always emitted, zero on non-Mac builds, so the schema slot is stable cross-platform)
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_telemetry.zig` â€” added the same two fields to `BackendTelemetry` (default zero)
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_runtime_telemetry.zig::refresh` â€” populates the new telemetry fields from the active Metal backend via `metal_backend.pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry_from_context`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/mod.zig` â€” new `pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry_from_context` helper delegates to `metal_pipeline_cache.process_active_cache_warmup_telemetry`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/metal_pipeline_cache.zig` â€” new file-scope `process_active_cache` pointer set at `MetalPipelineCache.init` and cleared at `deinit`; `process_active_cache_warmup_telemetry()` returns `(count, ns)` from its telemetry struct, or zeros when no cache is active
- `runtime/zig/src/cli/runtime_cli.zig` â€” before `trace.writeTraceMeta`, calls `execution_context.telemetry()` (which invokes `refresh`) and fills the two fields from the resulting `BackendTelemetry` snapshot. Uses the existing `execution_context` handle, so no new imports crossing the fence

Verified on Linux (non-Mac path): `/tmp/cache_test.meta.json::pipelineCacheWarmupCount=0, pipelineCacheWarmupNs=0` â€” field present, zero as expected. On Mac with the cache active, `run_artifact.py`'s existing `_pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry` reader will surface these into `runtimeIdentity.pipelineCacheWarmup = {count, ns}`.

### #2 â€” `--no-pipeline-cache` flag on `doe-zig-runtime`

CLI knob that disables the Metal pipeline archive init, for fair-cold Doe-vs-Dawn comparisons of cached kernels. Default unchanged (cache enabled); existing users unaffected.

- `runtime/zig/src/cli/runtime_cli_args.zig` â€” new `RunOptions.no_pipeline_cache: bool = false`, parser arm for `--no-pipeline-cache`. Boolean flag, no value
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/metal_pipeline_cache.zig` â€” new file-scope `process_pipeline_cache_disabled` flag + `set_process_pipeline_cache_disabled(bool)` / `is_process_pipeline_cache_disabled()`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/metal_native_runtime.zig:381` â€” cache-init guard now reads `if (HAS_PIPELINE_CACHE and !metal_pipeline_cache.is_process_pipeline_cache_disabled())`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/mod.zig` â€” `set_pipeline_cache_disabled(bool)` helper
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_runtime_telemetry.zig` â€” cross-platform-safe wrapper `set_metal_pipeline_cache_disabled` that's a no-op on non-Mac; keeps the `cli/` â†’ `backend/metal/` import fence clean
- `runtime/zig/src/cli/runtime_cli.zig` â€” calls the wrapper *before* `ExecutionContext.init`, so the cache init sees the flag set

Verified on Linux: `./doe-zig-runtime ... --no-pipeline-cache` accepts the flag, runs to completion, trace_meta fields zero. On Mac with the flag set, the cache init loop at `metal_native_runtime.zig:381-402` is skipped entirely.

This gives the fair-cold lane: `doe-zig-runtime --backend-lane metal_doe_comparable --no-pipeline-cache` vs `doe-zig-runtime --backend-lane metal_dawn_release` is genuinely apples-to-apples because neither side opens an MTLBinaryArchive.

### #4 â€” 10% phase-asymmetry threshold replaced with all-zero-vs-any-material formulation

CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #11: "if one side reports zero in a timing phase while the other reports material cost ... the timing scopes are measuring different things." The existing median-fraction threshold (`_PHASE_ASYMMETRY_THRESHOLD = 0.10`) only fires when the non-zero side's median crosses 10% of total â€” permitting a steady-state-zero side paired with intermittent spikes whose median is 8% to pass.

New formulation in `bench/native_compare_modules/comparability.py`:

- `_PHASE_ZERO_EPSILON: float = 1e-9` â€” samples below this are treated as zero (float-noise tolerance)
- `_PHASE_MATERIAL_FLOOR_FRACTION: float = 0.005` â€” a sample is "material" if phase fraction â‰¥ 0.5% of `executionTotalNs` (20Ã— stricter than the old 10% median)
- `_PHASE_MATERIAL_MIN_SAMPLES: int = 2` â€” the non-zero side must have at least 2 material samples, so a single spike doesn't false-fire
- `_all_samples_zero(values)` / `_material_sample_count(values)` helpers

Gate logic in `comparability_runtime.py::assess_timing_phase_equivalence`, `assess_submit_scope_equivalence`, and `claimability.py::assess_phase_equivalence`:

> if one side is all-zero AND the other side has â‰¥ `_PHASE_MATERIAL_MIN_SAMPLES` samples â‰¥ `_PHASE_MATERIAL_FLOOR_FRACTION`, the phases are measuring different things and the comparison is not claimable.

The legacy `_PHASE_ASYMMETRY_THRESHOLD = 0.10` is retained in the details payload for backwards-compatible diagnostic reporting but no longer controls the gate. The new `phaseGateFormulation: "all-zero-one-side-vs-any-material-other-side"` field on the details payload documents the active rule.

Intentional behavior: near-zero legitimate signals (warm-cached compute setup_ns that medians to ~0.1% of total) no longer false-fire; a steady-state-spike profile with 2+ samples above 0.5% still correctly fires even when the median is below 10%.

### #5 foundation â€” shared ad-hoc claim-gating module

`compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py` and `compare_subgroup_kernels.py` each reimplemented the same local=7-samples+p50/p95 vs release=15-samples+p50/p95/p99 gate logic with slight drift. Extracted to `bench/lib/adhoc_claim_gating.py`:

- `ClaimPolicy.for_mode("local"|"release")` â€” canonical policy object with `min_timed_samples`, `required_positive_percentiles`, `timer_overhead_budget_percent`, `policy_source`
- `DeltaPercentiles(p50, p95, p99)` â€” typed delta record with policy-aware `.get(pct)`
- `gate_workload_claim(...)` â€” single-row gate returning the existing artifact-compatible record; checks sample-count floors (including optional warm-sample count), positive-percentile requirements, optional timer-overhead-budget
- `aggregate_claim_status(workloads)` â€” collapses per-row records into `(status, pass, reasons)`

**First adopter: `compare_subgroup_kernels.py`.** Per-row gate reduced from ~30 lines to a single `gate_workload_claim(...)` call. Aggregate status via `aggregate_claim_status`. Claim-policy JSON built via `ClaimPolicy.to_dict()` with one local override for the subgroup-vs-tree delta-convention string. Smoke-tested: `compare_subgroup_kernels.py --iterations 20 --claim-mode local` still emits a valid claim report with `pass: true`.

**Second adopter deferred:** `compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py` has Tint-specific `binaryProvenance`/`timingScopeSymmetry`/`warm` fields and risks breaking the committed claim-report format for the 8-of-13 Unity shader release claim evidence. Logged as next adopter.

**Test coverage:** `bench/tests/test_adhoc_claim_gating.py` â€” 13 unit tests covering `ClaimPolicy` for both modes, `gate_workload_claim` positive/negative cases, timer-overhead budget, warm-sample gate, `aggregate_claim_status`. All pass.

### Files changed

- `runtime/zig/src/trace.zig` â€” `TraceRunSummary` fields + JSON emission
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_telemetry.zig` â€” `BackendTelemetry` fields
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_runtime_telemetry.zig` â€” `refresh` populates Metal cache fields; new `set_metal_pipeline_cache_disabled` wrapper
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/mod.zig` â€” `pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry_from_context`, `set_pipeline_cache_disabled`

- `runtime/zig/src/cli/runtime_cli.zig` â€” pre-init `set_metal_pipeline_cache_disabled`; end-of-run pull of cache telemetry into `trace_summary`

## Prior audit fixes landed: dispatch-count parity fail-closed; release-path strict-mode guard; breadth-config `allowBaselineNoExecution` rationale pinned (2026-04-16 UTC)

Three of the four items queued from the earlier fairness audit (see `Next-session follow-up queue` in the 2026-04-16 pipeline-cache entry below) are now in code. The remaining two items (Zig-side trace_meta emission for pipeline-cache warmup telemetry; `--no-pipeline-cache` flag on `doe-zig-runtime`) require Mac hardware and stay queued.

### What landed

**1. Dispatch-count parity fail-closed on unknown counts.**
`bench/native_compare_modules/compare_assessment.py::compare_execution_shapes` previously short-circuited to `(True, "")` when either side's `executionDispatchCount` set contained no `>= 0` value â€” i.e. an unknown-dispatch comparison passed silently. The check now fails with `dispatch counts unknown for row/success=â€¦` when either side has no known counts, independent of the other side's state. The prior "differ" branch is preserved. Verified against `bench/out/apple-metal/compare/20260409T210659Z/` artifacts that none of the recent compare runs legitimately report unknown dispatches, so the tightening is net-no-op for existing valid artifacts but closes the silent loophole going forward.

**2. Release-path strict-mode guard.**
`bench/lib/compare_claim_artifacts.py` now exports `RELEASE_REQUIRED_COMPARABILITY_MODES = ("strict",)`, `comparability_mode()`, and `ensure_release_strict_comparability()`. The enforcer is invoked from:

- `bench/runners/run_blocking_gates.py::main` immediately after `report_path.exists()` â€” this covers `run_release_pipeline.py`, `run_market_readiness_bundle.py`, and `run_release_claim_windows.py` transitively (those paths invoke `run_blocking_gates.py`).
- `bench/runners/publish_apple_runtime_release.py::ensure_compare_step_acceptable` on both the `step["pass"] == True` and `returnCode == 3` branches â€” `publish_apple_runtime_release.py` runs its own gates and does not transit `run_blocking_gates.py`, so defense-in-depth enforcement lives here directly.

Local diagnostic use of `--comparability-mode warn` or `off` at `bench/cli.py:58` is preserved; the trust boundary is the release entry points, not the dev CLI. Net effect: any compare-report JSON with `comparabilityPolicy.mode != "strict"` is rejected at the first release gate with a message naming the file, the observed mode, the required mode list, and the two ways to resolve it (re-run strict, or route through a non-release path). Per the (b) decision recorded in the prior audit: local exploration stays frictionless; release paths reject on read, every time.

No schema addition was required â€” `comparabilityPolicy.mode` is already serialized into compare artifacts today (verified against `bench/out/amd-vulkan/smoke/20260412T171500Z/compute_workgroup_atomic_1024.compare.json`, which carries `"comparabilityPolicy": {"mode": "strict", "requireTimingClass": "operation"}`).

**3. `allowBaselineNoExecution: true` justified at `compare.config.apple.metal.breadth.json`.**
The breadth config is the single compare config in `bench/native-compare/` that sets `allowBaselineNoExecution: true`; every other compare config in the directory sets it false. Reading the config: baseline runs `metal_doe_directional`, comparison runs `metal_dawn_release`, selector includes both `comparable` and `directional` benchmark classes, `claimability.mode: "off"`, `claimEligibleOnly: false`, mode is `warn`. This is a legitimate coverage-characterization lane, not a vestigial config â€” it intentionally exercises Doe-only coverage where Dawn may report `executionUnsupportedCount>0` / `executionSkippedCount>0`, which is exactly what `allowBaselineNoExecution` is designed for.

Justify-not-delete: added an inline `comparability.rationale` field to the config itself naming the lane's purpose, the two backend-lanes, the relaxation it grants, the guards that prevent promotion (`claimability.mode: "off"` + `claimEligibleOnly: false`), and the release-path rejection surface (`ensure_release_strict_comparability`). Rationale lives with the config so future readers don't need to trace back to status shards to understand why the flag is set.

### Why this matters

The three fixes address the combination called out in the prior audit: "a `--comparability-mode warn` run with an unknown-dispatch baseline, no claim gate, hits zero of the strict guards and emits a compare-report.json byte-identical in shape to a strict-mode comparable artifact." After this push:

- unknown-dispatch baselines fail the execution-shape parity check (fix #1),
- release paths reject `mode != strict` at read time (fix #2),
- and the single config that legitimately uses `allowBaselineNoExecution: true` carries its own rationale so it's auditable in isolation (fix #3).

### Next-session follow-up queue (unchanged from prior entry)

1. Zig-side trace_meta emission for `pipelineCacheWarmupCount` / `pipelineCacheWarmupNs` (Mac-only)
2. `--no-pipeline-cache` flag on `doe-zig-runtime` (Mac-only)
3. Re-run the 7 Apple Metal cache-asymmetric workloads with `pathAsymmetry: true` disclosure (Mac-only)
4. Phase-asymmetry threshold tightening (CLAUDE.md #11 says "zero vs material", code still says 10% median) â€” needs a deliberate "material" spec to avoid flagging legitimate near-zero warm-cache signals; not a one-liner.
5. Centralize comparability contract across ad-hoc compare scripts (e.g. `compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py` has a parallel implementation that doesn't share `compare_assessment.py`). Strategic risk: the next person adding a comparison surface will copy whatever's nearby, not the canonical contract.

## Apple Metal pipeline-cache asymmetry auto-disclosed; 7 cache-asymmetric workloads now flagged; partial retraction of the 2026-04-15 Metal native compare-dev "23/25 wins" claim (2026-04-16 UTC)

A code-grounded fairness audit surfaced a real, undisclosed Apple Metal asymmetry: the Doe Metal native runtime opens an `MTLBinaryArchive` at `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/metal_native_runtime.zig:380-402` and pre-warms PSOs for kernels enumerated in `bench/kernels/doe_pipeline_archive.manifest`. The Dawn delegate path (`--backend-lane metal_dawn_release`, also running through `doe-zig-runtime`) routes execution through Dawn's Metal backend which doesn't open Doe's archive, so Doe gets a setup-time advantage that lands outside the timed `setup_ns` window via the warmup loop, plus in-window savings on each dispatch via cached PSO lookup.

Per CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #7 ("hardware-path asymmetry must carry explicit transferability caveats and cannot be presented as a general speed claim"), this should always have been disclosed via `pathAsymmetry: true` on affected workloads. It wasn't.

### Wrinkle that strengthened the finding

The cache is **benchmark-specific, not a generic product feature.** The manifest enumerates exactly the named bench kernels (`workgroup_atomic`, `workgroup_non_atomic`, `dispatch_noop`, `shader_robustness_matmul_512_f32`, `concurrent_execution_runsingle_u32`, `zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_2048`, `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_naive_swizzle0`, `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1`, `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1`) â€” not arbitrary user shaders. So this isn't "a real Doe runtime feature any user benefits from" â€” it's an asymmetry tuned for the benchmarks themselves.

### Auto-detection landed

Added `bench/lib/metal_pipeline_cache_manifest.py` that:

- parses `bench/kernels/doe_pipeline_archive.manifest` (line-oriented `R:N` for render entries plus `C:<basename>` for compute kernels) and returns a set of cached compute-kernel base names
- walks a workload's `commandsPath` JSON, extracts kernel base names from every `kernel_dispatch` entry (handles both `"kernel"` and `"kernel_name"` aliases per `command_parse_dispatch.zig`), strips `.wgsl`
- returns true iff the workload is Apple-Metal-routed AND dispatches at least one kernel in the manifest set
- exposes a canonical disclosure note that names the archive path, the runtime file/lines responsible, and explicitly distinguishes the warmup vs in-window cost components

`bench/native_compare_modules/run_artifact.py` now calls this helper inside both `build_run_artifact` (current path) and `_normalize_legacy_artifact` (legacy artifact loader path). Auto-detection only escalates to `pathAsymmetry: true`; it never demotes a workload-declared asymmetry (e.g. UMA-upload `pathAsymmetry: true` from existing workload manifests stays as-is). When auto-detection fires and the declared note is empty, the canonical disclosure note is applied.

Net effect on this Linux host's existing Apple Metal workload corpus (7 of 18 compute workloads in `workloads.apple.metal.json`):

| Workload ID | Cached kernel dispatched |
| --- | --- |
| `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` | `workgroup_atomic` |
| `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` | `workgroup_non_atomic` |
| `compute_concurrent_execution_single` | `concurrent_execution_runsingle_u32` |
| `compute_zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_256` | `zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_2048` |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` | `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_naive_swizzle0` |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` | `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` | `matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` |

These 7 workloads will now produce run-receipts with `pathAsymmetry: true` and the canonical note, regardless of what their workload manifest entry declared. Strict-mode comparability (`comparability.py:149`) treats `pathAsymmetry: true` as a directional marker and refuses claimable promotion under apples-to-apples discipline.

The 11 remaining compute workloads (notably `inference_gemma3_270m_*`, `inference_gemma3_1b_*`, `compute_dispatch_*`, `compute_monte_carlo_*`) do not dispatch cached kernels and are unaffected.

### Cache warmup telemetry plumbing (reader side only this push)

`metal_pipeline_cache.zig:609-621` already exports `doeNativeMetalPipelineCacheWarmupTelemetry` (`out_warmup_count`, `out_warmup_ns`) but no Zig caller currently emits these into the trace_meta JSON that the Python harness reads. Added the **reader** side anyway: `_pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry()` in `run_artifact.py` reads `pipelineCacheWarmupCount` / `pipelineCacheWarmupNs` from `trace_meta` and surfaces them as `runtimeIdentity.pipelineCacheWarmup = {count, ns}` when present. The Zig side wiring (call the export at end-of-run, write into trace_meta) is logged as next-session work; the schema is now reserved.

### Retraction of the 2026-04-15 "Metal native compare-dev: 25/25 pass, Doe faster on 23/25" status entry

The earlier 2026-04-15 entry "SPIR-V graphics path and robustness verified complete; Metal native smoke green on all 3 workload types" (in this same shard) reported "Metal native compare-dev (25 workloads): 25/25 pass on both Doe and Dawn. Doe faster on 23/25." That entry's per-workload "Doe wins include" list contains at least the following cache-asymmetric workloads:

- `compute_zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_256` (cited as Doe `+70%`)

Other entries in the cited "Doe wins" list (e.g. `pipeline_compile_stress`, `texture_sampler_write_query_destroy`, `upload_write_buffer_*`, `render_draw_*`) are not in the cache manifest and are unaffected. But the headline "Doe faster on 23/25" cannot be claimed as a clean apples-to-apples result without re-running the affected rows with the disclosure landed.

The entry remains in the shard for historical fidelity (per the append-only convention), but is **partially retracted here**: any per-workload number in that entry whose workload ID appears in the table above is contaminated by the cache asymmetry and should not be cited as a runtime-engineering win. The 2 render regressions (`render_bundle_dynamic_pipeline_bindings_200k`, `render_draw_throughput_200k`) and the upload/texture wins remain valid. The compute wins on cached kernels need re-running with `pathAsymmetry: true` recorded.

The entry was already classified as `diagnostic, not claimable` ("All results are diagnostic (2 samples, 0 warmup per config); not claimable per apples-to-apples discipline"), so no claimable artifact was promoted on the back of those numbers. The retraction here is about the directional reading, not a withdrawn claim.

- `bench/tests/test_metal_pipeline_cache_manifest.py` (new) â€” 15 unit tests covering manifest parser, kernel-name extraction, Apple Metal lane gating, and the canonical disclosure note shape

## P2/P1/P3 sequential push: spirv-val gate auto-discovers all WGSL; second Doe-Vulkan bug fixed (matmul subgroup release-claimable); ORT EP grows from 7 to 10 ops with end-to-end session smoke (2026-04-16 UTC)

Three sequential priorities executed in one push:

### P2: spirv-val gate now auto-discovers all WGSL kernels and validates fresh emission (would catch the prior subgroup-op bug retroactively)

Existing `bench/gates/spirv_val_gate.py` validated only pre-built `.spv` artifacts under `bench/kernels/` and `bench/out/`. That coverage missed the subgroup-op SPIR-V bug fixed earlier today because no subgroup-using kernel had a pre-built `.spv` in those directories.

Enhanced the gate with `--discover-wgsl` mode that:
- walks `bench/kernels/` and `bench/inference-pipeline/kernels/` for all `.wgsl` files (83 found)
- compiles each via `runtime/zig/zig-out/bin/doe-emit-spirv` to a temporary `.spv`
- runs `spirv-val` on the result
- reports per-file pass/fail tagged with `PASS-SG` / `FAIL-SG` when the kernel uses subgroup ops, so subgroup coverage is auditable in the gate output
- new `--require-subgroup-coverage` flag fails when zero subgroup-using kernels are discovered (defends against the kernels being moved out of discovery dirs)

End-to-end gate run (`python3 bench/gates/spirv_val_gate.py --discover-wgsl --require-subgroup-coverage`):
- pre-built validation: `34/34` pass (after regenerating 9 stale `.spv` artifacts in `bench/kernels/` that were emitted by an older buggy version of the SPIR-V emitter â€” same `ID 'X' decorated with Block multiple times` error class that's now fixed in the current emitter; fresh emit produced valid SPIR-V)
- discovered validation: `83/83` pass
- subgroup-using kernels validated: `4` (`rmsnorm_subgroup.wgsl`, `matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` Ã— 2 directories each)

The 9 regenerated `.spv` artifacts (`bench/kernels/{attention-decode,attention-prefill,gather,gelu,matmul-gemv,matmul-tiled,residual,rmsnorm,rope}.spv` and `monte_carlo_paths_fixed_samples.spv`) are now byte-different on disk; their content is functionally equivalent to the prior versions because both versions describe the same WGSL source, but the new ones pass `spirv-val` and the old ones did not.

### P1: Doe Vulkan backend missing-entry-point segfault root-caused and fixed; matmul_gemv subgroup variant now RELEASE-CLAIMABLE on AMD Vulkan

Yesterday's matmul_gemv RADV crash was traced. Root cause was in `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline.zig::build_pipeline_for_words` line 326: `const entry_name = entry_point orelse "main";`. The `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl` kernel exports two entry points (`main_vec4` and `main_multicol`) but neither is named `"main"`. When the runtime defaulted to `"main"` and called `vkCreateComputePipelines` against a SPIR-V module that has no entry point of that name, RADV's pipeline compiler segfaulted inside `libvulkan_radeon.so` instead of returning a clean `VK_ERROR_INVALID_SHADER_NV`.

Two-layer fix:

- **Defensive guard in Doe** (`vk_pipeline.zig`): added `spirv_has_entry_point(words, name)` helper that scans the SPIR-V `OpEntryPoint` instructions and walks the packed-word literal Name string, comparing against the requested entry name. If `build_pipeline_for_words` is called with an entry name that doesn't exist in the SPIR-V, return `error.InvalidArgument` instead of letting the driver crash. Doe should never feed a driver a known-mismatched entry point.
- **Caller-side fix** (`examples/matmul_gemv_{tree,subgroup}_commands.json`): added `"entry_point": "main_vec4"` to both command JSONs so they explicitly name a valid entry point. The command JSON parser at `runtime/zig/src/command/command_parse_dispatch.zig::parseDispatchCommand` already supports this field.

After the fix, both kernels execute cleanly. With `iterations=50`, AMD Vulkan timestamp queries:

| Kernel | tree p50/p95/p99 ns | subgroup p50/p95/p99 ns | delta% (subgroup faster) | release-claimable |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `rmsnorm` | 6562 / 6596 / 6626 | 6339 / 6540 / 6578 | p50 +3.51%, p95 +0.86%, p99 +0.73% | âœ… |
| `matmul_gemv` | 2796 / 3353 / 3608 | 2652 / 3059 / 3270 | **p50 +5.44%, p95 +9.64%, p99 +10.33%** | âœ… |

`matmul_gemv` shows the larger win as predicted: workgroup_size=64 = 1 subgroup on AMD RDNA wave64, so the cross-subgroup merge has zero loop iterations and the entire reduction collapses to a single `subgroupAdd`.

Aggregate `pass: true, claimStatus: claimable` in `bench/out/subgroup-kernels/subgroup-vs-tree.claim.json` sha256=`bc83b20a96d177f5fcf90c7165eef0fb47d4510fb0f4f915e1a3c8177aa22dfc` (release mode, 50 iter). This is the first non-trivial kernel-perf release claim on AMD Vulkan from the inference-pipeline kernels surface.

### P3: ORT EP op coverage grows from 7 to 10 ops; end-to-end session smoke green for all 12 cases

`runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.cc` now claims, compiles, and computes `Sigmoid`, `Tanh`, and `Gelu` in addition to the existing 4 single-node ops (Identity, Add, Relu, MatMul, Gemm) and 4 fused patterns (MatMulâ†’Add, MatMulâ†’Addâ†’Relu, Addâ†’Relu, Gemmâ†’Reluâ†’Gemm). Per-op edits at the 12 mechanical sites the audit identified (op-type constant, enum entry, claim/compile/compute counter atomics, `CompiledOpKindName`, `ClaimedNodeCountForKind`, `ExpectedInputCountForKind`, `IsSupportedNode` else-if, validation case, `Execute*` function, `Compute` dispatch case, `Reset` entry, `SnapshotDebugCounters` field) plus header struct extensions for the new counters.

Implementation: element-wise via `<cmath>` â€” `1.0f / (1.0f + std::exp(-x))` for Sigmoid, `std::tanh(x)` for Tanh, `0.5 * x * (1 + std::erf(x * 0.70710678118654752440f))` for Gelu (exact erf-based formula matching the ONNX reference; the `approximate=tanh` attribute variant is not supported in this slice).

Session smoke runner (`doe_ort_ep_session_smoke.cc`) extended with three new test cases plus three structural fixes I had to make to surface the new counters correctly:

- `ComputeCounterDelta` was using designated initializers â€” fields not explicitly listed default to zero, so the new counters' deltas were silently always 0 even when increments happened. Added explicit field copies for all 9 new counters.
- `RenderCountersJson` did not print the new fields. Added 9 emit lines.
- A generic `CreateUnaryModelAtOpset` helper was added so Gelu (which requires ONNX opset â‰¥ 20) can use opset 20 while the other unary ops keep using opset 13.
- `FloatVectorsEqual` was doing exact float equality which fails on transcendental ops by a few ULPs even when the math is correct (Sigmoid/Tanh/Gelu literal expected values vs `std::exp`/`std::erf`/`std::tanh` runtime output). Switched to absolute-tolerance comparison (`1e-5`); existing exact-arithmetic ops (Identity/Add/Relu/MatMul/Gemm) still match exactly under this tolerance.
- New cases placed after existing 7-op coverage so any future opset-version regression in a new op doesn't halt the existing-op test surface (the runner breaks on first failure).

Final session smoke output (`zig build ort-plugin-ep-session-smoke-run -- --plugin-path ... --ort-lib-path ...` against `libonnxruntime.so.1` from `node_modules/onnxruntime-node/`, plugin sha256=`b9bf54e88bf4217867a30dcfab2353c854627d232db246bd0b61ece36b6fe4fe`): **12/12 cases pass, all 12 routed through Doe**. The 3 new ops (Sigmoid, Tanh, Gelu) all show `success: true, routedThroughDoe: true` with correct numerical output via real ORT C-API session execution.

Updated EP compatibility info: `kCompatibilityInfo` bumped from `"doe-ort-basic-ops-ep-v5"` to `"v6"` to reflect the new op coverage; consumers comparing compatibility info strings will correctly invalidate cached compiled models on upgrade.

### Files changed (this push)

- `bench/gates/spirv_val_gate.py` â€” `--discover-wgsl` and `--require-subgroup-coverage` modes
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline.zig` â€” `spirv_has_entry_point` helper + missing-entry-point guard in `build_pipeline_for_words`
- `examples/matmul_gemv_{tree,subgroup}_commands.json` â€” explicit `"entry_point"` fields
- `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.h` â€” 9 new counter fields
- `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.cc` â€” 3 new ops (Sigmoid, Tanh, Gelu), 12 mechanical sites each, ~80 LOC total
- `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep_session_smoke.cc` â€” 3 new smoke cases, generic unary-model helper, opset-20 path for Gelu, delta+JSON wiring for new counters, tolerance-based output comparison
- `bench/kernels/{attention-decode,attention-prefill,gather,gelu,matmul-gemv,matmul-tiled,monte_carlo_paths_fixed_samples,residual,rmsnorm,rope}.spv` â€” regenerated stale artifacts that failed the now-tightened gate

### What changed in the strategic posture

- **First defensible kernel-perf release claim from inference-pipeline kernels.** matmul_gemv subgroup now beats tree reduction by p50 +5.44%, p95 +9.64%, p99 +10.33% on AMD Vulkan with all percentiles positive. Wiring this into `bench/ir/gemma3_270m_literal.json` (swap `matmul_gemv_subgroup.wgsl` â†’ `matmul_gemv_truesubgroup.wgsl` per the prior entry's plan) would propagate the win into the live Gemma-3 270M pipeline.
- **ORT EP op coverage path proven for non-trivial scope.** The pattern for adding ops is now exercised across element-wise activations (Sigmoid/Tanh/Gelu) including the opset-version handling needed for newer ops (Gelu opset 20). The next-session 9 ops (LayerNorm, Softmax, Cast, Reshape, Transpose, Concat, Slice, Gather, ReduceMean) follow the same pattern; reduction ops (LayerNorm, Softmax, ReduceMean) will benefit immediately from the subgroup-op fix landed this session.
